1001 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Peterson v. Schwartz


CX-95-2486


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 436



April 3, 1996, Decided  
April 9, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Brown County; Hon. Warren Litynski, Judge. District Court File No. C7-95-226.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court, Brown County (Minnesota), which determined that a party who removed a case from conciliation court to district court and prevailed was not entitled to recover costs under Minn. Stat. § 491A.02(7)(b) (1994). The district court concluded that § 491A.02(7)(b) was unconstitutional and awarded costs and disbursements in plaintiff's favor.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sued defendant in conciliation court. The conciliation court awarded plaintiff $ 3,680 plus fees of $ 34. Defendant removed the case to district court. The district court reduced the conciliation court's award by more then $ 500. Defendant was entitled to recover costs under § 491A.02(7)(b). However, the district court concluded that § 491A.02(7)(b) was unconstitutional and against public policy. Instead of awarding costs in defendant's favor, the district court awarded costs to plaintiff. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the district court erred when it concluded that Minn. Stat. § 491A.02(7)(b) (1994) was unconstitutional and against public policy. The court noted that the district court did not identify any constitutional limitation violated by the legislative decision to assess responsibility for costs. The court further noted that the legislature was at liberty to ignore logic and perpetrate injustice so long as it does not transgress constitutional limits. The court concluded that a party who removed a case from conciliation court to district court and prevailed was entitled to recover costs under § 491A.02(7)(b).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment.

 

1002 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


City of Greenwood v. Plowman


C1-95-1498


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 371



April 2, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Peter J. Lindberg, Judge. District Court File No. 932316.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which upheld a decision by defendant city denying the property owners' application for a variance from the city's wetlands regulation in its zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The property owners installed three docks in violation of the city's wetlands ordinance. After the city filed an action to remove the docks, the property owners filed an application for an after-the-fact-variance from the ordinance. The board of adjustments found that the docks were not in the public interest and recommended that the variance be denied. The city subsequently denied the variance. The property owners claimed on appeal that their riparian rights were superior to the city's zoning authority, that the ordinance was preempted by the State's authority over water resource conservation, that the ordinance conflicted with State law governing wetlands, and that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague. The court rejected the property owners' claim. The court ruled that the ordinance was rationally related to the protection and preservation of wetlands, that there was no evidence that the city lacked authority to regulate the docks, that the city had express power to regulate the use of docks on navigable waters under Minn. Stat. § 412.221(12) (1988), and that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding the city's denial of the property owners' application for a variance from the city's wetlands regulation in its zoning ordinance.

 

1003 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Holmberg


C5-95-1164, CX-95-1578


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


545 N.W.2d 65; 1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 336



March 26, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Andrew W. Danielson, Judge. District Court File Nos. 94-071816/94-111572.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), defendants sought review of their convictions for violating Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 540.410(g), which regulated adult bookstores and adult entertainment centers.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were operators of adult bookstores. On appeal, they argued that the restrictions on adult bookstore windows set out in § 540.410(g) were overbroad and improperly regulated the time, place, and manner of speech. The court held that § 540.410(g) was a valid regulation on the time, place, and manner of speech. The ordinance was not void on its face as an overbroad restriction on free speech because it did not regulate the content of expression. Rather, it merely regulated the presentation of adult bookstore windows. The ordinance also served substantial government interests and provided ample alternative avenues of expression. The court further held that the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions and that Minneapolis was not estopped from prosecuting defendants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions.

 

1004 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Edstrom


C2-95-2448


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 337



March 26, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Anoka County; Hon. Donald J. Venne, Judge. District Court File No. PX-94-8354.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ward appealed from the initial and final orders of the District Court, Anoka County (Minnesota), by which he was committed as a sexual psychopathic personality and a sexually dangerous person. Respondent State petitioned to commit him. Clear and convincing evidence was found at trial and the review hearing that he was both a sexual psychopathic person and a sexually dangerous person under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18a-b (1994).


OVERVIEW: The ward was a 48-year-old white male with a family history indicative of pervasive sexual dysfunction. He also had a history of criminal sexual assaults. Violence and threats were involved in all of the incidents. He committed rape for which he was imprisoned for 15 years. He began a sex offender treatment program, but was uncooperative and was returned to prison. In anticipation of his release from prison, the State petitioned for his commitment under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02 (1994). Clear and convincing evidence was found below that he was a sexually dangerous person. The court affirmed the order below for his commitment. After 15 years of incarceration and treatment, he kidnapped a woman. His conduct in committing that offense was strikingly similar to his prior sexual assaults. That his conduct was dangerous to other persons was particularly clear from the victims' testimony. Clear and convincing evidence established the statutory conditions for a sexual psychopathic personality and all experts agreed that he was highly likely to victimize again. Also, clear and convincing evidence showed that his commitment was the least restrictive alternative.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the final order of commitment.

 

1005 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Murphy v. Wood


C8-95-2101


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


545 N.W.2d 52; 1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 317



March 19, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Washington County; Hon. David E. Doyscher, Judge. District Court File # C9945087.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the District Court, Washington County (Minnesota), which granted the State's motion for summary judgment in defendant's declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 263.166, subd. 1, requiring registration for predatory offenders.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with committing criminal sexual conduct, burglary, robbery, assault and kidnapping. He pleaded guilty to the robbery and assault charges and was sentenced to a 78-month executed commitment. While defendant was still in prison, his case manager informed him that he was required to register as a predatory offender pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 243.166, subd. 1. Defendant filed a declaratory action, challenging the constitutionality of § 243.166. The State filed a motion for summary judgment, contending that defendant's conviction arose from the same circumstances as the charged predatory offense and, therefore, defendant was required to register as a predatory offender. The trial court granted the motion, and defendant challenged the judgment. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that a factual record was necessary to determine whether defendant's sexual assault arose from the same set of circumstances as defendant's robbery and assault conviction. The court reasoned that the facts underlying the offense were also necessary for a constitutional challenge to § 243.166. The court remanded for additional proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for further proceedings.

 

1006 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thaggard


C6-95-1822


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 332



March 19, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. H. Peter Albrecht, Judge. District Court File No. 94078283.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the District Court for Hennepin County (Minnesota), which convicted defendant of drug charges after it denied his motion to suppress, which alleged that the police violated Minn. R. Crim. P. 6.01 when they arrested him rather than issuing a citation for a misdemeanor traffic offense and they searched inside defendant's underwear after arresting him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested on a drug charge and driving after his license was suspended. The trial court dismissed the driving charge and convicted defendant of the drug charge. Defendant sought review, challenging the validity of the arrest and the search. The court affirmed, finding that (1) the arrest was lawful because the officers reasonably could have determined that arrest was necessary to prevent defendant's further criminal conduct of driving with a suspended license; (2) the officers' identification testimony was supported by evidence that they had an opportunity to see defendant as their squad car pulled alongside his vehicle; (3) the arrest was lawful because, before stopping defendant, the officers verified that the owner of the vehicle had a suspended drivers license, and they knew that fact when they arrested him; (4) the trial court was justified in crediting the officers' contradictory testimony; and (5) the search was lawful because it was a search incident to defendant's lawful arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the motion to suppress evidence and the judgment of conviction.

 

1007 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Kingbird v. Indep. Sch. Dist. No. 38


C1-95-2053


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 283



March 12, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Kingbird v. I.S.D. No. 38, 1996 Minn. LEXIS 339 (Minn., May 9, 1996)
Appeal after remand at Kingbird v. Independent Sch. Dist. No. 38, 1997 Minn. App. LEXIS 422 (Minn. Ct. App., Apr. 15, 1997)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Beltrami County; Hon. James E. Preece, Judge. District Court File No. C692863.
Kingbird v. Independent Sch. Dist. No. 38, 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 754 (Minn. Ct. App., Aug. 9, 1994)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant instructors sought review of the order of the District Court, Beltrami County (Minnesota) granting respondent school district's motion for summary judgment in a suit whereby the instructors claimed that their human and Indian rights had been violated.


OVERVIEW: The school district employed ten Native American instructors. The instructors did not hold college degrees and were paid 12 percent less than teachers with degrees. Thereafter, the instructors filed suit, claiming that their rights pursuant to the Minnesota Human Rights Act and the American Indian Education Act had been violated. The trial court granted the district's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the instructors challenged the order. Additionally, an individual instructor challenged the order. The court noted that the order granting summary judgment was not supported by the memoranda. Specifically, the court explained that it could not determine the basis for the order. Because the record was inadequate for review purposes, the court remanded the cause for more specific findings and rationale. Next, the court noted that the only method of appealing a school board's decision on teacher related matters was by writ of certiorari. Because the individual instructor did not file such a writ, the court held that the district court did not have jurisdiction to hear the matter. As such, his appeal was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The cause was remanded in order that the district court could make detailed findings of fact and the individual instructor's appeal was dismissed.

 

1008 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wold


C0-95-827


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 290



March 12, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Chisago County; Hon. Linn Slattengren, Judge. District Court File No. K09287.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the District Court, Chisago County (Minnesota), denying his suppression motion, claiming that a photo lineup was unduly suggestive.


OVERVIEW: Appellant held up a store. Thereafter, the storeowner chased appellant, who drove away in a black car. Appellant was arrested after he was found lying injured next to the black car. At a pretrial hearing, appellant sought to suppress evidence obtained through a photo lineup where the storeowner identified him as the perpetrator. He claimed that the lineup was impermissibly suggestive because his photo's background color differed from the background color of the other photos. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the court noted that a similar case had held that a lineup was not unconstitutional where the photo of the accused contained numbers in the background while the other photos did not. The court held that fine differences, such as background numbers or colors did not rise to the level of suggestive necessary to render a lineup unconstitutional. Further, the court found that the record contained ample evidence that appellant was the burglar. As such, the court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The order denying the suppression motion was affirmed on appeal.

 

1009 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cooper


CX-95-1449


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 299



March 12, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Itasca County; Hon. John Hawkinson, Judge. District Court File No. K2-94-725.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Itasca County (Minnesota), which convicted defendant of first-degree arson under Minn. Stat. § 609.561, subd. 1 (1990) and defrauding an insurer under Minn. Stat. § 609.611, subd. 1(b) (1990).


OVERVIEW: A fire occurred at defendant's family residence when the home was in foreclosure. During the course of defendant's trial, the jury toured defendant's burned home. Defendant was subsequently convicted of arson and insurance fraud. The court affirmed, holding that defendant was not denied his due process rights when the jury's viewing of the home did not strictly comply with the procedures outlined in Minn. R. Crim. P. 26.03, subd. 10, where a court reporter was not present. Because defendant did not object to the viewing at trial, the court reviewed under a plain error analysis. The court found that defense counsel's approval of the viewing procedure, presence during the entire viewing procedure, and lack of any issues raised at the site by either party satisfied the common sense reasons for having a court reporter at a viewing site. Defendant's allegation regarding the alleged improper search and seizure of his home was untimely. Defendant was not denied his right to a speedy trial because he was convicted two years after the fire occurred. There was no error in refusing defendant's request for a change in venue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1010 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kielmeyer


C8-95-932


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 251



February 27, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Wright County; Hon. Bruce R. Douglas, Judge. Dist. Ct. # K9-94-345.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions, by a jury, and sentence in the District Court, Wright County (Minnesota), for criminal vehicular homicide.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving home from a bar when he fatally struck a 13-year-old girl. Defendant did not report the accident. The girl's mother found her lying near a driveway. A reconstruction specialist ascertained that the vehicle pieces at the scene came from a 1983 Chevrolet Silverado. The officers confirmed that defendant visited a bar that evening and that he owned a Chevrolet pickup. The officers drove to defendant's residence where, with defendant's consent, looked at his truck, and finding front-end damage, seized the vehicle. Defendant told an officer that he hit the girl. Defendant was charged with two counts of criminal vehicular homicide. Defendant was convicted. His sentence was in excess of the presumptive sentence under the statutory guidelines. Defendant appealed. The court held that the evidence indicated that defendant was negligent and that such evidence was sufficient to sustain his conviction for criminal vehicular operation. The trial court did not err in departing from the presumptive sentence under the statutory guidelines. Defendant's flight from the scene of the crime and the emotional impact of the incident on the victim's family supported the departure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for criminal vehicular homicide.

 

1011 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Cohen v. Little Six, Inc.


C6-95-928


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


543 N.W.2d 376; 1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 155



February 13, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Scott County; Hon. Michael A. Young, Judge. District Court File No. C9501701.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant casino customer tried to sit on a chair in front of a slot machine at respondent tribal casino, the chair snapped, and she fell to the floor. The casino customer filed an action against the tribal casino and alleged that the fall caused injuries that required hospitalization. The casino customer challenged the decision of the District Court, Scott County (Minnesota), which dismissed her personal injury action for want of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The court held that because the tribe created, owned, and controlled the tribal casino to further the legitimate governmental purpose of raising and redistributing revenue for the welfare of the tribe, the tribal casino was entitled to assert the tribe's sovereign immunity. The tribal casino's operation of a gaming hall did not waive sovereign immunity because the Indian Gaming Regulatory Act, 25 U.S.C.S, §§ 2701-2721, did not waive sovereign immunity for actions for money damages. The court held that the appointment of an agent for the service of process and the registration as a foreign corporation waived only personal jurisdiction defenses, not sovereign immunity. The court held that 28 U.S.C.S. § 1360(a) was inapplicable to tribal corporate entities that were equivalent to the tribe for purposes of sovereign immunity. Because the events giving rise to the cause of action transpired wholly within the reservation, state court jurisdiction would infringe on tribal self-governance. Thus, the court lacked authority to hear the merits of the action. The court held that the casino customer was not denied due process because she was only deprived of her day in the court of her choice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that dismissed the casino customer's action because the tribal casino could assert the tribe's sovereign immunity, no federal statute authorized state jurisdiction over the action and state court jurisdiction would infringe on tribal self-governance. By dismissing the action for want of jurisdiction, the trial court did not violate the casino customer's right to due process.

 

1012 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Hart


C9-95-2057


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 156



February 9, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Kandiyohi County; Hon. Marilyn J. Justman, Judge. District Court File # P5931142.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant putative ward sought judicial review of an order of the District Court, Kandiyohi County (Minnesota) for his commitment to a security hospital as both a sexual psychopathic personality and as a sexually dangerous person. In a prior order upon respondent State's petition, the district court had committed him for a 60-day evaluation. After a hearing to review the evaluation period, the district court made his commitment indefinite.


OVERVIEW: The ward claimed that the evidence was insufficient to support his commitment. He sexually assaulted at least ten minor victims. The assaults spanned a period of approximately 30 years. He had been convicted of alcohol and drug offenses. Also, he had pled guilty to six counts of criminal sexual conduct. The district court found, inter alia, that his conduct displayed an utter lack of control. The court affirmed the order below, as clear and convincing evidence supported his commitment as a sexual psychopathic personality and a sexually dangerous person under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subds. 18a, 18b (1994 and Supp. 1995). A habitual course of sexual misconduct was evident in his convictions of criminal sexual conduct. He committed hundreds of sexual assaults on at least ten young boys using threats and force to commit such acts. The criminal acts to which he pled guilty created a rebuttable presumption that he engaged in harmful sexual misconduct, under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 7a(b), which he did not rebut. The expert testimony further buttressed the finding of his utter lack of control. Also, he refused treatment. Thus, he remained a danger to young boys.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of commitment.

In re Linehan


C1-95-2022


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


544 N.W.2d 308; 1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 162



February 9, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Bertrand Poritsky, Judge. District Court File No. P8940382.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convict challenged the decision of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which granted the petition of respondent State and county to commit the convict under the sexually dangerous persons statute, Minn. Stat. § 253B.02(18b).


OVERVIEW: The convict, a diagnosed psychopath, had served time for child molestation, rape, and murder, and had been before the court three prior times for matters relating to such offenses. Rather than jeopardize public safety with the convict on parole, the State and the county obtained his commitment by the trial court as a sexually dangerous person pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 253B.02(18b). The court affirmed the trial court's decision because (1) eight harmful sexual acts clearly and convincingly established a course of harmful conduct under Minn. Stat. § 253B.02(7a)(b), (2) his antisocial personality disorder bore a reasonable relationship to the grounds for commitment as required by Minn. Stat. § 253B.02(18b)(a)(3), (3) it was highly likely that his disorder would result in future harmful conduct, and (4) Minn. Stat. § 253B.02(18b) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to grant the request of the State and the county to commit the convict as a sexually dangerous person.

 

1014 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Oanes


C1-95-1064


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


543 N.W.2d 658; 1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 141



February 6, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Thomas W. Wexler, Judge. District Court File No. 94097138.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which convicted her of prostitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant greeted an undercover police officer at the door of a known brothel, and defendant led the officer into a room where she began to undress. Defendant was arrested and ultimately convicted of prostitution. On appeal, she challenged the sufficiency of the evidence to support the conviction. The court held that the officer's touching of defendant's breast constituted illegal sexual contact within the meaning of Minn. Stat. § 609.324, subd. 3(1) (1994). The court further held that the State was not required to show that the officer intended to sexually gratify himself in order to prove defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The court also held that because the evidence showed defendant's predisposition to engage in illegal sexual conduct, the trial court did not err in failing to make written findings regarding her entrapment defense. Finally, the court held that the trial court's reference in its findings of fact to legally irrelevant evidence regarding defendant's past was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's prostitution conviction.

 

1015 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Saunders


C9-95-907


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


542 N.W.2d 67; 1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 60



January 16, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Review of Appeal from Certiorari to District Court, Watonwan County; Hon. Terence M. Dempsey, Judge. District Court File No. K6-93-234.



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered in the negative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Where defendant was charged with violating Minn. Stat. § 147.081, subd. 3(3) (1994), regarding unauthorized medical practice, the District Court, Watonwan County (Minnesota) certified a question to the court, asking it to review the constitutionality of the act.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a dairy farmer who claimed that cows injected with the blood of a human would produce milk with specific immune properties that could cure diseases. In the course of selling this special form of milk, defendant dispensed medical advice concerning the treatment of cancer. A jury impaneled to try the dairy farmer for practicing medicine without a license in violation of § 147.081, subd. 3(3) deadlocked. The lower court certified the question of whether § 147.081, subd. 3(3) was unconstitutionally vague such that it violated the Constitutions of the United States and Minnesota. The lower court refused to certify three other issues that defendant desired to have reviewed by the court. The court answered the certified question in the negative, holding that § 147.081, subd. 3(3) provided a person of reasonable intelligence with sufficient guidance as to what conduct was prohibited and that it was not unconstitutionally vague even though it was somewhat general. The court ruled that the three questions not certified by the lower court were not reviewable because certification by the trial court was a precondition to review of the questions by the court.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the negative, holding that the statute prohibiting the practice of medicine without a license was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

1016 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Kruger v. Commissioner of Human Servs.


C4-95-1866


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 27



January 9, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Washington County; Hon. John E. Cass, Judge. District Court File No. C8-94-4075.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mental inmate sought review of the decision of the Washington County District Court (Minnesota) that dismissed his petition for a writ of habeas corpus challenging his psychiatric commitment.


OVERVIEW: The mental inmate was convicted of criminal sexual conduct and kidnapping in relation to an incident in which he abducted two 13-year-old children, raped the girl, forced the boy to perform sex acts, and ultimately killed the girl. The trial court ordered a psychiatric evaluation, as a result of which the inmate was committed as a psychiatric personality. Seventeen years after commitment the inmate petitioned the commissioner for discharge and also filed a writ of habeas corpus that challenged his commitment. The trial court dismissed the petition. The court held that all required factors for commitment were demonstrated in the criminal proceeding. The court held that the inmate's behavior exhibited a habitual course of misconduct in sexual matters, utter lack of power to control sexual impulses, and that he was a danger to others. In affirming the judgment the court held that commitment did not violate double jeopardy rights because commitment was remedial and was not for preventative detention.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1017 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State by Humphrey v. Directory Publishing Servs.


C1-95-1470


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 62



January 9, 1996, Decided  
January 16, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Gregg Johnson, Judge. District Court File No. C9-93-13373.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, directory publisher and president, sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), made in favor of respondent attorney general that ordered them to cease and desist from improper business practices and that imposed a penalty for violation of, inter alia, the Uniform Deceptive Trade Practices Act, Minn. Stat. § 325D.44(1). The violation stemmed from solicitation of advertising for appellants' directory.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, directory publisher and president, solicited advertising for their directory, which was a business-to-business directory and which was not distributed to customers. Respondent attorney general sued appellants for deceptive sales practices under various state laws including the Uniform Deceptive Trade Practices Act, Minn. Stat. § 325D.44(1). The trial court rendered summary judgment in favor of respondent that included an imposition of a civil penalty on appellants and a cease and desist directive. Appellants sought review in the court, and the court reversed in part and affirmed in part but upheld that directive and penalty. The court concluded that the trial court properly granted summary judgment. The court examined the 10 sales techniques utilized by appellants including using the term Yellow Pages and printing of the solicitations on yellow paper. The trial court had concluded from these undisputed techniques that the direct mail solicitations and invoices of appellants taken as a whole created the overall impression that recipient businesses were being solicited for yellow page advertising in their area telephone directory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in part. The cease and desist directive and civil penalty were upheld against appellants, directory publisher and president, and in favor of respondent attorney general. The court found that the trial court did not err in using a tendency to deceive standard in applying an applicable state act and ruled that the standard was not invalid and that the applicable act was not void for vagueness.

 

1018 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Watley


C4-95-1107


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


541 N.W.2d 345; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1571



December 26, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Isabel Gomez, Judge. District Court File No. 94-68870.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a judgment by the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which dismissed criminal drug charges against defendant. The district court ruled that double jeopardy barred the criminal prosecution because of a prior civil administrative forfeiture of property found in proximity to the controlled substances seized from defendant.


OVERVIEW: Police stopped defendant's vehicle because it matched a description of a vehicle involved in a "shots fired" call earlier. In a search of defendant's vehicle, drugs were found. Defendant's vehicle, jewelry, and other items were seized, and he was provided with a "Notice of Seizure and Intent to Forfeit Property" form. Defendant did not demand judicial review of the administrative forfeiture. Subsequently criminal drugs charges were filed. The trial court dismissed the criminal complaint on double jeopardy grounds. The court reversed and remanded for trial. The court held that the double jeopardy clause protected against multiple punishments for the same offense. The court held defendant had the burden of proof to show that a civil remedy was punitive for purposes of invoking the double jeopardy clause. The court held that an administrative forfeiture was "remedial" in nature. Thus, the court concluded that the stipulation of forfeiture that defendant entered into was not in the form of a judgment and that jeopardy did not attach because defendant did not subject himself to risk of punishment or guilt.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for a new trial.

 

1019 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Reuhl v. W.W. Holes Mfg. Co.


C6-95-1304


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1592



December 26, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Thomas H. Carey, Judge. District Court File No. 94014581.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant boat club appealed the decision of the District Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota), which, in plaintiff purchaser's action alleging fraud, consumer fraud, and deceptive trade practices, denied the boat club's pretrial motion to compel arbitration.


OVERVIEW: The purchaser contracted the boat club concerning certain problems he had with the boat. The boat club responded that the purchase contract required arbitration. However, the parties did not pursue arbitration. The purchaser eventually filed a complaint alleging that the boat club had violated the deceptive trade practices act, had committed consumer fraud and common law fraud, and that the arbitration clause was void. The boat club answered and filed various counter claims, including a permissive counterclaim. It did not assert arbitration as an affirmative defense. Shortly before trial was to commence, the boat club filed a motion to compel arbitration. The trial court held that the boat club had waived its right to arbitrate the dispute, and the boat club appealed. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, holding that the boat club was required to assert arbitration as a defense at the onset of the litigation. Furthermore, the boat club's assertion of counterclaims demonstrated a deliberate waiver of the contract's arbitration provision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision denying the boat club's motion to compel arbitration.

 

1020 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Greyeagle


C9-95-1295


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


541 N.W.2d 326; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1540



December 19, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Brown County; Hon. Terri Jean Stoneburner, Judge. District Court File No. T295361.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the District Court, Brown County (Minnesota), which convicted her of driving without a license and driving a vehicle with revoked license plates, and denied her motion to dismiss the charges on grounds that the trooper's decision to stop her was not based on a specific, articulable suspicion of criminal activity.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by police solely because the car she drove bore WX plates, which indicated that the plates were specially issued by the Commissioner of Public Safety pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 168.041 (1994). After the trooper stopped defendant, he learned that her driver's license had been revoked after a driving under the influence charge, and the plates, issued because of her husband's conduct, had been revoked after defendant's conviction for driving without insurance. The court determined that when the trooper stopped defendant, he entertained only the general suspicion that some drivers would have misused the special license privilege. The court explained that because the trooper stopped defendant's car solely pursuant to his policy of stopping every VX or VY car, he did not have the required suspicion for making the stop. The court noted that the policy of routinely stopping all such vehicles constituted a violation of the constitutional requirement that vehicles could not have been stopped absent particularized police suspicion. The court concluded that the State failed to meet its burden of demonstrating the effectiveness of its suspicionless search policy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court, which convicted defendant of driving without a license and driving a vehicle with revoked license plates, and denied her motion to dismiss the charges on grounds that the trooper's decision to stop her was not based on a specific, articulable suspicion of criminal activity.

 

1021 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Anker v. Little


C4-95-1575


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


541 N.W.2d 333; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1560; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P14,504



December 19, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Blue Earth County; Hon. Richard L. Kelly, Judge. District Court File No. CX94198.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trustee sought review of the decision of the District Court, Blue Earth County (Minnesota), which awarded summary judgment to respondent manufacturer in his action that asserted that the manufacturer's automobiles were uncrashworthy. The trustee asserted that the court improperly construed Minn. Stat. § 169.685, subd. 4 (1994) as applying to crashworthiness actions.


OVERVIEW: A trustee brought an action against a manufacturer that accused it of making uncrashworthy vehicles. The trial court awarded summary judgment to the manufacturer and the court affirmed. Minn. Stat. § 169.685, subd. 4 (1994) unambiguously provided that proof of the installation of seat belts was not admissible in litigation that involved personal injuries resulting form the use of a motor vehicle and the plain language of that statute was binding. Although courts could engage in a broad inquiry of statutes whose language produced an absurd result, this authority could only be exercised sparingly and where a statute's plain language violated the legislature's expressed goal. The trustee challenged the constitutionality of § 169.685, subd. 4 under Minn. Const. art. I, § 8, and the Equal Protection and Due Process Clauses of the Minnesota and United States Constitutions, but the court found that the trustee had not proved his claims beyond a reasonable doubt. Statutes were always presumed to be constitutional. Parties had no right to present irrelevant evidence and thus the restrictions created by Minn. Stat. § 169.685, subd. 4 did not violate the trustee's due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's award of summary judgment to the manufacturer.

 

1022 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Minnesota Council of Dog Clubs v. City of Minneapolis


C4-95-1284


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


540 N.W.2d 903; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1510



December 12, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied January 25, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Minn. LEXIS 89.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hennepin County; Hon. Thomas H. Carey, Judge. District Court File No. 9318522.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, two nonprofit state and national organizations of dog owners, were successful in their action against respondent city, which had challenged the constitutionality of several provisions of the Minnesota Cruelty to Animals Act, Minn. Stat. §§ 343.22, 343.235, 343.29, and filed a request for attorney fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. The District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota) denied the request, and the organizations sought review.


OVERVIEW: In denying the request for fees, the district court concluded that the city's conduct had nothing to do with the constitutional infirmities alleged; that the city had not violated the organizations' due process rights; and that the organizations' lawsuit had only challenged "anticipatory enforcement" of the challenged provisions. On review, the court affirmed, holding that the organizations had properly asserted a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim, as required for a fee award under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, but that the city was not liable under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for merely following state law. A local government could only be held liable if, under color of some official policy, it cause the violation of another's constitutional rights. A municipality must make a deliberate choice to follow a course of action from among various alternatives to sustain § 1983 liability. In this case, the city was limited to following now invalidated state law to achieve certain enforcement objectives. The city's policy was innocuous and constitutionally permissible and its causal connection to the alleged violation was more attenuated than a policy of enforcing state law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of attorney fees and costs to the organizations.

 

1023 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crims


C6-95-41, C1-95-304


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


540 N.W.2d 860; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1441



November 28, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. John J. Sommerville, Judge. District Court File No. 93105448.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which, based on a jury verdict, convicted him of third-degree criminal sexual conduct, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 609.3441(c). The trial court denied defendant's motion for a new trial. Defendant's first trial ended in a hung jury.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction of third-degree criminal sexual conduct. The court held: (1) that the trial court did not commit plain error by failing to provide to an additional instruction when the jury requested clarification as to whether rape included forcible continuance of initially consensual sexual relations because the trial court had referred the jury to its initial written instructions and there was nothing in the record which indicated that the jury was incapable of resolving its confusion by reviewing the initial instructions; (2) that defendant incorrectly argued on appeal that rape was a legal impossibility after a victim initially consented to penetration; (3) that defendant failed to show that the victim's sexual history was relevant to his defense of the charge of rape; particularly, defendant failed to establish a modus operandi because the record showed no pattern of similar sexual behavior on part of the victim; and (4) that the trial court did not abuse its discretion to grant a new trial on the basis of alleged juror misconduct because defendant failed to prove the actual misconduct and prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of third-degree criminal sexual conduct.

Jacobson v. County of Goodhue


C9-95-1118


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


539 N.W.2d 623; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1421



November 21, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Goodhue County; Hon. Robert R. King, Jr., Judge. District Court File No. C1-87-32596.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bar owners sought review of a decision from the District Court, Goodhue County (Minnesota), which granted respondent county's motion to vacate an injunction prohibiting the enforcement of a county ordinance prohibiting nudity in liquor establishments.


OVERVIEW: Four years after the bar owners obtained an injunction prohibiting the county from enforcing an ordinance prohibiting nudity in liquor establishments on the ground that the ordinance violated Minn. Const. art. 1, § 3, the county moved to vacate the injunction based on a subsequent state supreme court decision holding an identical ordinance constitutional. The trial court granted the county's motion and vacated the injunction. On appeal, the court affirmed. The county's action seeking to have the injunction vacated was not barred by res judicata. The precedent established by the state supreme court constituted a sufficient change in legal circumstances to warrant relief from the injunction. Under the trial court's equitable powers and under Minn. R. Civ. P. 60.02(e), it retained jurisdiction to vacate the injunction. The decision in the state supreme court case was controlling at the trial level. The county had the authority to restrict nudity in liquor establishments pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. 21. Under state law, that authority existed notwithstanding the free speech provision of Minn. Const. art. 1, § 3.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment vacating the injunction.

In re Welfare of L.J.S.


C6-95-993, CX-95-995


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


539 N.W.2d 408; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1386



November 14, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Charles A. Porter, Jr., Judge. District Court File Nos. 184032; 175307.



DISPOSITION: Certified questions answered in the negative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota) certified two questions raising constitutional challenges to the new extended jurisdiction juvenile statute and to the new presumption of certification applied in certain juvenile delinquency proceedings, Minn. Stat. §§ 260.125, subd. 2a, 260.126, subd. 1(2), in two juvenile actions.


OVERVIEW: Petitions were filed against two juveniles for various criminal conduct. The trial court presented consolidated certified questions to the appeals court: (1) Is the provision in Minn. Stat. § 260.126, subd. 1(2) for prosecutor-designated extended jurisdiction juvenile proceedings unconstitutionally vague? (2) Does the prosecutor-designated extended jurisdiction juvenile provision violate the separation of powers? (3) Does the presumptive certification statute, Minn. Stat. § 260.125, subd. 2a, violate equal protection? (4) Does the presumptive certification statute violate due process by creating a mandatory irrebuttable presumption of certification? (5) Does the presumptive certification statute violate due process by placing on the juvenile the burden of persuasion? The court concluded that the statutes were constitutional and answered the consolidated certified questions in the negative. The court noted that the statutory criteria are very specific and neither vague nor conducive to arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement. The court also found that the limited prosecutor-designated extended jurisdiction juvenile provision did not violate the separation of powers.


OUTCOME: The court answered the two certified questions in the negative and held that the prosecutor-designated extended jurisdiction juvenile provision did not violate the separation of powers and that the statutory provision for a prosecutor-designated extended jurisdiction juvenile proceeding was not unconstitutionally vague and did not violate the separation-of-powers doctrine.

Hartson v. City of Duluth


C8-95-1062


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1397



November 14, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, St. Louis County; Hon. David S. Bouschor, Judge. District Court File No. C8-94-600624.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen sought review of a decision of the District Court of St. Louis County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent city in the citizen's action for personal injury damages arising from her fall in a city park.


OVERVIEW: The citizen fell while descending a staircase. She filed suit on theories of negligence and strict liability alleging the accident was caused by a small gap between two halves of a step on the staircase. The city filed a motion for summary judgment relying on Minn. Stat. § 466.03, subd. 6e. The trial court granted the motion. The court affirmed, finding that the statute afforded the city no greater immunity than that enjoyed by private landowners, thus it created no inequality and the citizen's equal protection challenge, made on the basis of Minn. Stat. art. I, § 2, failed. The court held that because private citizens enjoyed no common law remedy for injuries caused by governmental acts, such as the maintenance of public recreational facilities, the municipal park immunity statute did not violate Minn. Const. art. I, § 8. The court held that while a defendant's alleged breach of tort duties often presented a question of fact for the jury, the trial court could grant summary judgment if the plaintiff failed to offer any specific facts to support an element of the claim, thus, the trial court properly granted summary judgment in favor of the city.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of the city was affirmed.

State v. Palkovich


C3-95-62


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1404



November 14, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, St. Louis County; Hon. Gerald E. Maher, Judge. District Court File No. T9-94-604312.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of the judgment of the District Court, St. Louis County (Minnesota), which convicted him for failure to provide proof of auto insurance under Minn. Stat. § 169.791 (1994).


OVERVIEW: The driver was convicted for failure to provide proof of auto insurance under Minn. Stat. § 169.791 (1994). The court affirmed the driver's conviction. Although the driver was convicted for only the failure to provide proof of insurance, he claimed that § 169.791 and the compulsory insurance requirement of Minn. Stat. § 65B.42, .48 did not unconstitutionally infringed upon his right to travel. The right to travel was a fundamental right under the federal constitution; however, the court did not find that the requirement to provide proof of insurance implicated the right to intrastate travel, as it affected only one mode of transportation. Moreover, the statute affected motor vehicle owners and permitted non-owners 10 days to provide the identity and address of the owner. Nor did the compulsory insurance requirement deny the driver equal protection of the laws by creating two classes of persons: those who could afford insurance and those who could not, as even if the law was not rationally related to a legitimate state interest, the driver was admittedly in a high-risk category because of a DWI conviction, a classification that resulted from his own actions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the inmate's conviction for failure to provide proof of auto insurance.

Vern Reynolds Constr. v. City of Champlin


C7-95-1196


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


539 N.W.2d 614; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1363



November 7, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Peter J. Lindberg, Judge. District Court File No. 9419769.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City of Champion sought review of an order of the District Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment and a judgment of mandamus to appellee landowner compelling eminent domain proceedings. At issue was whether a lack of notice that a taking had previously occurred provided a subsequent landowner with standing to pursue an inverse condemnation claim upon showing that the former owner was not compensated.


OVERVIEW: Prior to the landowner purchasing the property, the City had constructed a water main that ran under the easterly part of the land and a lift station and water pumping facility to pump water away from a shopping center through reinforced concrete pipe under a highway and onto the westerly part of the land. The City never commenced eminent domain proceedings. It initially planned to reroute the storm water but finally decided to permanently divert storm water onto the property. The City refused to initiate eminent domain proceedings to obtain a permanent water drainage easement. The landowner sued. The trial court granted its motion for summary judgment and a writ of mandamus. The City appealed. The landowner sought counsel fees on appeal under Minn. Stat. § 117.045 (1994). The court affirmed finding that notice of the taking was a critical factor in determining whether a party had standing to pursue a condemnation claim. The court noted that the landowner was the owner at the time that the City changed its use from a trespass/nuisance into a permanent drainage easement. The court held that counsel fees on appeal were not provided for in the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of the landowner and issuing a writ of mandamus compelling eminent domain proceedings was affirmed. The landowner's request for counsel fees on appeal was denied.

Neumann v. City of St. Paul


CX-95-1080


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


538 N.W.2d 921; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1367



November 7, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. John S. Connolly, Judge. Dist. Ct. File C4944509.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured party sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which dismissed his negligence action against respondent city pursuant to the recreational services immunity statute, Minn. Stat. § 466.03, subd. 6(e) (1994).


OVERVIEW: The injured party was tossed into a lake when the supervisor of the paddle boat concession jumped onto one of their boat's pontoons in an effort to disengage it from the dock. The injured party filed a negligence claim against the city, but the trial court dismissed the claim on summary judgment, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 466.03, subd. 6(e) (1994), the recreational immunity statute. The court first ruled that the city owed no duty to the injured party as a potential trespasser because no claim was asserted that a dangerous condition existed that necessitated that the city have taken preventative steps. Because the injured party's claim was one exclusively in negligence, the court held that the matter fit squarely under § 466.03, subd. 6(e), which provided immunity to the city for the negligent operation of a municipal park by one of their employees. The court also held that under the rational basis test, § 466.03, subd. 6(e) was not a violation of the Equal Protection Clause because the shield provided to the city from potentially huge tort liability was rationally related to the purpose of "the preservation of Minnesota's outdoor recreational resources."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which dismissed the injured party's negligence claim against the city.

Manteuffel v. City of N. St. Paul


C3-95-837


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


538 N.W.2d 727; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1308; 11 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 208



October 24, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Michael T. DeCourcy, Judge. District Court File C4947007.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city employee sought review of an order of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which dismissed, for a lack of subject matter jurisdiction, the employee's action alleging that respondent city had violated the Whistleblower Act. The district court held that the employee's sole method of obtaining judicial review of the city's decision to terminate his employment was by writ of certiorari directly to the court.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for the city as a probationary police officer. One of his training officers was involved in an altercation with a youth. The employee told the officer that he thought the officer had used excessive force. The employee was terminated shortly thereafter on the recommendation of the police chief. The employee filed a claim for age discrimination and a violation of the Whistleblower Act. The age discrimination claim was dismissed through summary judgment, which the court upheld. The Whistleblower claim was dismissed by the district court on the ground that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction. The court held that the district court erred in dismissing the claim. A writ of certiorari to the court was not the exclusive method of review available to the employee for his injuries arising from the city's violation of the Whistleblower Act. The Act, at Minn. Stat. § 181.935(a), specifically provided a civil remedy in the district court for violations. A writ of certiorari would only have been proper if there was no adequate method of review or legal remedy The employee was entitled to a civil cause of action in the district court as provided by Minn. Stat. § 181.935(a).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order dismissing the employee's Whistleblower Act claim and remanded for a trial on the merits.

Roatch v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C5-95-659


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1288



October 17, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Dakota County; Hon. Patrice K. Sutherland, Judge. Dist. Ct. File C8952009.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commissioner of Public Safety sought review of the judgment of the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota), which rescinded the revocation of respondent motorist's driving privileges under Minn. Stat. § 169.123 (1994), the implied consent statute, for driving with .10 or more alcohol concentration. The motorist moved to dismiss the appeal, to strike the references in the Commissioner's brief to excluded evidence, and for attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped to assist the motorist, whose car was parked on the side of the road with the hood raised. The officer detected an odor of alcohol and saw empty beer cans in the vehicle. The officer asked where the motorist had come from and whether he had been drinking; the motorist answered that he had come from home and that he had been drinking. A breathalyzer test indicated that the motorist's alcohol concentration was .10 or more. The Commissioner revoked the motorist's license pursuant to § 169.123. The trial court concluded that the motorist was in custody when the officer initially questioned the motorist and that, because no Miranda warnings were given, the motorist's answers to the questions and all evidence of intoxication observed by the officer had to be suppressed; accordingly, the trial court rescinded the revocation of the motorist's license. On appeal, the court reversed. There was no need for the officer to have a reasonable articulable suspicion of criminal activity when he stopped to assist the motorist. Assuming that Miranda warnings were required, sufficient evidence apart from the motorist's answers existed to warrant administration of intoxication tests.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and reinstated the revocation of the motorist's driving privileges. The court denied the motorist's motion to dismiss the appeal, to strike the references in the Commissioner's brief to excluded evidence, and for attorney fees.

Zuehlke v. Independent Sch. Dist. No. 316


C0-95-1007


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


538 N.W.2d 721; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1293



October 17, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari to Independent School District No. 316.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator non-licensed education support employees, who worked for a cooperative school district at the time of the cooperative's dissolution, sought certiorari review of a decision of respondent member school district, which passed two companion resolutions on the posting of non-licensed positions. Respondent union was allowed to intervene.


OVERVIEW: The employees worked for the cooperative school district until its dissolution. The cooperative school district provided special education services to six member school districts, including the district the employees brought their action against. Anticipating the cooperative school district's dissolution, the district passed two companion resolutions on the posting of non-licensed positions for a certain school year. The employees brought their action after the district under its collective bargaining agreement with the union allowed only union members to bid on the four positions that the employees claimed were created as a result of the dissolution. On review, the court overturned the district's decision and remanded. The court held that, because Minn. Stat. § 122.895, subd. 8 (1994) allowed the employees to bid for positions created as a result of the dissolution of a cooperative in the order of their seniority within the dissolved cooperative, the district's posting process violated their rights. The court ruled that reversal was warranted when a school district has either failed to show a substantial basis in the record or had misapplied the applicable law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the district and remanded for development of a record on the creation of the disputed positions.

State v. Fox


C1-95-481


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1258



October 10, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. John J. Sommerville, Judge. District Court File No. 91082437.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) denying his petition for postconviction relief from the sentence imposed for his conviction, entered pursuant to a guilty plea, for criminal sexual conduct.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with two counts of first degree criminal sexual conduct and one count of kidnapping. Defendant pleaded guilty to one count of first degree criminal sexual conduct in exchange for the dismissal of the other charges and the State's agreement not to seek an upward departure of more than 1.5 times the presumptive sentence. At the time of the plea bargain, the parties believed that appellant's criminal history score was two and that the departure sought by the State would lead to a 165-month sentence. At the sentencing hearing, it was determined that appellant's criminal history score was three. Appellant was given the opportunity to withdraw his plea but he did not do so and he was sentenced to 183 months' imprisonment. On direct appeal, the court affirmed. On appeal from the denial of appellant's motion for postconviction relief, the court affirmed. Appellant's plea was voluntary, knowing, and intelligent. Appellant's medical records did not show that his plea was involuntary; rather, they indicated that he did not suffer from any mental incapacity. Appellant was not entitled to an evidentiary hearing because material facts were not in dispute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1034 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Starnes


C2-95-148


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1281



October 10, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Dakota County; Hon. William F. Thuet, Judge. District Court File # K2941833.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the District Court, Dakota County (Minnesota), to a charge of harassment in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.749, subds. 2(4) (1994), but he claimed on appeal that the harassment statute was overbroad in violation of the First Amendment and improperly created a strict liability offense in violation of his due process rights.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with harassing his estranged wife, which for him was a felony because he had earlier been convicted of violating his wife's order for protection. He pleaded guilty to harassment by means of repeated telephone calls in violation of § 609.749, subds. 2(4). On appeal he claimed that the statute violated his First Amendment and due process rights. The court affirmed the judgment, ruling that defendant failure to argue to overbreadth or due process claims at trial waived the issues on appeal, particularly given his guilty plea. The court ruled that despite a valid guilty plea, a person was able to argue on appeal that the charge was one that the State had no constitutional right to prosecute. Defendant, however, chose to plead guilty to violating § 609.749, subds. 2(4). That section defined an act and did not directly involve speech. He also agreed to a dismissal of the intent to injure charge under § 609.749, subd. 2(1) (1994). The court concluded that defendant did not demonstrate an intent to preserve a constitutional challenge. Accordingly, he was not able to raise the constitutional challenges for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for harassment.

State v. George


CX-94-2638


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1237



September 27, 1995, Decided  
October 3, 1995, FILED


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Nobles County; Hon. Timothy K. Connell, Judge. District Court File No. K3-93-529.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court, Nobles County (Minnesota), which convicted him for possession of a handgun without a permit under Minn. Stat. § 624.714.


OVERVIEW: An officer pulled defendant over because of a headlight violation. The officer asked defendant if he had any objections to a search of his motorcycle, and defendant replied that he did not. Although defendant earlier told the officer that he did not have any weapons in his possession, he later told the officer that he had a gun in his jacket pocket and that there was a semiautomatic weapon in the back of the motorcycle. The officer also found marijuana in defendant's possession. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress, holding that the stop was valid and the search was consensual. The court upheld defendant's conviction for possession of a handgun without a permit. The court rejected defendant's argument that the stop was a fabricated pretext, as the officer knew the violation alleged was not really a violation. The officer testified that he believed the placement and number of the headlamps on defendant's motorcycle was illegal. The court also did not credit defendant's claim that his consent was given out of fear and intimidation. Defendant testified that the officer did not threaten him, pull a gun, or become physically aggressive toward him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1036 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Lipka v. Minnesota Sch. Employees Ass'n, Local 1980


C1-95-707


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


537 N.W.2d 624; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1214; 150 L.R.R.M. 2694



September 26, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Beltrami County; Hon. James E. Preece, Judge. District Court File No. C893535.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, administrator of worker's estate, challenged the order of the District Court, Beltrami County (Minnesota), which awarded summary judgment against her to respondents, national and local unions, and local union president, for assault, gender discrimination, reprisal, intentional and negligent infliction of emotional distress, unfair representation, breach of contract, conspiracy, and tortious interference with contract.


OVERVIEW: The worker was harassed by the president, and filed complaints. The worker died. An administrator was appointed for the estate in the action. The district court awarded summary judgment to the unions and president on the basis that some of the actions had abated at the worker's death. The administrator appealed. The court affirmed. The claims for breach of contract, tortious interference with a contract and unfair representation had survived the worker's death. Because the assault and emotional distress claims were injuries to the worker's person, those claims had abated under Minn. Stat. § 573.02, subd. 2 (1994). The underlying acts of transfer, harassment, and assault on the unfair representation claim were not bargaining subjects and the worker failed to follow the reporting procedures. The breach of contract claim based upon union constitutions that had no provision for the monetary damages claimed was not viable. As parties to the contract, the unions were not liable for tortious interference and the claim was not viable against the president because essential element of damages was missing. Because only the president was involved, the conspiracy claim was unviable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the district court, which awarded summary judgment to the unions and the president.

 

1037 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Welfare of B.C.G.


C4-95-524


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


537 N.W.2d 489; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1217



September 26, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Clay County; Hon. Michael L. Kirk, Judge. District Court File No. J19550021.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Clay County (Minnesota). The district court declined to apply the 1994 amendments to the juvenile reference statute and decided to refer appellant, alleged to have committed first-degree criminal sexual conduct in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.342, subds. 1(a), 2, for adult prosecution.


OVERVIEW: The district court denied appellant's request to proceed under the 1994 amendments on the basis that the amended statute could be applied only to offenses occurring on or after January 1, 1995, the statute's effective date. Appellant allegedly committed the offense on December 21, 1994, and a juvenile delinquency petition was filed on January 11, 1995. The court held that the district court should have applied the 1994 amendments to appellant's case, rather than the unamended 1992 juvenile statute and rules. Both Minn. Stat. § 260.125, subd. 1 (1994), the new certification procedure, and Minn. Stat. § 260.126, subd. 1 (1994), the Extended Jurisdiction Juvenile (EJJ) process, stated that it was the "proceeding," rather than the alleged violation, that was to be certified or designated. The legislature's consistent reference to "proceeding" indicated that the relevant date for determining whether the amendments applied was the date juvenile proceedings were commenced. Appellant knowingly and voluntarily waived his protection against the ex post facto application of the new law, and no policy reasons existed for denying appellant the right to waive that constitutional protection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with directions to the district court to determine whether to certify appellant as an adult and whether to designate appellant's proceeding under the EJJ in light of the factors provided in the amended 1994 juvenile statute and rules.

 

1038 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Parker


C4-95-426


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


538 N.W.2d 141; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1226



September 26, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Wright County; Hon. Kim R. Johnson, Judge. District Court File KX931316.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court, Wright County (Minnesota), which convicted him of driving while under the influence of alcohol within 5 years of a prior impaired driving conviction. The court held that defendant's 180-day driver's license revocation for failing an intoxilyzer test, a civil sanction, did not constitute punishment and therefore did not bar his subsequent criminal prosecution for the same incident.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended on appeal that his civil sanction for driving while under the influence of alcohol, a 180-day revocation of his driver's license imposed after he failed an intoxilyzer test, constituted punishment and barred his subsequent criminal prosecution for the same incident. The court noted that Minnesota courts rejected defendant's argument that a remedy that was not solely remedial was punishment. The court held that defendant's case was an example of the all too common case in which a driver who repeatedly endangered the lives and well-being of others by driving while intoxicated was merely deprived of the privilege to drive for a six-month period. The court stated that the civil penalty was rationally related to the State's interest in protecting the public from impaired drivers. The court affirmed the judgment, as it found that the fact that the civil remedy could in some instances deter drunken driving or inconvenience those to whom it was applied did not render it punishment under the Double Jeopardy Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1039 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Kottschade v. City of Rochester


C3-94-2481


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


537 N.W.2d 301; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1194



September 19, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Olmsted County; Hon. John S. Gowan, Judge. Dist. Ct. # C7-88-5994.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Olmstead County (Minnesota) granted summary judgment to respondent landowner in his action against appellant municipality challenging the municipality's denial of applications for permission to convey land. The municipality appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner arranged to sell a portion of his land to a corporation. At first, the landowner's variance request was denied. However, the municipality later granted the landowner's applications for conveyances. Thereafter, the municipality denied several of the landowner's applications to convey land. The municipality also conditioned approval of the landowner's request for vacation of an easement on his payment of funds to the municipality. The landowner then filed an action against the municipality. The trial court granted summary judgment to the landowner on his equal protection claims and on his taking and substantive due process claims and granted summary judgment to the municipality on all other claims. On appeal, the court determined that the municipality did not take a portion of the landowner's property because the property was dedicated for public use. Also, the court found that the landowner's equal protection rights were not violated because the municipality could condition its vacation of an easement on a cash payment by the landowner. Therefore, the court concluded that that the municipality should have been granted summary judgment on all issues.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the landowner in his action against the municipality challenging the municipality's denial of applications for permission to convey land.
