R. B. v. C. S.


CX-95-365, CX-95-527


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


536 N.W.2d 634; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1117



August 29, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Norman County; Hon. John M. Roue, Judge. District Court File No. F89450037.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant putative father sought review of a decision of the District Court Norman County (Minnesota), which determined that he lacked standing to bring a paternity action. Appellant child sought review of the denial of her request for blood tests under Minn. Stat. §§ 257.55 and 257.57.


OVERVIEW: The child was born out of wedlock, and the putative father did not object when the mother told him that respondent, another man, was being named the child's father. The other man signed a declaration of paternity that was immediately submitted to the registrar for vital statistics. The trial court awarded physical custody of the child to her mother and joint legal custody to both parties subject to the putative father's liberal rights of visitation. The mother was killed in a car accident one month after the other man was adjudicated the child's father. He took custody of the girl and moved the court for sole custody. The trial court found that the putative father lacked standing to bring a paternity action and rejected the child's request for blood tests on the grounds that she failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision to deny standing and reversed the dismissal of the child's paternity action. The court found that the child's interests were paramount, and she was entitled to be a party to an adjudication of her paternity, notwithstanding any prior paternity action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to deny standing to the putative father, reversed the dismissal of the child's paternity action and request for blood tests, and reversed the case.

Bechtold v. City of Rosemount


C3-94-2366


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1126



August 29, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to City of Rosemount.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator employee appealed the judgment of respondent city, which dismissed him from his position as the city's director of parks and recreation in his writ of certiorari challenging his termination.


OVERVIEW: The city hired a new city administrator. The administrator evaluated the city government's organization and staff and solicited ideas from workers about how to streamline organizations. Some suggested combining the city's department of parks and recreation with the local community center and putting them under one person's authority. The administrators showed department heads the proposed organizational plans exhibiting the one department for parks and recreation and the community center. The administrator recommended that the director of community center be appointed as the director of the new department because he had experience in managing an arena. Before the issue came to the city council for a vote, the administrator discussed the recommendation with the council members individually. The administrator sent the employee a letter informing him of the layoff. The council voted to adopt the planned merger and the layoff of the employee. The employee appealed. The court affirmed, holding that city eliminated the employee's position for legitimate business reasons and did not violate the employee's due process rights. Further, there was no violation of the open meeting law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the city's decision terminating the employee.

Cressy v. Grassman


C5-95-886, C7-95-887


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


536 N.W.2d 39; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1089



August 22, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Carver County; Hon. Jean A. Davies, Judge. Dist. Ct. Files CX95117, C59525.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the driver and the bus owner, appealed the judgment of the District Court, Carver County (Minnesota), which rendered summary judgment in favor of respondent personal injury victims, arguing that the district court erroneously upheld the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 169.685(4), in an action for personal injuries in connection with a traffic accident.


OVERVIEW: The personal injury victims brought separate negligence actions against the bus owner and the driver in connection with a traffic accident in which the victims' car was struck from behind by a bus. Appellants raised as a defense the failure to wear a seat belt. The district court granted summary judgment motions in favor of the victims, explicitly upholding the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 169.685(4), which precluded admission of evidence of seat-belt nonuse. Appellants challenged both summary judgments, and the appeals were consolidated. The court affirmed because the statute was rationally related to a legitimate state interest, the safety of motorists, and it did not violate the equal protections clause. In addition, appellants' right to reduce a judgment against them was no less importation than the government's interest in maintaining efficient trial procedure by avoiding complicating trials with expert-witness testimony on the mitigating effects of seat-belt use; therefore, appellants' due process claim also failed.


OUTCOME: In an action for personal injuries arising from a motor vehicle accident, the court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the personal injury victims and against the driver and bus owner.

 

1043 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kinsella


C4-94-2277


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1049



August 15, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Deborah Hedlund, Judge. District Court File No. 93100065.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of indecent conduct pursuant to Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 385.160. The District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota) denied his motion for judgment of acquittal or, in the alternative, for a new trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance prohibited a person from fondling his unclothed genitals in a public place. Defendant argued that the video booth at the establishment where the offense occurred was not a "public place." The court disagreed based on the definitions of "public place" provided by Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 385.10 and by the Minnesota courts. Defendant had no reasonable expectation of privacy; an officer could see clearly into the booth and a sign was posted warning of police surveillance. Defendant argued that the ordinance was unconstitutionally overbroad because it was aimed at expressive conduct. The court held that the ordinance was not unconstitutional on its face. Fondling one's unclothed genitals in a public place was not protected expressive conduct. Defendant's co-defendant had pleaded guilty to indecent conduct under the ordinance. The court held that the erroneous admission his conviction constituted prejudicial error. The jury was not instructed to disregard and its specific inquiry about the conviction indicated that the verdict might have been more favorable to defendant if the evidence had not been admitted. Therefore, defendant was entitled to a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case for a new trial.

In re Thomas


C6-95-735


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 1011



August 8, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied March 18, 1996.
Review denied by In re Thomas, 1995 Minn. LEXIS 861 (Minn., Sept. 28, 1995)
Writ of certiorari denied Thomas v. Heise, 516 U.S. 1177, 116 S. Ct. 1274, 134 L. Ed. 2d 220, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 1852 (1996)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Cara Lee Neville, Judge. Dist. Ct. File P98933646.
In re Thomas, 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 1243 (Minn. Ct. App., Dec. 12, 1990)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate's commitment as a psychopathic personality was to be served at a correctional facility where he was serving sentences for sexual assaults. After a sex offender treatment program was terminated, the State sought to amend the place of commitment to a security hospital and to delay transfer until the prison sentences were completed. The District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota) granted the State's motion, and the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate, who was committed as a psychopathic personality while confined at a correctional facility, sought an immediate transfer to a security hospital, or, alternatively, an order requiring the Commissioner of Corrections and the Commissioner of Human Services to offer a treatment program at the correctional facility. On appeal, the court affirmed judgment denying the inmate's motion and ordering that the inmate be transferred to the security hospital upon the completion of his prison sentence. The court found that the inmate's challenges to the constitutionality of the psychopathic personality statute were merely restatements of arguments that had been previously rejected. The immediate transfer of the inmate to the security hospital was not possible because Minn. Stat. § 253B.185, subd. 2(b) provided that the criminal sentence had to first be served in the correctional facility. The court held that the inmate's request for treatment at the correctional facility was premature and that the claim would be ripe only when the inmate's release from prison was relatively imminent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Imprint Technologies v. Commissioner of Economic Sec.


C0-95-293


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


535 N.W.2d 372; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 977



August 1, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari to Department of Economic Security. Dept. of Econ. Sec. No. 543 T 93.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On certiorari, relator business challenged a determination by respondent, the Department of Economic Security (Minnesota), that the business was the successor employer of another company for purposes of reemployment insurance benefits.


OVERVIEW: The sole director and officer of the business was the former president of and a director for the company, which had filed for bankruptcy. When his wife filed for reemployment insurance benefits with the Department, a field auditor conducted an audit of the business, who determined that there was substantial evidence that the business was the successor employer to the company and that the company's rating record was to be transferred to the business. Ultimately, that determination was affirmed. On appeal, the court ruled that substantial evidence, such as the facts that business used the company's name in the phone book used the corporate and trade names that the company had used, supported the finding that the business acquired the organization, trade, or business of the company, under Minn. Stat. § 268.06, subd. 22(a). The evidence, that the two operations were both engaged in printing and that the business hired many of the company's employees, supported the finding that the business continued the company's business. Finally, the court ruled that the Department's combination of investigative and decision-making functions in did not violate the business's due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Department's judgment.

Boyum v. Main Entree


C0-95-438


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


535 N.W.2d 389; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 987



August 1, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Stearns County; Hon. Richard J. Ahles, Judge. D.C. File No. C9-93-4228.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a ruling from the District Court, Stearns County (Minnesota), which entered a partial summary judgment in favor of respondent and held that appellant's negligence per se claim was barred by the 10-year statute of repose under Minn. Stat. § 541.051. Appellant had filed a common law negligence and a negligence per se action for injuries she had sustained when she tripped and fell on steps inside a building leased by respondent.


OVERVIEW: Appellant tripped and fell inside a building, which was used as a restaurant and bar, that was leased by respondent. Appellant then filed a common law negligence and a negligence per se action against respondent alleging negligence in respondent's failure to warn, to post signs, or to take remedial steps and in continuing to allow an unsafe condition to exist within the building. Appellant also alleged that the stairway was in violation of the Uniform Building Code. The trial court granted a partial summary judgment in favor of respondent in holding that the negligence per se claim was barred by the 10-year statute of repose pursuant to § 541.051, subd. 1 because the improvement to the property was completed more than 10 years prior to the accident. On appeal, the court held that: (1) § 541.051, subd. 1 was intended to protect possessors of real property from negligence per se claims under the Code when the violations originated more than 10 years prior to the injury; (2) the standard of care prescribed under the Code was not the standard of care required at common law; and (3) as such, appellant's negligence per se claim was barred by the statute of repose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's ruling, which had entered a partial summary judgment in favor of respondent and had held that appellant's negligence per se claim was time-barred.

In re Adlophson


C5-95-533


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 965



July 25, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at In re Civ. Commitment of Adolphson, 2013 Minn. App. Unpub. LEXIS 780 (Minn. Ct. App., Aug. 19, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Pope County; Hon. Marilyn J. Justman, Judge. District Court File No. PX9373.
In re Adolphson, 1994 Minn. LEXIS 610 (Minn., July 27, 1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his commitment to a state security hospital for an indeterminate period of time as a psychopathic personality as found by the District Court, Pope County (Minnesota).


OVERVIEW: Appellant engaged in numerous instances of criminal sexual contact with male juveniles. Eventually, he pled guilty to five counts of criminal misconduct in the third degree. After he was scheduled for release from prison, a petition for his commitment as a psychopathic personality was filed. A court-appointed examiner testified that appellant was a pedophile who displayed both control and impulsivity. Accordingly, the trial court committed him to a state security hospital for an indeterminate sentence. On review, appellant argued that there was insufficient evidence to show that he had an utter lack of power to control his sexual impulses or that he was likely to inflict serous physical or mental harm in the future. The court found that his actions showed that he had no will to stop sexually assaulting adolescent males and that he had no remorse. Rather, appellant was convinced that he had provided a service to the young men. Thus, the court found that the evidence showed appellant's complete lack of control. Further, the court noted that the victims suffered physically and psychologically from the incidents and that appellant was likely to be similarly dangerous in the future.

Sharp v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C3-95-143


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 928



July 18, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Harold Kalina, Judge. D.C. File No. 472355.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner motorist sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which sustained respondent Commissioner of Public Safety's revocation of her driver's license at an implied consent hearing.


OVERVIEW: The motorist refused a breath test following her having been stopped for driving under the influence of alcohol, which led the Commissioner to revoke her driver's license pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 169.121(2)(a). Following an implied consent hearing, the district court sustained the revocation and the motorist brought an appeal. The court affirmed on appeal. The court ruled that the police officer had probable cause because the motorist was sitting in the driver's seat with an open container of alcohol on the dashboard and that her breath smelled of alcohol. The court held that the motorist's contention that she had no intention of driving at the time was irrelevant because under the totality of the circumstances, the officer had probable cause to believe the motorist was in physical control of her car while under the influence. The court also ruled that because the motorist had not offered evidence to rebut the officer's testimony that her refusal to submit to the breath test was based on insufficient grounds, she had lost her right to prove that her refusal was based on reasonable grounds as an affirmative defense pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 169.123(6).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the Commissioner that sustained the revocation of the motorist's driver's license.

 

1051 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Azhakh v. Northwest Airlines


C7-95-131


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 845



June 27, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. John J. Sommerville, Judge. District Court File No. 92-11357.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), ruling in favor of respondent employer in the employee's action for employment discrimination. The employee rejected the employer's settlement offer made prior to trial, and the trial court granted the employer's motion for costs. The employer's motion for attorney fees and the employee's motion for a new trial were denied.


OVERVIEW: The employee was discharged from his position for alleged sexual harassment. The employee alleged employment discrimination and, after lengthy and expensive discovery, the employer made a settlement offer to the employee, which was rejected. Subsequently a judgment was rendered in favor of the employer. The trial court granted the employer motion, pursuant to Minn. R. Civ. P. 68, to recover its costs from the employee. The employee asserted that Minn. R. Civ. P. 68 violated the state and federal constitutions and that he was entitled to relief for "financial hardship" under Minn. Stat. § 363.14, subd. 3. The court affirmed, rejecting the argument that application of Minn. R. Civ. P. 68 to civil rights cases violated the employee's due process and equal protection rights. The court held that the application of the rule had no "chilling effect" on individuals who challenged unlawful employment discrimination practices but rather promoted the judicial goal of encouraging settlement of disputes. The court held that the statutory "financial hardship" exception was inapplicable because costs were not awarded under the statute. The award of costs to the employer was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1052 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Naegele Outdoor Adver. Co. v. City of Lakeville


C6-94-2197


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


532 N.W.2d 249; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 713



May 30, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Dakota County; Hon. Richard G. Spicer, Judge. District Court File No. C9-93-10129.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company sought review of a summary judgment entered by the District Court, Dakota County (Minnesota), in favor of respondent city in the company's action for damages, a declaration of its rights, and initiation of condemnation proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The company entered into lease agreements to erect billboards. A city ordinance required removal of nonconforming billboards as a condition of land development. When the lessors expressed an interest in developing their land, the company removed the signs. The company's later applications for replacement billboards were refused. The company brought an action against the city for damages, a declaration of its rights, and initiation of condemnation proceedings. The trial court granted the city's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed. Although property rights in outdoor advertising devices were entitled to the protections of the Takings Clause, the company was not entitled to compensation because the property owners terminated the company's leasehold interests. The leasehold interests were not altered by the ordinance. Assuming the sign ordinance effected a taking, the company had no compensable interest in the properties because it agreed in advance to termination of its leasehold rights upon development of the land. The company had no vested right to construct replacement billboards under a repealed ordinance because there was no vested right in zoning matters.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the city in the company's action for damages, a declaration of its rights, and initiation of condemnation proceedings.

 

1053 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Manning


C7-94-2242


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


532 N.W.2d 244; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 722



May 30, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Stephen D. Swanson, Judge. District Court File No. 94018525.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which convicted him of violating the sex offender registration law, Minn. Stat. § 243.166. Defendant claimed that applying the statute to a felon who was convicted before it took effect violated the ex post facto prohibitions of the United States and Minnesota Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was serving a sentence for criminal sexual conduct, the state legislature passed the sex offender registration law, Minn. Stat. § 243.166. After defendant's release, he was charged with violating the registration law because he moved without notifying his corrections agent. Defendant claimed that applying the law to a felon who was convicted before it took effect violated the ex post facto prohibitions of the United States and Minnesota Constitutions. Defendant moved for dismissal on that basis. The lower court denied the motion and found defendant guilty. Defendant appealed his conviction. On appeal, the court noted that the law applied to offenders released from prison after the effective date of the statute regardless of the date of the offense. The court considered whether the legislature intended the law to punish an offender for a past act, or whether the restriction of the individual was incidental to the regulation of a present situation. The court found that the effects of the law, though somewhat burdensome, were not punitive. The law did not violate federal and state constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

In re Jahi Pili Sadiki


C7-95-419


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 692



May 23, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. James F. Finley, Civil Commitment Referee, Judge. District Court File No. P9911977.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged a decision of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which upheld its earlier commitment of the patient to respondent county as a psychopathic personality under Minn. Stat. § 526.09 (1992) and Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18a (1994) after a remand.


OVERVIEW: The trial court committed the patient as a psychopathic personality. The court remanded the case to the trial court after the state supreme court remanded the patient's first appeal. The record showed that (1) the patient committed at least five rapes during the three years he was not confined, (2) his victims were vulnerable females, including one 12-year-old girl, (3) he choked several of his victims, hit one victim's head against a garage door, and threatened to kill the victims during the sexual assaults, (4) despite treatment, he did not understand his propensity towards violence and rape, and (5) while incarcerated, he exhibited emotional instability through his inability to comply with the structure of the treatment facility and his recent marital problems. Experts testified that the patient could not control his sexual impulses or his anger and that he responded by raping unknown females. The trial court upheld its earlier decision. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the determination under Minn. Stat. § 526.09 and Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 18a that the patient was likely to commit crimes in the future was amply supported by clear and convincing evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which had committed the patient to the county as a psychopathic personality.

State v. Iverson


CX-94-1733


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 666



May 16, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Allen Oleisky, Judge. District Court File No. 93109498.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which convicted him of aiding and abetting aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aiding and abetting aggravated robbery. On appeal, defendant contended that (1) the trial court erred by ruling that the state could use prior felony convictions to impeach him; (2) the prosecution's introduction of a witness's hearsay statements constituted prosecutorial misconduct; (3) the career offender statute was void for vagueness; and (4) the trial court erred when it sentenced him under the "career offender" statute. The court ruled that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by admitting evidence of defendant's prior convictions because the prior convictions all occurred within the previous seven years. The court also ruled that the prosecution's admission of a witness' hearsay statements did not constitute prosecutorial misconduct because the decision whether to admit or exclude evidence rested with the trial court, and the evidence was admissible under the "catch-all" exception to the hearsay rule, Minn. R. Evid. 803(24). The court held that the career offender statute, including its definition of a "career offender," was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction and sentence.

 

1056 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Hanson v. City of St. Cloud


C3-94-1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 619



May 9, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Stearns County; Hon. Thomas M. Stringer, Judge. D. C. File No. C7-90-3306.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer challenged an order of the District Court, Stearns County (Minnesota), which entered a judgment for respondent City of St. Cloud (Minnesota) in the officer's action in which he sought to set aside an administrative order that upheld the city's termination of his employment. The court also denied the officer's motion to expunge his vacated criminal convictions from the official records.


OVERVIEW: The officer alleged that his termination violated the Equal Protection Clause and the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment in the Eighth Amendment because other officers that were found guilty of unbecoming conduct were not terminated. The court affirmed the district court's judgment, concluding that substantial evidence supported the civil service board's approval of the termination and that the officer received all of the due process to which he was entitled. The court also reasoned that the officer's unbecoming conduct provided a rational basis for his termination. The court further held that the officer could not have prevailed under Minn. R. Civ. P. 60.02(e) or (f) because he did not show that a present challenge to the board's determination would have had merit and that vacating the criminal convictions did not entitle him to relief due to the ample evidence that the board's decision was not based on those convictions. The court also found that not adhering to the specificity requirements that precedent established as to the expungement of the criminal records justified not granting that relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1057 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wendland


C3-95-272, C5-95-273


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 576



April 19, 1995, Decided  
April 25, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Brown County; Hon. Terri Stoneburner, Judge. District Court File Nos. K3-94-214, K5-94-215.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the District Court, Brown County (Minnesota), defendant pled guilty to the sale of marijuana, a fifth degree controlled substance crime, and to sale of 10 or more dosage units of LSD, a third degree controlled substance crime. He appealed a $ 50,000 fine on the LSD conviction and $ 250 surcharge on the marijuana conviction and argued that the surcharge statute, Minn. Stat. § 609.101, subd. 1(b), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: On the marijuana charge, the district court also stayed imposition of the sentence, placed defendant on probation for five years, ordered him to serve 45 days in the county jail, fined him $ 750, and assessed a $ 25 felony criminal surcharge. On the LSD charge, the district court also stayed the presumptive 21-month prison sentence and ordered defendant to spend six months in the county jail, to be on probation for 20 years. Also on the LSD charge the district court waived the mandatory surcharge on the $ 50,000 fine but imposed a $ 25 felony criminal surcharge. On appeal, the court pointed out that the minimum fine for conviction of a third degree controlled substance crime was $ 50,000. The court noted that Minn. Stat. § 609.101, subd. 5 implied some discretion as to reduction of a fine, but the court held that the district court did not abuse its discretion by not doing so in defendant's case. The State conceded that the $ 250 surcharge, 33 1/3 percent of the fine, was error, and the court modified the surcharge to $ 150, the 20 percent permissible. Finally, the court held that defendant had no standing to challenge the constitutionality of § 609.101, subd. 1(b).


OUTCOME: The court modified by reducing the surcharge and otherwise affirmed.

 

1058 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Lundman v. McKown


C1-94-891, C3-94-892, C5-94-893, C7-94-894, C9-94-895, C0-94-896, C2-94-897


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


530 N.W.2d 807; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 462



April 4, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Sean J. Rice, Judge. Dist. Ct. File 918197.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Christian Scientists sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which imposed liability on them and denied their posttrial motions in a wrongful death action brought by appellee trustee for the next of kin.


OVERVIEW: The trustee brought a wrongful death action against various Christian Scientists for the death of his son. The boy displayed various symptoms related to juvenile-onset diabetes which could have been treated even up to within two hours of his death. The Christian Scientists who cared for him failed to seek medical attention and he died. The district court found for the trustee and an appeal followed. The court affirmed as to some parties and reversed as to others. The court found that punitive damages should not have been awarded against defendant church and held it was unconstitutional to have imposed punitive damages on a church to force it to abandon teaching its central tenet. The court upheld the award of compensatory damages because the state's interest in protecting children outweighed the free exercise of religion. The court found those individuals who were directly involved and had a duty of care for the boy could be held liable but those who were not directly involved had no duty of care and were not liable.


OUTCOME: The court found the punitive damages award was unconstitutional, upheld the awards against those individuals who had a duty of care, and vacated the awards against those individuals who had no duty of care.

 

1059 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stewart


C7-94-1687


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


529 N.W.2d 493; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 469



April 4, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. John M. Stanoch, Judge. District Court File No. 93112485.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his misdemeanor conviction from the District Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota) for installing, connecting, repairing, altering, or adding to a hospital fire sprinkler system without a license in violation of Minneapolis, Minn., Ordinance §§ 227.3127 and 227.3128.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was adjudicated guilty of the misdemeanor offense of installing, connecting, repairing, altering, or adding to a hospital sprinkler system without a license in violation of a municipal ordinance. The court reversed defendant's misdemeanor conviction and held that defendant's on-site preparations were not prohibited by the ordinance. The court found that the terms of the ordinance were not defined and did not include the on-site preparation work done by defendant. As such, the court construed the ordinance in favor of lenity and concluded that defendant's work preparation duties were not covered under the ordinance. Also, the court ruled that defendant's activities were not covered by the ordinance merely because they were essential to the installation of the sprinkler system. The court held that the application of the ordinance by the municipality only to on-site work while exempting identical work off-site unreasonably treated similarly situated persons differently and violated due process and equal protection rights. The municipality's interpretation of the ordinance was not rationally related to protecting the public interest in maintaining fire protection systems.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's misdemeanor conviction for installing, connecting, repairing, altering, or adding to a hospital fire sprinkler system without a license in violation of a municipal ordinance.

 

1060 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Klosterboer


C9-94-1495


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


529 N.W.2d 705; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 405



March 28, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Chippewa County; Hon. Allan D. Buchanan, Judge. District Court File No. K6-93-161.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Chippewa County (Minnesota), which convicted him of two counts of theft, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.52, subds. 2(1), (3)(b), and (5) (1992).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his theft conviction, arguing that venue was improper, that the prosecutor engaged in misconduct, and that the trial court made various erroneous evidentiary rulings. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court found that defendant was properly tried in the county in which the thefts occurred, noting that under Minn. Stat. § 627.01, subds. 1 and 2 venue was properly had in any county in which an element of the crime was committed. The court rejected defendant's contention that the prosecutor committed prejudicial misconduct by calling defendant's wife as a witness, noting that defendant's assertion of marital privilege was not discussed in front of the jury, that the State did not attempt to draw any inference from the wife's failure to testify, and the trial court had given an appropriate cautionary instruction. The court found that any error in the trial court's evidentiary rulings was harmless, noting that police testimony concerning statements made by the wife was consistent with defendant's trial testimony and that testimony concerning statements made by defendant before he was Mirandized had not contradicted his trial testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1061 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Minnegasco v. Minnesota PUC


C5-94-1820, C7-94-1821


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


529 N.W.2d 413; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 407



March 28, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari to Minnesota Public Utilities Commission. Docket No. G-008/C-91-942.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator utility company sought review by writ of certiorari to the court from respondent Minnesota Public Utilities Commission, which ordered that the company's goodwill be valued to the extent it benefitted the company's unregulated operations, and that such value be imputed as revenue in subsequent rate-setting cases. Respondent, a consumer alliance, had filed a complaint with the Commission raising the issue.


OVERVIEW: The Commission previously ordered the company to adopt the cost allocation principles of the Federal Communications Commission (FCC). Later, upon the alliance's complaint that the company failed to properly implement that order, the Commission ordered the instant contested case proceeding on allocation issues. The alliance alleged, inter alia, that the company used the goodwill of its regulated utility operations to subsidize its unregulated appliance sales business. The Commission ruled that such goodwill should be treated as an asset. Thus, the Commission imputed as revenue to the utility the value of its goodwill in the unregulated market for purposes of setting rates. The court agreed and affirmed the Commission's order, as it was supported by substantial evidence. Record evidence showed that the goodwill of the regulated utility had value in the competitive market. The Commission had the statutory authority for rate-making purposes to impute as revenue to a utility's regulated operations the value of its goodwill as to its unregulated operations, where such imputation was necessary to avoid a subsidy to the company. Nor did the order amount to an unconstitutional taking.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Commission.

 

1062 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Trust Created by Hill ex rel. Schroll


C0-94-1773


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 357



March 14, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. M. Michael Monahan, Judge. District Court File C047260959.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trust beneficiaries sought review from a judgment of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which granted a motion for summary judgment in favor of respondents, a trustee and its agents, in the beneficiaries' malpractice claims, based on collateral estoppel. The beneficiaries had brought an action in equity, in which judgment was also granted to respondents.


OVERVIEW: As the basis for their malpractice claim against the trustee's agent, the beneficiaries asserted that the agent, an attorney, had conflicts of interest between the beneficiaries and the trustee during the years 1978-1984 and that the agent failed to inform the beneficiaries of the conflict. The agent had written the trust instrument in 1917 and had represented the trustee since then. The trustee's agent had represented the beneficiaries in prior litigation. Because there was not a substantial relevant relationship or overlap between the subject matters of the representation of two clients, there could be no liability for legal malpractice for failing to inform one client about the representation of the other client. Because the previous litigation was not substantially related to the issues raised in the trust litigation, the trustee's agent had no duty to inform the beneficiaries of his representation of the trustee. Therefore, the court held that the beneficiaries failed to present a viable claim for legal malpractice against the trustee's agent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Dakota County (Minnesota) that denied his motion for postconviction relief, following his guilty plea to one count each of first- and second-degree criminal sexual conduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that it was an abuse of discretion to revoke his probation, that the revocation was unconstitutional, and that he was denied effective assistance of counsel at the revocation hearing. In remanding the decision, the court found that the postconviction court failed to make any findings of fact or conclusions of law. Finally, defendant's motion for sanctions was denied because there was no evidence of bad faith in the State's motion to correct the record.

Northland Racquetball v. Bemidji State Univ.


CX-94-1621


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 272



February 28, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Beltrami County; Hon. Paul E. Rasmussen, Judge. District Court File No. CX-93-309.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a fitness club and its principals, sought review of a decision of the District Court, Beltrami County (Minnesota), which granted respondent state university's motion for summary judgment on appellants' claims that the university's sale of memberships to its recreational center forced appellants to close their business, and was a tortious interference with their business relations and an unconstitutional taking of their property.


OVERVIEW: The university decided to make its new recreational center available to the public for a modest fee because it was built with taxpayer dollars and community funding. Appellants alleged that in anticipation of the opening, non-student members did not join their club, and they were forced to close. In affirming the decision, the court held thatappellants were precluded from any relief because they failed to establish, beyond mere conjecture and speculation, that the university's sale of memberships to the public caused them to go out of business. Further, the sales were not unconstitutional because the university's action of providing public access to the center served the public purpose of promoting public health. The court also found that the university did not exceed its authority by engaging in a private enterprise because the public access to the center was limited and the modest fee generated minimal income. There was no evidence that the university's objective was to interfere with appellants' business and thus, the claim of tortious interference failed. Finally, because appellants did not bring a mandamus action, their taking claim was not properly before the district court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, which granted summary judgment to the university.

State v. Koenig


C0-94-901


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 231



February 14, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Todd County; Hon. Thomas A. Godzala, Judge. District Court #K293606.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the District Court, Todd County (Minnesota) convicting defendant of issuing a worthless check.


OVERVIEW: The State issued the complaint on July 19, 1993. Defendant appeared on August 21 and demanded a speedy trial. On September 24, 1993, following a dismissal, the State filed its second complaint. Defendant first appeared on October 18, filed a written demand for a speedy trial, and the trial court appointed a public defender. At the November 22 omnibus hearing, defendant's second public defender requested a continuance and agreed to modify defendant's demand for a speedy trial. Defendant next appeared on December 13, this time pro se. The trial began on January 4, 1994. Defendant represented himself, with standby counsel present in the courtroom. On appeal, defendant argued that his waiver of counsel was not knowing and voluntary, and that he did not receive a speedy trial. The court held that: (1) the trial court had implicitly found defendant's waiver valid in granting his request for self-representation; (2) defendant's conversations with public defenders helped show that he was aware of the consequences of proceeding pro se; and (3) defendant was tried within 60 days after his prospective reassertion of his speedy trial demand as required by Minn. R. Crim. P. 11.10.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction from the trial court.

City of Minneapolis v. Gradishar


C5-94-1266


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 207



February 7, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Ann Montgomery, Judge. Dist. Ct. # MC-93-012103.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business owner challenged a judgment from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), denying his application to expand his business to include nude dancers. The court found that respondent city did not violate Minneapolis, Minn., Ordinance 267.1155.


OVERVIEW: The business owner sought to expand his business to include nude dancers. The city did not respond to the business owner's request until some 71 days after receipt of the application. The business owner alleged that the city violated ordinance 267.1155 by failing to respond within 60 days. According to the business owner, the failure to respond meant that the application was granted by operation of law. The city sought an injunction, which was granted by the trial court. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the city's delayed decision on the business owner's application for a license did not violate the ordinance or invalidate the decision. The ordinance's language requiring that the decision be rendered within 60 days was discretionary, not mandatory. Moreover, the court noted that the business owner continued to operate its nude dancing business and did not suffer any monetary damages. Lastly, the court noted that the business owner's nude dancing enterprise was a nonconforming use. The 1992 amendment to the Minneapolis City Ordinance prohibited two or more regulated uses on the same block. Thus, the business owner could not expand.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1067 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Ascher v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C9-94-1061


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


527 N.W.2d 122; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 113



January 31, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Dakota County; Hon. Leslie M. Metzen, Judge. District Court File No. C89315712.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public safety commissioner sought review of the judgment of the District Court, Dakota County (Minnesota), which rescinded the commissioner's cancellation of appellee driver's conditional license after the driver refused a test at a sobriety checkpoint which was later determined to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The driver's license was conditioned upon his abstinence from alcohol. When he refused a test at a sobriety checkpoint, the commissioner cancelled the driver's license. The court later determined that the checkpoint was unconstitutional and rescinded the revocation. The driver then sought reinstatement of his license, but the commissioner again cancelled the license because of the driver's "continuing alcohol involvement." The trial court rescinded the cancellation on the ground that evidence obtained at an illegal checkpoint should have been excluded. The court held that: (1) res judicata did not bar the driver's action because the issues regarding the license cancellation were not before the trial court in the prior hearing, a challenge to the state's implied consent rules; (2) the exclusionary rule did not apply to evidence obtained at the checkpoint because the proceeding at bar arose out of his violation of a condition of his license and did not relate to the implied consent rules; (3) the driver, by virtue of his conditional license, was on constructive notice of the reason for the cancellation; and (4) the clean hands doctrine did not bar the commissioner's action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court reinstating the driver's license.

Estate of Benson by Benson v. Minnesota Bd. of Medical Practice


C1-94-1765


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


526 N.W.2d 634; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 145; 23 Media L. Rep. 1475



January 31, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Joanne M. Smith, Judge. District Court File No. C0-93-11804.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant personal representative (representative) sought review of the decision of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which granted judgment to respondents, Minnesota Board of Medical Practice (Board), and Minnesota Department of Health (Department), holding the action was barred by the survival statute, Minn. Stat. § 573.01 (1992).


OVERVIEW: The decedent was a doctor who was HIV-positive. The Department conducted an epidemiological investigation of the decedent's practice. The Department reported the investigation's methodology, procedures, and conclusions in two articles published while the decedent was still alive. The representative claimed the articles violated the decedent's statutory privacy rights, and caused the decedent to suffer emotional and physical devastation, and professional humiliation and ostracism. The representative sued the Board and the Department for publishing articles. The trial court found that the claims were barred by the survival statute. The court found that the alleged violations were personal to the decedent in that the articles were published while he was still alive. The court found that the alleged violations were not violations of the estate's property interests under the survival statute. The court held that the representative's claim for invasion of the decedent's statutory privacy interests was an action for personal injury which did not survive the decedent's death. The court found that the trial court properly granted summary judgment in favor of the Department and Board.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

State v. Holmberg


C3-94-696


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


527 N.W.2d 100; 1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 89



January 24, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; District Court File No. 93083856. Hon. Catherine L. Anderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the District Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota), which convicted him for operating a disorderly house, under Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 385.170(b)(1) (1991).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction for operating a disorderly house, a misdemeanor ordinance violation. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that defendant did not show that the ordinance was directed at expressive conduct. He also did not show that the lack of a knowledge requirement was relevant to any First Amendment claim. The ordinance did not penalize defendant for the people he associated with, but for the activities conducted on his premises. The court found that the trial court did not err in failing to suppress evidence seized under the search warrants, nor in declining to dismiss the complaint for lack of probable cause.


OUTCOME: The order of the lower court convicting defendant for operating a disorderly house was affirmed.

Happel v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C7-93-1579


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 67



January 17, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Anoka County; Hon. Donald J. Venne, Judge. D. C. File No. C4-93-1342.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Anoka County (Minnesota) that sustained the order of respondent, the Commissioner of Public Safety, that revoked the driver's license, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 169.123, subd. 4.


OVERVIEW: The driver was arrested for driving while under the influence of alcohol, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 169.121, subd. 1(a), (d) (1992). The arresting officer read the driver the implied consent advisory form and offered him a breath test. The driver chose a blood test. The test was conducted and revealed an alcohol concentration above the legal limit. The Commissioner subsequently revoked the driver's license for a period of 90 days. The trial court sustained the revocation. On further appeal, the court affirmed. Although the blood test was not drawn using only items taken from the approved BCA blood kit, there was ample evidence to support a finding by the district court that the test was valid. The technician who took the driver's blood testified that she always followed a specific procedure in drawing blood for legal blood alcohol testing and that by this procedure she used only the items found in the BCA kit. The court held that the trial court did not clearly err in its implicit finding that the driver's blood test was valid and reliable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State by Humphrey v. Casino Mktg. Group


C9-94-1268


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1995 Minn. App. LEXIS 24



January 3, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Mary Louise Klas, Judge. District Court File No. C6-90-12442.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by respondent attorney general, appellant telemarketer challenged a judgment of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota). He contended that the district court abused its discretion in denying his motion to amend his answer and counterclaim to attack the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 325E.26- .31 (1992) after he was enjoined from using his telemarketing system.


OVERVIEW: The telemarketer used an automatic dialing-announcing device to make thousands of phone calls soliciting business for defendant credit card company. Due to numerous complaints about the devise, the attorney general brought this action against the telemarketer and the companies for which he worked. The district court issued an injunction and rejected the telemarketer's constitutional challenge to Minn. Stat. § 325E.26- .31 (1992). The appellate courts affirmed the injunction. The telemarketer then moved to amend his answer and counterclaim to add a new basis for constitutional attack in light of two recent United States Supreme Court decisions. The court denied the motion and, pursuant to the parties' agreement, entered final judgment and a permanent injunction against the telemarketer. On review, the court found that because there were no issues to be litigated, the district court properly determined that the Minnesota Supreme Court's decision in the case controlled. The court also found that Minn. R. Civ. P. 15, the trial court could deny a motion to amend if any substantial delay would result and if the amendment would accomplish nothing.


OUTCOME: The judgment in against the telemarketer was affirmed.

 

1072 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


LeBlanc v. Morrison County


C8-94-1343


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 1308



December 27, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Morrison County; Hon. Skipper J. Pearson, Judge. Dist. Ct. # C9-93-426.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant deputy sheriff challenged an order from the District Court for Morrison County (Minnesota), which granted respondent county's summary judgment motion in the deputy's action claiming that the county violated his constitutional rights by refusing his request under Minn. Stat. § 465.76 (1992) for reimbursement of legal fees incurred in defense of careless driving charges brought against him.


OVERVIEW: The deputy sheriff's car collided with an unlit tractor, killing the driver of the tractor. The deputy was charged with careless driving and was acquitted. He requested the county to reimburse his legal fees under § 465.76, and the county refused. He filed an action against the county, the trial court entered summary judgment in favor of the county, and on appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction. The deputy's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims were not barred by operation of Minnesota's procedural rule requiring plaintiffs challenging administrative decisions to proceed by petition for writ of certiorari because the 60-day filing requirement in Minn. Stat. § 606.01 was insufficient to allow civil rights victims to recognize that they had a claim. The court held that the deputy was not deprived of a constitutional right because the county had the discretion to grant or refuse reimbursement under Minn. Stat. § 465.76. Equal protection did not demand that the deputy receive reimbursement simply because other municipal employees were reimbursed under their municipalities' discretionary powers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's entry of summary judgment in favor of the county.

Rieck v. State


C6-94-1230


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 1317



December 27, 1994, Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an inmate, filed a post-conviction petition and requested resentencing under Minn. Stat. § 590.01, subd. 3 (1992). The District Court of Crow Wing County (Minnesota) denied the inmate's resentencing request. The inmate filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: The inmate threatened a young girl with a knife, kidnapped her, and sexually penetrated her at knife point. Subsequently, the inmate entered a plea of guilty to kidnapping, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.25, subd. 1 (1976), and criminal sexual conduct in the third degree, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.344(b) (1976). Defendant received an indeterminate sentence of 3-20 years for the kidnapping conviction and a concurrent 0-10 years for the criminal sexual conduct conviction. After the enactment of Minn. Stat. § 590.01, subd. 3 (1992), the inmate filed a post-conviction petition and requested resentencing. The trial court denied the request without permitting a hearing. On appeal, the supreme court reversed and remanded for a hearing on the postconviction petition. On remand, the trial court again denied the inmate's resentencing request. On appeal, the inmate challenged the constitutionality of § 590.01, subd. 3. In affirming the trial court's judgment, the court held that the statute was sufficiently precise. Furthermore, the court concluded that the statute provided sufficient guidelines to discourage arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement.

Humenansky v. Minn. Bd. of Medical Examiners


C5-94-1090


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


525 N.W.2d 559; 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 1271



December 20, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Filed January 19, 1995. As Corrected.
Review denied by Humenansky v. Minnesota Bd. of Medical Examiners, 1995 Minn. LEXIS 116 (Minn., Feb. 14, 1995)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Kenneth J. Fitzpatrick, Judge. District Court File No. C5-94-2638.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a duly licensed doctor, appealed a decision from the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which denied her request for an injunction to prevent defendants, the Minnesota Board of Medical Examiners and others, from requiring her to submit to a mental examination under Minn. Stat. § 147.091(6)(a) (1992).


OVERVIEW: In response to complaints about the doctor, a committee of the Board found probable cause to believe that the doctor could not practice medicine with the requisite skill to assure her patients' safety and it ordered the doctor to submit to a mental and physical examination. The doctor argued that the law requiring such examination was constitutionally defective. The court found that as a condition of licensure, the doctor gave her consent to a board-directed examination. In order to prevail on her request for an injunction, the doctor had to show she would suffer irreparable harm and that she was likely to succeed on the merits. The court found neither. The circumstances under which the examination was to take place did not cause an irreparable loss of privacy. The statute was constitutionally valid, because it was within the police power of the state to protect the health of its citizens. Because the Board's probable cause determination was subject to review both before and after any disciplinary action and because the physician was entitled to a hearing, the statute did not deny the doctor due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision denying an injunction to the doctor and permitting the Board to order her to submit to the required examination.

 

1075 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Welfare of L.D.B.


C9-94-847


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 1244



December 13, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Olmsted County; Hon. John S. Gowan, Judge. District Court File No. J9-94-50198.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of the judgment of the District Court, Olmsted County (Minnesota), which adjudicated the juvenile a delinquent for violation of Minn. Stat. § 152.024, subd. 2(2) -- possession with intent to sell cocaine.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was adjudicated a delinquent for possession with intent to sell cocaine, a violation of Minn. Stat. § 152.024, subd. 2(2). The court affirmed the juvenile's adjudication as a delinquent. The search warrant was not unconstitutionally invalid. Key details of two informants' allegations were corroborated by each other. The interlocking tips from different informants enhanced the informants' credibility. Moreover, the police corroborated other details provided by the informants. Thus, the affidavit contained sufficient information, corroborated by the police and other information, to establish the informants' reliability. Nor was the officer's search of the juvenile unconstitutional. Where police had a valid search warrant to search one party and they reasonably mistook a second party for the first, the search of the second was valid. The officer believed only two males lived in the residence. The officer had met one and knew the person in the bedroom he entered was not him. The officer did not discover that the juvenile was not the suspect until after he conducted the search. The officer made a reasonable mistake in thinking that the juvenile was the suspect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment, which adjudicated the juvenile a delinquent.

 

1076 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burns


C9-94-332


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


524 N.W.2d 516; 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 1206



December 6, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Roberta K. Levy, Judge. District Court File No. 93-033147.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which convicted him of one count of criminal sexual conduct in the first degree in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.342, subd. 1(h)(iii) (1992) and sentenced him to 43 months in prison. On appeal, defendant contended that his prosecution was barred by the prohibition of ex post facto laws of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1 and Minn. Const. art. I, § 11.


OVERVIEW: In 1993, the State charged defendant with criminal sexual abuse of his son and stepson occurring between 1982 and 1986. At the time the criminal conduct occurred, the limitations period was seven years under Minn. Stat. § 628.26(c) (1982). However, the limitations period was twice amended: first so that where the victim was under age 18 the limitations period expired two years after the offense was first reported to authorities, Minn. Stat. § 628.26(c) (1990), and second, to apply retroactively to crimes for which the limitations period had not expired by August 1, 1991, by 1991 Minn. Laws ch. 232, §§ 3-4. The court rejected defendant's contention that the amendments deprived him of a defense which would have been available to him under the 1982 version of the statute of limitations, holding that a statute of limitations was a defense or protection from prosecution only after the limitations period had elapsed. Moreover, no ex post facto violation occurred because the change effected was merely procedural and did not increase the punishment, change the elements of the offense, or change the ultimate facts necessary to establish guilt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1077 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wilson


C8-94-208


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


524 N.W.2d 271; 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 1185



November 29, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Isanti County; Hon. James Dehn, Judge. District Court File No. KO-92-886.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court, Isanti County (Minnesota), which convicted him of incest under Minn. Stat. § 609.365 (1992). Defendant was accused of engaging in sexual relations with his adult niece. He argued that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and that his actions did not constitute incest within the meaning of the statute. Defendant also claimed his sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had engaged in sexual intercourse with the daughter of his half sister. He was aware of the family relationship at the time. He and the victim's mother had the same mother. The trial court sentenced defendant to 26 months in prison, stayed, with probation for 10 years under conditions including 180 days in jail (with work release or sentence to serve) and restitution. On review, the court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. As to the sentencing issue, the court held that because incest was not assigned a severity level in the sentencing guidelines and defendant had been acquitted of the criminal sexual conduct charges, the judge could exercise his discretion by assigning an appropriate severity level. The court found that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion by assigning a severity level of six to the felony incest conviction, and the sentence was within the presumptive range for level six crimes. The trial court supported its sentence with its statements that defendant had used very poor judgment in his relations with his niece and in his past relations as evidenced by similar crime evidence that had been admitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for incest and the sentence that the trial court imposed on him.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court, Blue Earth County (Minnesota), which committed him to the Minnesota Security Hospital for an indeterminate period as a psychopathic personality under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 526.09 (1992).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with first-degree and second-degree criminal sexual conduct. The evidence showed that defendant's behavior was impulsive and without volitional control, he refused treatment, he denied his misconduct, and it was likely that he would cause harm in the future.

Alton v. Wabedo Township


C1-94-695


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


524 N.W.2d 278; 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 1189



November 18, 1994, Decided  
November 29, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Cass County; Hon. Michael J. Haas, Judge. District Court File No. C0-92-816.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township sought review of the decision from the District Court, Cass County (Minnesota), which granted respondent landowner summary judgment and issued a permanent injunction preventing the township from clearing brush and trees adjacent to the township road easement. The district court found that the method for recording town roads in Minn. Stat. § 164.35, subd. 4 (1992) was unconstitutional since it was a taking without compensation.


OVERVIEW: The landowner brought the action to prevent the township from clearing brush and trees for eight feet back from the surface of a road adjacent to his property. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that Minn. Stat. § 164.35, subd. 4, did not provide a mechanism for compensation, and therefore to give effect to § 164.35, subd. 4 would have resulted in an uncompensated, and therefore unconstitutional, taking of private property. The court reasoned that although the township had followed all of the procedural requirements of § 164.35, subd. 4, pursuant to Minn. Const. art. I, § 13, private property could not be taken for public use without just compensation therefor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision which granted the landowner summary judgment and issued a permanent injunction preventing the township from clearing brush and trees adjacent to the township road easement.

State v. Johnson


C0-94-297


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 1128



November 15, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Dolores Orey, Judge. District Court File No. 93-004894



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the judgment of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which convicted him of aggravated robbery, Minn. Stat. § 609.245 (1992) and second degree assault, Minn. Stat. § 609.222 (1992).


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of aggravated robbery, a violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.245 (1992), and second degree assault, Minn. Stat. § 609.222 (1992). The court affirmed the inmate's convictions. The inmate was not entitled to a new trial although no African-Americans were among the venire from which the jury was drawn, as under both U.S. Const. amend. VI and Minn. Const. art. I, § 6, evidence that a distinctive group was not represented in a venire was, by itself, insufficient to establish a constitutional violation. Nor was the pretrial identification process and identification testimony unconstitutional and improperly admitted. The one-person show-up conducted soon after the crime did not create a substantial likelihood of misidentification. All four witnesses closely observed the inmate during the crime or soon thereafter, their descriptions of the him were substantially similar, and they identified the inmate with certainty. Although the jury heard a prejudicial, unsolicited statement from an interpreter during a witness' identification, the inmate's due process rights were not violated; the trial court took remedial measures and four other witnesses also identified the inmate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the inmate's convictions for aggravated robbery and second degree assault.

In re Patterson


C0-94-1367


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 1094

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota) committed appellant inmate as a psychopathic personality. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted several times of violently raping and robbing women. The associate superintendent of the correctional facility where the inmate was housed, following yet another violent rape and robbery, petitioned for the inmate's commitment as a psychopathic personality. At the commitment hearing, the trial court heard testimony from some of the inmate's victims, three doctors, and others and found that the inmate had a psychopathic personality. The court determined that the doctor's invocation of the Fifth Amendment precluded the State from meaningful cross-examination. Thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in striking the testimony.

Bilal v. Northwest Airlines


C4-94-416


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 1052



November 1, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed January 20, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Dolores Orey, Judge. District Court File MC9122738



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and judgment modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer airline (employer) challenged the judgment of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which ordered damages against the employer for discriminating against respondents, employee and his wife, based on their religion in violation of the Minnesota Human Rights Act, as set forth at Minn. Stat. § 363.03(3)(a)(1), and which ordered damages for the employee's and his wife's mental anguish.


OVERVIEW: While using an employee travel pass, the wife was pulled aside on the jetway by a customer service representative (representative) of the employer, told that her traditional Muslim clothing was inappropriate according to the employee travel pass dress code, and advised that she should dress as if she were going to church. The court held that the employee and his wife proved discrimination under § 363.03(3)(a)(1) based on the entire sequence of events. The court held that (1) the representative perceived the wife's religious clothing as inappropriate and this, combined with the statement that she should dress as if going to church, indicated inferentially that religion played at least some role in the representative's decision to question the wife, (2) the representative's remark as to "church" was offensive to one of the Islamic faith, and (3) the wife's technical violation of the dress code, namely her footwear, was not called to her attention before she was escorted from the jetway. The court held that damages were properly awarded to the wife for mental anguish but that the employee could not recover such damages because he was not present during the discriminatory incident.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court in part, reversed it in part, and modified the judgment.
