Minnesota Council of Dog Clubs v. City of Minneapolis


C3-94-939


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 1076



November 1, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Beryl A. Nord, Judge. District Court File No. 9318522



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dog owners organizations brought a declaratory judgment action that challenged the constitutionality of the Minnesota Cruelty to Animals Act, Minn. Stat. §§ 343.20-343.37 (1992 & Supp. 1993). On the motion of respondent City of Minneapolis, the District Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota) dismissed the complaint for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and failure to state a claim. The organizations prosecuted an appeal.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court noted that a plaintiff had to possess, at a minimum, a bona fide legal interest that had been, or was about to be, affected in a prejudicial manner to obtain declaratory judgment relief. The trial court found that the organizations failed to show that they or any of their members were the subject of an enforcement action under the Cruelty to Animals Act, or that they were immediately threatened by such an action. The trial court dismissed the action for lack of concrete, legally cognizable interests directly threatened by the Cruelty to Animals Act. The court disagreed. Minn. Stat. § 343.21, subd. 2 (1992) of the Cruelty to Animals Act provided that no person could deprive any animal over which the person had charge or control of necessary food, water, or shelter. The provision subjected the organizations and their members to an affirmative duty. The Declaratory Judgments Act, Minn. Stat. § 555.01-555.16 (1992) was remedial in nature and liberal construction applied to afford relief from uncertainty and insecurity. The case was one where a declaratory judgment action was singularly appropriate for resolution of the dispute before commission of wrongs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the organizations' action and directed the trial court to reinstate the organizations' complaint.

 

1084 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Multiple Miscellaneous Items Numbered 1-424


C6-94-966


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


523 N.W.2d 238; 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 1026



October 25, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Anoka County; Hon. Dan Kammeyer, Judge. District Court File No. C7-89-14050



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the property claimant pleaded guilty to receiving and concealing stolen property, appellant county brought a forfeiture action against respondent property under Minn. Stat. § 609.5312 (1988). The District Court, Anoka County (Minnesota) denied forfeiture. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: After about 75 items found in the claimant's possession were returned to their owners, the county commenced forfeiture proceedings against another 350 items, which included drugs, illegal weapons, and stolen goods. Noting that § 609.5312 provided that all contraband property was subject to forfeiture, the court applied the rules of construction for contraband statutes contained in Minn. Stat. § 609.531, subd. 1a (1988) and concluded that "contraband" was intended by the legislature to include property that was illegal for a claimant to possess. Moreover, the court stated, it was not necessary that a claimant know the property was stolen in order for it to be subject to forfeiture. Therefore, the court concluded, because neither party had contested the trial court's finding that the property was stolen, it was illegal for the claimant to possess it, and the property was thus subject to forfeiture. The court declined to rule on the issue of the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 609.5312 because the question had not been raised in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision.

In re McGaughey


C6-94-952


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 969



October 4, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed November 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Marilyn J. Justman, Judge. Dist. Ct. # MI05797



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant patient appealed an order from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), committing him as mentally ill, contending that he did not meet the standard for dangerousness contained in Minn. Stat. § 253B.02, subd. 13(b) (1992), and that the trial court erred in rejecting less restrictive alternatives of placement.


OVERVIEW: The hospital filed a petition to commit a patient as mentally ill after he was diagnosed with schizophrenia. Testimony at trial showed that he was inappropriate with others in violating personal boundaries and had inappropriate sexual behavior towards women. The treatment team recommended commitment while the patient's brother protested, and one doctor favored short-term treatment. The trial court committed the patient as mentally ill. The patient appealed. The court held that a nursing home had refused to accept the patient until his behavior was under control, the patient was unable to care for his hygiene and clothing, and he became confused about his medication. Thus, the court held that the trial court decision was not clearly erroneous. The court held that Minn. Stat. § 253B.02 was applied in a constitutional manner because the patient met the standard for dangerousness. The record supported the trial court's decision, which was not clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commitment.

 

1087 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wanli


C1-94-342


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 939



September 27, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Renville County; Hon. John J. Weyrens, Judge. Dist. Ct. # K3-93-77



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the District Court, Renville County (Minnesota), which convicted him of possession of stolen property.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of stolen property. Defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence and raised claims of ineffective assistance of counsel, prosecutorial misconduct, and erroneous evidentiary rulings. The court stated that the jury heard ample evidence from which it could infer that defendant knew or had reason to know that he possessed a stolen car. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to permit the jurors to reach they verdict which they did reach. The court further concluded that defendant had not met his heavy burden to establish that his attorney rendered ineffective assistance of counsel in making decisions regarding the calling of witnesses. The trial court did not err when it ruled that defendant's prior petty misdemeanor and misdemeanor convictions were admissible. Defendant's petty misdemeanor conviction could not be used to impeach him under Minn. R. Evid. 609 because Minn. R. Crim. P. 23.06 directed that a petty misdemeanor would not be considered a crime. However, the petty misdemeanor conviction was admissible under Minn. R. Evid. 608(b) as a specific instance of conduct probative of defendant's truthfulness or untruthfulness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of stolen property.

 

1088 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. American Family Mut. Ins. Co.


C6-94-725


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


521 N.W.2d 366; 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 886



September 6, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Bruce Hartigan, Judge. District Court File No. CT 91-13008



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of an order from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which found that it was liable for the full amount of underinsured motorist (UIM) coverage available under the automobile policy of respondent passenger's father.


OVERVIEW: The passenger was injured when the car in which he was riding went out of control and struck a fence and a building. The passenger contended that he was entitled to the full amount of the insurer's UIM coverage because he sustained, but did not recover the full amount of his damages from the driver's liability policy. On appeal, the court concluded that Minn. Stat. § 65B.49(4a) applied where an injured passenger had not collected underinsured motorist benefits first from the car owner or driver's policy. Minn. Stat. § 65B.49(3a)(5) should have been invoked against an injured person only when that person sought UIM benefits under his or her own policy after already qualifying for UIM benefits from another source. There was no "excess" coverage under subdivision 3a(5) because there was no coverage available to the passenger under the driver's policy that was "like" the coverage that he sought from the insurer. The trial court did not err in applying Minn. Stat. § 65B.49(4a) to permit the passenger to receive the total amount available under the insurer's UIM coverage. The trial court also did not err in allowing the passenger to make a UIM claim under only one policy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order finding that the insurer was liable for the full amount of underinsured motorist coverage.

 

1089 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Schweninger


CX-94-825


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


520 N.W.2d 446; 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 783



August 16, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Marilyn J. Justman, Judge. District Court File No. PP05292



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which committed him indefinitely as a psychopathic personality pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 526.09 after he served his sentence for criminal sexual conduct in the first degree, second degree, and third degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to criminal sexual misconduct charges for incidents that involved three juvenile male victims. A petition for his commitment as a psychopathic personality was filed when defendant was scheduled for a release from prison. At the hearing, defendant testified that he had molested 17 children. A psychologist diagnosed defendant as an entrenched pedophile with a 15-year history of varying sexually inappropriate behavior toward young boys. A psychiatrist who was the clinical director of a sex offender program testified that defendant planned and plotted for opportunities to exploit children. The court reversed the district court's decision that committed defendant as a psychopathic personality. Absent a showing of violence, persons in the class of repetitive pedophiles were not to be committed as psychopathic personalities unless it was shown that they committed violent acts in the past and that they had such an utter lack of power to control their behavior that they were likely to do so in the future. Under the Minnesota Criminal Code, defendant's prior acts of sexual misconduct were not violent or assaultive.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment.

 

1090 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Larson


C2-93-1991


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


520 N.W.2d 456; 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 791



August 16, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Larson, 1994 Minn. LEXIS 845 (Minn., Oct. 14, 1994)
Post-conviction relief denied at Larson v. State, 1997 Minn. App. LEXIS 627 (Minn. Ct. App., June 10, 1997)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Larson v. Fabian, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 74793 (D. Minn., Oct. 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Goodhue County; Hon. Raymond Pavlak, Judge. Dist. Ct. # K9-92-302
State v. Larson, 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 1005 (Minn. Ct. App., Oct. 19, 1993)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the District Court, Goodhue County (Minnesota) for three counts of first degree criminal sexual assault and one count of second degree criminal sexual assault in violation of Minn. Stat. §§ 609.342, subd. 1(g) and (h)(i) and 609.343, subd. 1(g) (1990).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's niece filed a complaint alleging that he forced her to have intercourse with him twice. One incident occurred in Renville County and the other occurred in Goodhue County. He was charged with multiple counts in Goodhue County and, after a trial, he was found guilty. He was sentenced to terms of imprisonment on two of the counts that were to run consecutive with sentences imposed for the sexual assault of another niece. On appeal, the court affirmed his convictions on two counts. The trial court properly accepted venue for the Renville charges. The plain language of Minn. Stat. § 627.15 (1990) and its legislative history revealed the intent to include a child's county of residence as a place the child may be "found." Because defendant was in a position of authority as defined in Minn. Stat. § 609.341, subd. 10 (1990), the child abuse that occurred fell under the provisions of Minn. Stat. § 627.15 (1990). His failure to object to Spreigl evidence at trial constituted a waiver of the right to appeal that issue. Convictions on two of the counts had to be overturned because one count arose out of the same course of conduct and the other was a lesser-included offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions on the charges of first degree criminal sexual conduct committed in Renville County and first degree criminal sexual conduct with use of force or coercion committed in Goodhue County. His convictions on the charges of second degree criminal sexual conduct committed in Renville County and first degree criminal sexual conduct, without force or coercion, committed in Goodhue County were reversed.

Bellini v. University of St. Thomas


C6-94-367


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA

Kingbird v. Indep. Sch. Dist. No. 38


C8-94-63


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 754



August 9, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed August 30, 1994.
Review denied by, Motion granted by Kingbird v. Independent Sch. Dist. No. 38, 1994 Minn. LEXIS 814 (Minn., Sept. 28, 1994)
Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by Kingbird v. Independent Sch. Dist. No. 38, 1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 283 (Minn. Ct. App., Mar. 12, 1996)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Beltrami County; Hon. James E. Preece, Judge. D. C. File No. C6-92-863



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district denied a grievance filed by respondents, 10 teachers and their union, under Minn. Stat. § 126.49, subd. 7, asserting that their compensation violated the American Indian Education Act. Respondents brought a declaratory judgment action, and the district Court, Beltrami County (Minnesota) denied the district's motion for summary judgment and sua sponte awarded summary judgment to respondents. The district appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district was located on an Indian reservation, and the 10 teachers were American Indians. After the district denied the grievance, respondents first requested arbitration, but one month later brought their legal action. The trial court denied the district's motion for summary judgment, which was based on the argument that the trial court did not have jurisdiction to review the actions of a school board in teacher-related matters. The trial court then, sua sponte, issued an order and a memorandum interpreting § 126.49 in respondents' favor and reserving the question of whether respondents' arbitration request was still pending, so as to enable review by certiorari. Respondents moved to compel arbitration and to stay court proceedings. The trial court ordered the parties to proceed with arbitration, but stayed arbitration pending appellate review. The court reversed the trial court's judgment, holding that the only proper procedure for reviewing the district's actions was though a petition for certiorari. Furthermore, certiorari review was no longer available to respondents because they had made an election of remedies. Their decision to litigate waived their right to arbitrate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motorist sought review of a decision from the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which upheld respondent Minnesota Commissioner of Public Safety's order cancelling the motorist's driving privileges on the grounds that his continued driving was inimical to public safety.

Brayton v. City of New Brighton


C0-94-252


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


519 N.W.2d 243; 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 686



July 26, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed August 25, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Gregg E. Johnson, Judge. District Court File No. C7-93-2677



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant resident sought review of a decision of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee city on the resident's action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief against the city, asserting that an ordinance regulating the content and placement of signs was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After the resident placed two signs in her front yard criticizing a decision of a local judge and relating to the treatment of animals, she received a letter from the city planner stating that the signs violated the city ordinance and directing her to remove them. The trial court ruled that the ordinance was not unconstitutional, and on appeal, the court affirmed. The purpose portion of the ordinance stated that it was based on concerns for public safety, order, cleanliness, aesthetics, and administrative convenience. Because these concerns were not related to content, the ordinance was content neutral. Because the ordinance allowed the posting of at least one opinion sign, which could contain multiple messages, on one or multiple issues, at any time of the year, it was reasonably and narrowly tailored. In addition to the signage and the multiple messages, there were alternative means to express opinions such as handbills, picketing, and letters.


OUTCOME: The judgment finding the city ordinance restricting the placement of signs in a resident's property to be constitutional was affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Anoka County (Minnesota), which convicted him of violating Anoka, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 20-4.5 (1992), a city's cruising ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of violating Anoka, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 20-4.5 (1992), a city's cruising ordinance. Accordingly, defendant's conviction under the ordinance was reversed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.

Minter-Weisman Co. v. Comm'r of Revenue


C9-94-167


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


520 N.W.2d 1; 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 689



July 26, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed August 25, 1994.
Review denied by Minter-Weisman Co. v. Commissioner of Revenue, 1994 Minn. LEXIS 791 (Minn., Sept. 28, 1994)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari to Department of Revenue



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator appealed the decision of the Minnesota Department of Review, which granted respondent's summary affirmance motion in an action that involved cigarette rebates pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 325D.33 (1992).


OVERVIEW: Relator, a cigarette wholesaler, issued rebates to retailers following the purchase of cigarettes. Respondent, the commissioner of revenue, through the Minnesota Department of Revenue, issued a warning letter that such rebates violated Minn. Stat. § 325D.33 (1992) which prohibited rebates or concessions on the sale of cigarettes. In a hearing before an administrative law judge, both parties filed summary affirmance motions. Relator appealed the grant of respondent's motion on the basis that the price did not fall below the minimum legal price with the rebate and consequently did not violate the intent of the law. The court affirmed the grant of respondent's motion because relator's interpretation of the law was incorrect since the prohibition against rebates and concessions was independent of the regulations regarding minimum legal price.


OUTCOME: Where the statutory prohibition on rebates and concessions on the sale of cigarettes was independent of the regulations regarding the minimum legal price of cigarettes, relator improperly provided rebates and the court affirmed the grant of respondent's summary affirmance motion.

Thompson v. State


C7-94-68


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 702



July 20, 1994, Decided  
July 26, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied September 16, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Minn. LEXIS 733.
Review denied by Thompson v. State, 1994 Minn. LEXIS 733 (Minn., Sept. 16, 1994)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Marilyn J. Justman, Judge. District Court File No. 90078067
State v. Thompson, 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 458 (Minn. Ct. App., May 5, 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed denial of his postconviction relief petition from District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), arguing that the postconviction court abused its discretion because he did not receive effective assistance of counsel, he was entitled to counsel for his postconviction claim, he was denied a postconviction hearing, and the judge that ruled on his jury waiver also decided his postconviction relief motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of assault, and the trial court imposed an upward durational departure from the presumptive sentence. On direct appeal, defendant challenged the upward departure, but the court affirmed, and defendant moved for postconviction relief, appointment of counsel, and a new trial. Defendant was not entitled to public defender representation and, because the record showed that he was not entitled to postconviction relief, defendant was not entitled to a hearing. Defendant did not show any conflict of interest of counsel or resulting prejudice to him, and no error resulted because the postconviction judge was also the trial judge.

1098 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Bauman by Bauman v. Twp. of Franklin


C7-93-2392


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 657



July 8, 1994, Decided  
July 19, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed August 18, 1994.
Review denied by, Request denied by Bauman by Bauman v. Township of Franklin, 1994 Minn. LEXIS 804 (Minn., Sept. 28, 1994)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Wright County; Hon. Kim R. Johnson, Judge. District Court File No. C0-92-2593



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants landowners challenged a judgment from the District Court, Wright County (Minnesota), finding that respondent township's special assessment for improvements to road was valid. The landowners also challenged the denial of a green acre deferred classification.


OVERVIEW: The landowners asserted that the valuation method for determining the amount each property would be assessed for road improvement was invalid. The trial court disagreed and entered judgment in the township's favor. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. In affirming, the court held that special assessments were presumed to be valid if the land received a special benefit from the improvement, the assessment was uniform upon the same class of property, and the assessment did not exceed the special benefit to the property. Because the assessment was uniform upon the same class of property and the assessment did not exceed the special benefit to the property, the assessment was valid. In addition, the court noted that the assessment formula was based on a standard of accessibility and was not arbitrary and capricious. The landowners failed to overcome the presumption of validity. The fact that all benefited properties were not assessed equally or that some benefited properties were not assessed did not invalidate the assessment. In reversing, the court held that the landowners were entitled to a green acre deferred classification because the township awarded it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the special assessment for improvements but reversed the trial court's denial of a green acre deferred classification.

Coleman v. Town of Forest Lake


CX-93-2385


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 628



July 5, 1994, Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developer sought review of a judgment of the Washington County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent town in the developer's action seeking a writ of mandamus directing the town board to grant his application to subdivide four platted lots or a declaratory judgment that the town's new ordinance was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The developer applied to the town to resubdivide already platted lots. The proposed lots met all existing zoning requirements. Subsequently, the town adopted an ordinance limiting subdivision of previously platted property and then denied the developer's request for noncompliance with the ordinance. Furthermore, the court declined to find that the developer was entitled to relief under the reasonable reliance doctrine created by Minn. Stat. § 462.358, subd. 3c (1992) because the developer was not trying to complete his project as previously approved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment.

Johnson v. 6508 Hodgson Rd.


C9-93-2362


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 636



July 5, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed August 10, 1994.
Review denied by Johnson v. 6508 Hodgson Rd., 1994 Minn. LEXIS 809 (Minn., Sept. 28, 1994)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Anoka County; Hon. Spencer J. Sokolowski, Judge. D. C. File No. C8-89-13943



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a forfeiture order issued by the District Court, Anoka County (Minnesota), ordering the forfeiture of his house in a civil action by the county following defendant's guilty plea to third- and fifth-degree controlled substance possession.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to one count of third-degree controlled substance possession and one count of fifth-degree controlled substance possession. The county commenced a forfeiture action against defendant's house. In a pretrial deposition, defendant admitted selling and using drugs in his house with friends. At a bench trial, the trial court found that the value of the drugs was $ 1,600. The trial court adjudged defendant's house forfeited. Defendant appealed, but the court held that, because defendant had admitted selling drugs out of his house to friends, the evidence supported the trial court's finding that defendant sold cocaine from his house. Thus, the relationship between the real property and the offense was met. Further, the evidence supported the trial court's findings that the value of the drugs seized exceeded $ 1,000. Finally, the court held that the trial court properly considered the statutory factors, compared defendant's investment in the real property to the maximum fine for the applicable crimes, and found that the forfeiture was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order of forfeiture.

 

1101 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Baldwin


C8-93-2126


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 572



June 21, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Isabel Gomez, Judge. District Court File No. 92092768



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought to vacate her convictions from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), for first degree tampering with a witness in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.498, subd. 1(c), and terroristic threats in violation of § 609.713, subd. 1. Defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to support her convictions and that § 609.498, subd. 1(c) was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant made two arguments that her convictions should be vacated: (1) that she did not intend to threaten or intimidate her victim and (2) that the statutes were unconstitutional. The court reviewed the evidence, including the victim's testimony, which defendant claimed conflicted with that of another witness, and the victim's fear of defendant as a result of defendant's alleged threats. The court held that, while there might have been a conflict between the witness testimony, the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction because either interpretation could lead a jury to believe that defendant had threatened the victim. The court also held that the reaction of the victim was circumstantial evidence of defendant's intent. The court then considered defendant's claim of unconstitutionality and held that defendant had the burden of showing that the statutes were unconstitutionally vague for failing to define a criminal offense. The court held that § 609.498, subd. 1(c), specifically defined the crime and did not leave any doubt as to which persons fell within its scope. Defendant thus failed to show beyond a reasonable doubt that the statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

1102 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Stodola v. City of Orono


C2-93-2445


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 576



June 21, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. John M. Stanoch, Judge. District Court File No. 91-8308



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a judgment from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which determined that the city acted arbitrarily and capriciously in refusing to allow respondent property owners a variance to build a shared dock and which ordered the city to adopt the property owners' shared dock proposal.


OVERVIEW: The property owners bought a lot for the purpose of building a dock but not a residence. The adjoining lot had a house on it. A city ordinance required that in order to build a dock, there had to be a house on the property. The property owners built a new dock and after the city informed them that it was illegal, they applied for a variance. When the city denied their application, they proposed conveying some of their property to the adjoining lot owner and building a shared dock. The city denied their proposal. The district court determined that the denial of the property owners' application was arbitrary and capricious and ordered the city to approve their application for a shared dock. On appeal, the court reversed. The shared dock proposal was not acceptable under the zoning code because the use of the dock by the property owners would not have been incidental to the adjoining lot owner's use of his house. The denial of a variance was reasonable because the property owners were aware of the zoning code when they purchased the property. Their "hardship" was not a condition unique to their property. Further, the shared dock proposal was contrary to the aims of the zoning code.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the property owners.

 

1103 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Miller


C6-93-1976


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 528



June 7, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Charles A. Flinn, Jr., Judge. Dist. Court File K8922466



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance after it denied his motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: The officer smelled alcohol on defendant's breath. Because he thought that defendant looked underage, he asked for identification. Defendant said he did not have identification and tried to leave. The officer grabbed defendant's arm and asked again for identification. Seeing a wallet-shaped object in defendant's pocket and believing that it was a wallet, the officer forcibly took the object and discovered that it was a plastic bag containing mushrooms. The trial court convicted defendant of possession of a controlled substance. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that the search of defendant's pocket could not be justified as a search incident to a lawful arrest because defendant could not have been lawfully arrested when his pocket was searched, inasmuch as the officer had not seen him drink any alcohol. Even if the officer had authority to search defendant for identification, he should have first asked defendant to provide his name and age. The officer had no reason to pat-search defendant because he did not believe defendant was armed. The "plain feel" exception did not apply because the officer did not believe that the object in defendant's pocket was contraband.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for possession of a controlled substance.

 

1104 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Mid-City Hotel Assocs. v. Hennepin County Bd. of Comm'rs


C7-94-6


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


516 N.W.2d 574; 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 473



May 24, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed June 24, 1994. Petition for Review Denied August 29, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Minn. LEXIS 700.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Deborah Hedlund, Judge. District Court File No. 93-11358



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which denied a writ of mandamus to compel respondent, the Hennepin County Board of Commissioners, to consider its property tax abatement applications. The trial court declared that Minn. Stat. § 375.192 ratifying the county's policy on filing deadlines was constitutional and denied relief.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether, in the absence of any record that the legislature was aware of the details of the policies that it was ratifying, Minn. Stat. § 375.192, subd. 2 (Supp. 1993) unconstitutionally delegated legislative authority to the counties to establish their own limitation periods for property tax abatement applications. The taxpayer conceded that the legislature had authority to ratify the county ordinances. It contended only that the legislature violated the constitutional limitations on delegating power by acting in the absence of a record showing that it knew the precise contents of the various ordinances. However, the court found that there was nothing in the case law to suggest that under the delegation doctrine the legislature had to ascertain the contents of a law before it could ratify it. All the constitution required was that the legislative standards created by the ratification were clear and ascertainable by those to whom the standards would apply. Here, the limitations periods applicable to abatement applications were unambiguous, regardless of whether the legislature actually knew the details of the policies of the individual counties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying the taxpayer's request for a writ of mandamus to compel the Board to consider its property tax abatement applications.

 

1105 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


City of Worthington Police Dep't v. One 1988 Chevrolet Berreta


C2-93-2266


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


516 N.W.2d 581; 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 475



May 24, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Nobles County; Hon. Jeffrey L. Flynn, Judge. District Court File No. C79395.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner of forfeited vehicle challenged a decision from District Court, Nobles County (Minnesota) granting summary judgment in favor of respondent city police department in a proceeding for the forfeiture of a motor vehicle used as transportation to and from the scene of a burglary.


OVERVIEW: The owner of a vehicle drove to a motel. He entered one of the guest rooms without permission and stole a color television set valued at $ 300. He then used the car to deliver the TV to another person. The owner pled guilty to third-degree felony burglary charges. The city police department seized the vehicle, valued at between $ 2500 and $ 4500, initiated forfeiture proceedings, and moved for summary judgment, which the trial court granted. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding the trial court's application of the forfeiture statute did not violate the constitutional prohibition against excessive fines. Minnesota courts were never required to order forfeiture. A law enforcement agency that wished to deprive an owner permanently of property had to petition the court for an order of forfeiture. Once the court determined that property was subject to forfeiture, it had to decide whether to order forfeiture. Thus, Minnesota courts had discretion to order forfeiture of property used to commit a designated offense under the forfeiture statute. If the use of property played a significant part in committing an offense, then the property could be forfeited, no matter what its value.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision granting summary judgment in favor of the city police department in its proceeding for the forfeiture of the owner's motor vehicle used as transportation to and from the scene of a burglary.

 

1106 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Miller


C9-94-220


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 483



May 18, 1994, Decided  
May 24, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied July 27, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Minn. LEXIS 592.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Kanabec County; Hon. James R. Clifford, Judge. District Court File No. K4-93-555



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed an appeal from the decision of the District Court, Kanabec County (Minnesota), which held that a search and seizure was unconstitutional and dismissed the charges against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession of a controlled substance in violation of Minn. Stat. § 152.025, subd. 2(1) (1992). Defendant moved to suppress the evidence seized for lack of a search warrant. The trial court determined that the search and seizure was unconstitutional and dismissed the charges. The trial court noted that defendant did not have a reasonable expectation of privacy in the open fields where the marijuana plants were being grown and that the officer was within his rights to view the plants both from above and from the ground. The court, however, concluded that the extended intrusion and continued trespass was unreasonable and unwarranted. The appeal followed. The court held that since the marijuana was seized in an open field, defendant had no reasonable expectation of privacy in his activities there. Thus, he did not have standing to object to the search and seizure. Because defendant did not have standing to object to the search, the reasonableness of the search was not an issue. Accordingly, the trial court erred in dismissing the charges against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the matter.

State v. Dressen


C7-93-1324


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 444



May 17, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Lincoln County; Hon. George A. Marshall, Judge. District Court File No. K892126



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the District Court of Lincoln County (Minnesota), which convicted him of two counts of arson and one count of conspiracy to commit arson.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of arson and one count of conspiracy to commit arson. Defendant appealed, contending that the trial court violated his due process rights by allowing testimony of a witness who was granted immunity and paid $ 1,000, that there was insufficient corroboration of the accomplice's testimony, and that the trial court committed reversible error by failing to give a jury instruction on accomplice testimony. The court affirmed, holding that the witness explained the circumstances and the substance of the agreement at length during direct and cross-examination and that there was no violation of defendant's due process rights. The court held that the witness' testimony was sufficiently corroborated to support defendant's convictions and that the trial court's failure to provide an accomplice instruction did not render defendant's trial fundamentally unfair.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

Pine County v. Minnesota Dep't of Natural Resources


C2-93-2140


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 460



May 17, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied July 27, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Minn. LEXIS 597.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Pine County; Hon. Timothy R. Bloomquist, Judge. District Court File No. C393283



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county government officials, appealed from the judgment of the District Court, Pine County (Minnesota), which held that they did not have standing to file suit against respondent, Minnesota Department of Natural Resources, over legislation that was repealed by the state legislature which impaired their contract obligations.


OVERVIEW: The state legislature passed legislation which allowed county governments to maintain tax forfeited land and use the natural resources instead of collecting property taxes. Thereafter the state legislature repealed the legislation and the county government officials filed suit, claiming that the repeal impaired their contract obligations. The trial court dismissed the lawsuit for lack of standing and the officials appealed. The court held that under the general rule, a public official or governmental unit, in performing a ministerial duty under a statute, may not question the constitutionality of that statute. The court stated that to hold that a political subdivision employer was entitled to assail the constitutionality of legislative enactments every time the public was subject to the slightest economic burden would unjustifiably erode the doctrine of standing as it has been traditionally applied. The court determined that because the county officials were performing ministerial duties under the legislation, they lacked standing to challenge the repeal of the legislation. The court upheld the lower court's ruling and dismissed the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

In re Fitzpatrick


C6-94-255


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 408



May 3, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County. Hon. Marilyn J. Justman, Judge. District Court File No. PP05356.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), that committed him to the Minnesota Security Hospital as a psychopathic personality. On appeal, the patient contended, inter alia, that he did not fit the legal criteria for commitment as a psychopathic personality.


OVERVIEW: Under Minn. Stat. §§ 253B.18, subd. 1, 526.10, subd. 1 (1992), the State had the burden of establishing by clear and convincing evidence that a proposed patient was a psychopathic personality. Psychopathic personality was defined by Minn. Stat. § 526.09 (1992). The court disagreed with the arguments of the patient that there was no evidence presented below that he had an utter lack of power to control his sexual impulses and that the trial court failed to apply the proper standard. In disagreeing, the court considered that he had committed multiple sexual assaults, which included force, beatings, and threats to kill and that he admitted that he was unable to control himself regarding heat of passion. The court ruled that the trial court's conclusion that the patient should be committed as a psychopathic personality was not clearly erroneous. The court stated that the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. §§ 526.09-526.20 (1992) had been upheld. In rejecting the argument that the evidence was insufficient because it was largely based on written documents, the court stated that the patient agreed to the admission of all documents taken as evidence.


OUTCOME: Ruling against the patient, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

In re Lawful Gambling License of Thief River Falls Amateur Hockey Ass'n, License No. 02008


C2-93-1943


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


515 N.W.2d 604; 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 396



April 26, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari to MN Lawful Gambling Control Board



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator, a hockey association, sought review of a decision of respondent, the State of Minnesota Lawful Gambling Control Board, which suspended the association's premises permit for a certain bar for one year because illegal gambling had been conducted at the bar. The Board adopted an administrative law judge's (ALJ) findings of fact and conclusions, with minor clerical corrections.


OVERVIEW: The association operated a youth hockey program. The association was licensed to conduct lawful gambling. Agents of a department of public safety conducted an undercover investigation into allegations that illegal sports boards were being used at a certain bar. The association did not participate in the illegal gambling and was not aware of any unlawful gambling. The ALJ concluded that illegal gambling was conducted at the bar and that the Board was required to suspend the association's premises permit for the bar location for one year. The association brought a substantive due process challenge to Minn. R. 7861.0050 (Supp. II 1992). In affirming the decision, the court concluded that Minn. R. 7861.0050 (Supp. II 1992) was rationally related to maintaining the integrity of, and public confidence in, lawful gambling because it ensured that the public could enter an establishment where there was lawful gambling and be confident that no illegal gambling has been conducted on the premises. Minn. R. 7865.0050 (Supp. II 1992) did not contravene substantive due process on its face, nor was it invalid as applied to the association.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

In re Sadiki


C4-93-2317


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 295



April 5, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied June 1, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Minn. LEXIS 432.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; James F. Finley, Ramsey County Court Commissioner. District Court File No. P9911977



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant psychiatric patient complained of a judgment of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which committed him as a psychopathic personality for an indeterminate period.


OVERVIEW: The patient raped three young women, the youngest of whom was a 12-year-old girl. He was imprisoned and paroled. Several months later, he raped another 12-year-old girl and was imprisoned again. He was paroled and raped two more young women. The patient contended there was no evidence that he had an utter lack of power to control his sexual impulses. The trial court explicitly found that the patient met the statutory criteria in Minn. Stat. § 526.09 (1992). It further found the patient's conduct showed an utter lack of power to control his sexual impulses, that his condition was only partially treated, and that he continued to be an imminent danger to others from sexual attack. Evidence showed that the patient committed habitual sex offenses, had no insight into his condition, did not believe he needed treatment, and continued to be hostile, angry, and dangerous. The trial court made proper findings, which were not clearly erroneous. The patient's arguments from civil commitment procedures were inapposite; the statutory definition of mentally ill and dangerous should not be used for determining whether an individual met the standards for commitment as a psychopathic personality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Andrews v. Benson


C0-93-2038


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 277



March 29, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed April 18, 1994. Petition for Review Denied May 17, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Minn. LEXIS 396.
Review denied by Andrews v. Benson, 1994 Minn. LEXIS 396 (Minn., May 17, 1994)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; District Court File No. MC 90-004312. Hon. John J. Sommerville, Judge.
Andrews v. Benson, 476 N.W.2d 194, 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 994 (Minn. Ct. App., 1991)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant neighbors sought review of a decision from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent owners in their declaratory judgment action, which sought to challenge the validity and duration of restrictive covenants. This was the second appeal in the action.


OVERVIEW: The owners' and the neighbors' properties were burdened by restrictive covenants. The owners brought a declaratory judgment action, which challenged the validity of the covenants. The trial court granted the owners' motion for summary judgment, but the court reversed that decision and remanded the case. On remand, the trial court against granted the owners' motion for summary judgment, and the neighbors appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court found that Minn. Stat. § 500.20, subd. 2a (1988) set a 30 year duration for covenants but allowed a filing of a notice of claim, which delayed application of the 30 year provision. Because the neighbors had filed a notice of claim, the court held that the covenants were extended for an additional seven years under § 500.20, subd. 2a. There were justiciable controversies throughout the litigation over whether § 500.20, subd. 2a applied to the covenants and over whether the covenants were nominal. Section §500.20, subd. 2a did not violate due process and was not unconstitutional. It did not violate the contracts clause of the United States and Minnesota Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1113 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Koenig


C1-93-1254, C4-93-1572


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 237



March 22, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Granted in part, Denied in part June 1, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Minn. LEXIS 433.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Pope County; D. C. File No. T8-92-1308. Hon. Jon Stafsholt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the District Court, Pope County (Minnesota), which convicted defendant of careless driving and driving with no insurance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was transporting farm equipment in a tractor-trailer when an oncoming vehicle crossed the center line and collided with defendant. The driver of the vehicle was killed. Defendant was charged with numerous safety and regulatory misdemeanors. When defendant reached trial he was charged with reckless driving, careless driving, no Minnesota driver's license and no insurance. Throughout the entire process defendant represented himself. The court held that the trial court's failure to obtain a waiver of counsel on the record required a remand for a new trial. The court noted that defendant's right to counsel was the most important trial right he could have, and when defendant sought to appear pro se, the trial court was required to find that the request was clear, and that defendant knowingly and intelligently waived his right to counsel. Minn. R. Crim. P. 5.02 required that a waiver of counsel be in writing or on the record, or that the trial court appoint counsel to defendant. The trial court failed to accomplish any of those tasks. That defendant appeared to know what he was doing did not mitigate the requirements of the rule.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the matter for a new trial.

In re Welfare of K.C.


C8-93-1543


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


513 N.W.2d 18; 1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 215



March 15, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected. Petition for Review Denied May 17, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Minn. LEXIS 398.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; District Court File No. 17377497. Hon. Andrew W. Danielson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A juvenile sought review of a juvenile reference order, entered by the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota) under the prima facie reference statute, Minn. Stat. § 260.125, subd. 3 (1992). The juvenile was charged by delinquency petition with one count of first degree murder and two counts of second degree murder. The State moved for a reference for adult prosecution, citing the prima facie reference statute.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was charged with one count of first degree murder and two counts of second degree murder based on his role as an accomplice. The victim was shot by two young men. The juvenile told police that the victim had been harassing him lately with threats, and that he and the two men had driven to the victim's house to scare him. The juvenile admitted handing one of the men a shotgun and giving the other man a handgun. The juvenile was referred for adult prosecution. On appeal, the juvenile contended that the prima facie reference statute was not properly applied to him because he was only a passive accomplice. The court affirmed the trial court's order. The court found that the juvenile participated in the planning of the planned assault, and that a violent confrontation with the victim was a foreseeable consequence. The court further found that (1) the prima facie reference statute was not void for vagueness; (2) the statute did not shift the burden of proof to the juvenile; and (3) the statute did not violate equal protection because it created an age-based distinction rationally related to the objectives of the juvenile justice system.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order referring the juvenile for adult prosecution.

In re Sabo


CX-93-2175


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult male sought review of a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which committed him as a psychopathic personality to a security hospital for an indeterminate period.


OVERVIEW: A man committed a series of rapes or attempted rapes over seven years, and had been convicted of criminal sexual conduct. The man also had multiple admissions to sex offender and chemical dependency treatment programs, which he had been able to complete even though he was considered to be at high risk to reoffend. Thereafter, following a hearing, a trial court committed him as a psychopathic individual to a security hospital, a commitment that the court earlier affirmed on appeal. State v. Villalobos


C6-93-1072


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 194



March 8, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied May 3, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Minn. LEXIS 362.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; File No. K9921956. Hon. Paulette K. Flynn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which convicted and sentenced him for criminal vehicular homicide. The trial court sentenced defendant to 87 months, a departure from the presumptive sentence of 58 months. The court also imposed a $ 4,000 fine and ordered $ 1,093 in restitution.


OVERVIEW: A car knocked the victim to the ground in a crosswalk. After hesitating briefly, the driver sped away, running directly over the victim. The victim died immediately, or soon after. Two witnesses who knew defendant recognized him as the driver of the car. Defendant challenged: (1) a photographic lineup; (2) sufficiency of the evidence; (3) upward durational departure; and (4) imposing of the fine. The court affirmed in part, but vacated the fine. The court concluded that the lineup was not unconstitutionally suggestive and was not tainted by prior improper showup identification where the lineup occurred two days after the showup identification. The court further found sufficient evidence to support the conviction, noting that the in-court eyewitness identification of defendant was not based on a fleeting observation and so could support the conviction. The court further concluded that defendant's actions indicated a callous disregard for the law and dangerousness, which was sufficient to support the upward departure. However, the statute making a fine mandatory had not been in effect at the time the accident occurred, and so the fine had been improperly imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision except for the imposition of the fine, which was vacated.

In re Buckhalton


C2-93-2428


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 164



February 15, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which ordered him committed to the Minnesota Security Hospital for an indeterminate period for care and treatment as a psychopathic personality under Minn. Stat. §§ 526.10, subd. 1, 253B.18, subd. 1 (1992).


OVERVIEW: The patient claimed that there was no evidence presented at the review hearing that he was a psychopathic personality and that he had an utter lack of power to control his sexual impulses. The court affirmed the order of commitment, holding that there was ample evidence to support the trial court's decision. The court found that the patient was impulsive and lacked customary good judgment. His convictions were a direct result of his impulsiveness, anger, and attitude towards women. He shifted the blame and was resistant to addressing his sexual problems. He used force to get his way and often violated the rights of others to satisfy his urges, and he failed to appreciate the consequences of and had no remorse for his actions. The court also affirmed commitment to the Minnesota Security Hospital. The patient claimed that it was not the least restrictive alternative. The court found that it was the only facility offering the intense long-term treatment required for psychopathic personalities.

Carey v. Jorgenson


CX-93-1012


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 98



February 1, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.

Review denied by Carey v. Jorgenson, 1994 Minn. LEXIS 256 (Minn., Mar. 31, 1994)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Mower County; Dist. Ct. # C3911441. Hon. James L. Mork, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of a judgment of the Mower County District Court (Minnesota), which ordered a directed verdict in favor of respondent driver in respondent's action for injuries suffered in an accident.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and a friend left a party. Respondent and two friends, in three cars, followed appellant to retrieve a stereo from appellant's possession. Appellant and another friend passed respondent and blocked the road in front of him with their cars. The third car approached from behind. There was an impact between respondent's car and the third car, initiated by respondent backing up or the third car hitting him. Respondent was injured and sued appellant and the other two drivers. The drivers of the second and third cars settled with respondent prior to trial. At the close of evidence the trial court ordered a directed verdict for respondent on the issues of causation and respondent's negligence. The jury determined damages. Appellant sought review of the directed verdict. The court held that if appellant had not illegally parked in the road, the collision would not have occurred. The court further held that the trial court properly applied the emergency rule to the action, which provided that a person who did not choose the best way out of an emergency was not negligent by virtue of that choice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Golden Valley Lutheran College v. City of Golden Valley


CX-93-1852


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 92



January 25, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected. Petition for Review Filed February 23, 1994. Petition for Review Denied March 15, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Minn. LEXIS 221.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; District Court File 899790. Hon. Ann Montgomery, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, former operators of a two-year college, challenged the grant by the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), of summary judgment in favor of respondent city and against their claims of unconstitutional taking of property and tortious interference with prospective business advantage. They also argued that the chief judge of the district erred in denying their motion to remove the judge who granted summary judgment in the case.


OVERVIEW: The operators argued that the city's imposition of a one-year development moratorium forced their property into foreclosure, amounting to an unconstitutional taking of property without just compensation. The court disagreed and found no evidence of a taking by the city either under the "categorical takings" or the "Penn Central balancing" tests. There was no evidence that the moratorium prevented the sale of the property to prospective buyers. The court noted that even if all economically beneficial use was denied during the moratorium, economic use existed at the end of the moratorium period. There was no evidence that a judge ordered foreclosure because of the moratorium. The operators presented no evidence to support their assertion that the moratorium affected their ability to sell the property before the foreclosure. There were no genuine issues of material fact as to whether the city tortiously interfered with three prospective business relationships. The chief judge of the district did not err in failing to remove the judge hearing the summary judgment motion; inter alia, a removal motion could not rest on a family relationship that no longer existed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1120 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jackson


C0-93-63


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1994 Minn. App. LEXIS 68



January 18, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; District Court File No. 92000404. Hon. Richard B. Solum, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which convicted him of both a first and second degree controlled substance crimes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the sale of crack cocaine, a first degree controlled substance crime. Subsequently, the complaint was amended to include additional charges of a second degree controlled substance crime and aiding and abetting. The State dropped the aiding and abetting charge, and defendant was convicted of the other two charges. The court affirmed the convictions. The trial court did not err in refusing to dismiss the entire jury panel based on defendant's entry into the jury panel room before voir dire because no juror bias was shown. Even though the officers', without a warrant, may have entered the hallway of the apartment building in which the drug transaction took place in order to ascertain the correct apartment number, the application for a search warrant was sufficient even without the apartment number. The warrantless search of defendant's backpack was lawful because no warrant was required for a search incident to a lawful arrest in a motor vehicle. The elements of proving possession did not change when the aiding and abetting charge was added to the complaint or when it was dropped. Thus, defendant was not prejudiced by the amendments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for first and second degree controlled substance crimes.

 

1121 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Will


CX-93-1771


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 1229



December 21, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; District Court File No. PP05180. Hon. Marilyn Justman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), that committed him as a psychopathic personality.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court was clearly erroneous in committing him as a psychopathic personality based on its finding that he exhibited an utter lack of power to control his sexual impulses. Defendant also contended that the psychopathic personality statute was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the judgment and held that the record supported the determination that defendant had a lack of power over his sexual impulses. The trial court found that defendant forced intercourse on a pregnant woman, put his hands inside the pants of two young girls, forced sex upon his former girlfriend, and sexually assaulted a 16 year old girl. The court held that based upon the testimony of the experts and the court's assessment of the incidents in which defendant was involved, the trial court's determination was not clearly erroneous. The court rejected the argument that the psychopathic personality statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1122 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Jones by Blume v. Kvamme


CX-93-944


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


510 N.W.2d 6; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 1269



December 17, 1993, Decided  
December 28, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed January 28, 1994. Petition for Review Granted March 15, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Minn. LEXIS 204.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Nicollet County; District Court File No. 84-DC-26. Hon. Warren E. Litynski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtor challenged a decision of the District Court, Nicollet County (Minnesota), which held that a "rollover" account held by the debtor's bank was not exempt from garnishment because Minn. Stat. § 550.37(24) violated the Minnesota Constitution and the funds were not necessary for the debtor's support.


OVERVIEW: Appellee personal representative served a garnishment notice on the debtor's bank in an attempt to satisfy a judgment against the debtor for fraudulent misrepresentation. The debtor claimed that his bank assets were exempt under Minn. Stat. § 550.37(24) (1990). The trial court disallowed the exemption. On appeal, the court reversed and allowed the exemption, but the Minnesota Supreme Court remanded the case for a determination of the constitutionality of § 550.37(24). The trial court held that the rollover account was not exempt because § 550.37(24) violated the constitution. The court held that the representative had not demonstrated beyond a reasonable doubt that the statute violated the "reasonable amount" requirement in Minn. Const. art. I, § 12. The court held that Minn. Const. art. XII, § was not violated by § 550.37(24)(1) because different treatment of nonexempt retirement funds from qualified tax-exempt retirement funds did not make clause (1) unconstitutional special legislation. The court found that the Internal Revenue Code provisions cited in § 550.37(24)(1) provided objective limitation criteria that prevented unlimited contributions to qualified retirement accounts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed holding that the trial court erred by concluding that the constitution's "reasonable amount" requirement was violated by the statute and that the statute violated the prohibition against special laws. The court affirmed upholding the trial court's determination that the rollover account was not reasonably necessary for the support of the debtor, but that the funds were nevertheless exempt from garnishment or attachment.

 

1123 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Neal v. State Farm Ins. Co.


C4-93-647


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


509 N.W.2d 173; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 1178



December 7, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Filed January 10, 1994. Petition for Review Granted February 1, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Minn. LEXIS 85.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Dist. Ct. File No. 9118324. Hon. Pamela G. Alexander, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insured sought review of the judgment from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which found in favor of respondent insurer and vacated an arbitration award that allowed the insured to recover further no-fault benefits after failing to attend a medical examination.


OVERVIEW: The insured had been injured in a car accident and incurred wage loss and medical expenses. The insured was reimbursed by her no-fault insurer. The insurer then scheduled a medical examination for the insured and the insured failed to attend. The insurer then suspended payment of further no-fault benefits. The arbitrator ordered the insurer to pay medical and wage loss benefits, but the trial court vacated the award, concluding that the insured's unreasonable failure to attend the examination automatically allowed the insurer to terminate payment of further no-fault benefits. In reversing, the court held that mere noncooperation, without more, did not mandate automatic termination. Although an insured who failed to cooperate with a properly scheduled examination had to be prepared to accept negative consequences, noncooperation did not automatically zero out all insureds in all claims. The court further held that the requirement of mandatory arbitration pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 65B.525, subd. 1, did not violate the Minnesota Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.
