In re Rickmyer


CX-93-1446


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 1143



November 23, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed December 27, 1993. Petition for Review Granted February 1, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Minn. LEXIS 89. Petition for Review Granted February 2, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Minn. LEXIS 80.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; District Court File No. 911857. Hon. James F. Finley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which committed him as a psychopathic personality for an indeterminate time under Minn. Stat. § 526.09 (1992).


OVERVIEW: The patient had three convictions for sexual contact with young boys. Upon receipt of the patient's 60-day treatment report, following his initial commitment, the district court conducted a two-day commitment hearing. Testimony was presented about the patient's conduct and his criminal acts, psychologists testified as to the patient's condition, and the patient's medical records and psychological evaluations were admitted. The court held that the district court did not clearly err in concluding that the patient was a psychopathic personality. The record demonstrated that the patient had three convictions in three years for crimes involving exposing himself to or abusing young boys, he was diagnosed as a pedophile and as having a psychopathic personality, the patient refused to participate in assessment or treatment, he had a high probability of reoffending, and he sought out activities that placed him in contact with young children. The court rejected the patient's constitutional challenges to the psychopathic personality statute. Nothing in the record indicated that the county attorney agreed to waive the opportunity to start civil commitment proceedings against the patient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commitment order.

 

1125 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C4-93-874, C6-93-1122, C8-93-1123, CX-93-1124, C3-93-1143, C7-93-1226, C9-93-1227, C0-93-1228, C2-93-1229, C4-93-1393, C6-93-1394


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


509 N.W.2d 380; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 1171



November 22, 1993, Decided  
November 30, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed December 27, 1993. Petition for Review Granted January 21, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Minn. LEXIS 41. As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Dakota, Hennepin, Scott, and Washington Counties; District Court File Nos.: 471188, 9302762, 9302761, 9302982, C6-92-6936, 9302181, 9303607, 9303385, 9302534, C8-93-6928, C2-93-6682. Hon. Thomas Murphy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner drivers challenged the decisions of respondent Commissioner of Public Safety, who revoked their drivers' licenses pursuant to the implied consent law, Minn. Stat. § 169.123, subd. 4 (1992). The cases were heard by the District Courts of Hawker, Schmelzer, Lettow, Berg, Willetts, Iverson, Dopp, and Decker Counties (Minnesota), which made findings as to whether the law violated due process and addressed statutory challenges to the law.


OVERVIEW: The drivers challenged on statutory, fundamental fairness, and procedural due process grounds the Commissioner's decision to revoke their drivers' licenses pursuant to the implied consent law. It was held that one driver's right to counsel was not vindicated. Other district courts vindicated the drivers' constitutional and statutory challenges to the implied consent law. One district court determined that there was probable cause as to one driver's revocation. Upon consolidated review, the court affirmed as to the right to counsel issue, concluding that the driver was not given enough time to contact an attorney. The court also affirmed the finding that probable cause was established by a preponderance of the evidence. However, the court reversed on the constitutional and statutory grounds, holding (1) that under the applicable balancing test, the implied consent law did not violate procedural due process, (2) that the failure to advise the drivers of all of the potential consequences of not submitting to an intoxication test was not fundamentally unfair, and (3) that refusing to take the test did not provide them with a "safe harbor" because they had a limited right to counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order rescinding the license revocation of a driver whose right to counsel was not vindicated, affirmed the orders which rejected two drivers' argument that the proceedings under the implied consent statute were criminal, and affirmed the rejection of a driver's probable cause argument. The court reversed the orders which rescinded the revocations on statutory, fundamental fairness, and procedural due process grounds.

 

1126 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Welsh v. Johnson


C9-93-1132


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


508 N.W.2d 212; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 1125



November 16, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, St. Louis County; District Court File C093600428. Hon. Gerald Martin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant picketer sought review of a decision of the District Court, St. Louis County (Minnesota), which enjoined the picketer from any further contact with respondent director of a women's health center for the next two years pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 609.748 (1972).


OVERVIEW: Abortion protests began outside the clinic where the director worked. The picketer would call the director out by name and made her feel intimidated. Thereafter, the picketing moved to in front of the director's home. The director obtained an ex parte temporary restraining order, pursuant to § 609.748 against the picketer, and within an hour of being served with the order the picketer began following her at a close distance. The trial court thereafter issued a two-year restraining order, which provided that he could not come within two blocks of her home. On review, the court found no error. The court held that § 609.748 was not an unconstitutional infringement of the picketer's First Amendment, U. S. Const. amend. I, rights of free speech and free exercise of religion. Because the order prohibited him from communicating with the director, and not from communicating his political or religious beliefs, the court held that it was content neutral. Further, the court held that the state's interest in protecting the well being, tranquility, and privacy of the home was of the highest order in a free and civilized society.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the findings of the trial court.

 

1127 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Austin Daily Herald v. Mork


C4-93-2186


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


507 N.W.2d 854; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 1096; 22 Media L. Rep. 1442



November 5, 1993, Decided  
November 5, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed November 19, 1993. Petition for Review Denied December 14, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 818.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Mower County; District Court File No. K9931092. Hon. James L. Mork, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of prohibition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner newspapers filed an application for a writ of prohibition against respondent trial judge. The newspapers challenged trial judge's order that restricted media access during parts of a criminal trial.


OVERVIEW: The trial judge ordered the public excluded from the criminal trial during the testimony of juvenile victims and scheduled a hearing on media objections to the restricted access. The trial judge modified its restrictive order to permit the newspapers to attend, on condition that they not reveal the names or information about juvenile records of the underage victims and witnesses. The newspaper challenged the order by filing a petition for a writ of prohibition, which was denied. The court rejected the newspapers' claim that the trial judge had imposed an impermissible prior restraint on the publication of information. The court noted that the trial judge did not restrain the newspapers from publishing information already in their possession about the juveniles or their prior involvement with the juvenile court system, or information they might later obtain from other sources. The court found that the trial judge properly focused on "the incremental injury" to the juveniles that would be caused by testifying in public, as distinguished from the effect of confronting the criminal defendant and the trauma inherent in testifying about personal matters.


OUTCOME: The court denied the newspapers' petition for a writ of prohibition.

 

1128 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Claude v. Collins


C0-93-564, C5-93-642


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


507 N.W.2d 452; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 1031



October 26, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed November 29, 1993. As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, St. Louis County; District Court File No. C592300440. Hon. Robert F. Berger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant council member and respondent council members sought review of decision of the District Court, St. Louis County (Minnesota), which found that they violated the Minnesota Open Meeting Law, Minn. Stat. § 471.705 (1990). Respondent citizens appealed from the decision insofar as the trial court failed to remove the members and allegedly miscalculated the number of violations.


OVERVIEW: The members allegedly violated the Open Meeting Law, Minn. Stat. § 471.705, by conducting certain nonpublic meetings. The trial court fined each member $ 100 per "intentional" violation, but declined to remove the members from office. On appeal, the members alleged that they did not violate the Open Meeting Law and that their equal protection rights were violated when the citizens settled with two council members who were former defendants in the underlying action. The citizens asserted that the members should have been removed from office pursuant to § 471.705, subd. 2. The court held that the trial court's conclusion that the gatherings were subject to the Open Meeting Law was not clearly erroneous because the gatherings were meetings and closed to the public. The court further held that the members' equal protection rights were not violated because the citizens' actions did not involve state action. Moreover, the council members failed to prove that the citizens intentionally discriminated against them. The trial court properly declined to remove the members because although their acts may have constituted misfeasance, the acts did not constitute malfeasance or nonfeasance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Hirt v. State


C9-93-1115


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 1296



October 12, 1993, Decided  
October 13, 1993, FILED


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: District Court File No. K390337.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed an order of the district court (Minnesota), which denied his petition for post conviction relief in which he claimed that the controlled substances statutes, Minn. Stat. §§ 152.022 and 152.023 were unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner appealed the denial of his petition for post-conviction relief, contending the controlled substance statutes, Minn. Stat. §§ 152.022 and 152.023, were unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed the denial of post-conviction relief, holding that the absence of a maximum amount to delineate between the different degrees of controlled substance possessory crimes did not render the statutes unconstitutional and that the statutes' graduated scale defined the varying offenses with sufficient definiteness that ordinary people can understand what conduct is prohibited. The court also held that petitioner failed to provide evidence to suggest that he was the victim of arbitrary or discriminatory enforcement and that the district court did not abuse its discretion in denying relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying post-conviction relief.

In re Rodriguez


C9-93-1258


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


506 N.W.2d 660; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 976



October 5, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied November 30, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 824.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Olmsted County; District Court File No. P4922717. Hon. John S. Gowan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a decision of the District Court, Olmsted County (Minnesota), which committed him to the Minnesota Security Hospital upon finding that he had a psychopathic personality.


OVERVIEW: A petition was filed to commit the patient as a psychopathic personality based on a lengthy history of sexual misconduct. Prior to the filing of the petition, the patient had been convicted of numerous indecent exposure offenses. At the commitment hearing, conflicting testimony was offered as to whether the patient met the standards for commitment. A clinical psychologist testified that the patient suffered from a psychopathic personality. A social worker testified that the patient's illness was becoming progressive, and that if the patient continued to deny the incidents, his involvement in non-touch offenses would escalate to touch offenses. Another psychologist testified that the patient would reoffend by exposing himself in the future. But in the psychologist's opinion, the patient with only exposing offenses did not meet the statutory criteria under Minn. Stat. § 526.09 (1992) for commitment as a psychopathic personality. The lower court committed the patient as a psychopathic personality. On review, the court reversed. The court held that applying the § 526.09 to a nonviolent exhibitionist was beyond the intent of § 526.09 and the applicable case law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the commitment of the patient as a psychopathic personality.

State v. Castellano


C4-93-356


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


506 N.W.2d 641; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 955



September 28, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; District Court File No. T49185738. Hon. John S. Connolly, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Ramsey County (Minnesota), which convicted him of violating Town of White Bear, Minn., Ordinance No. 63 (1990), a township ordinance that prohibited targeted residential picketing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating Town of White Bear, Minn., Ordinance No. 63 (1990), a township ordinance that prohibited targeted residential picketing. Defendant had been arrested for violating the targeted residential picketing ordinance after he refused to stop picketing in front of the residence of the executive director of Planned Parenthood of Minnesota. On appeal, defendant facially challenged the constitutionality of the ordinance on the grounds of overbreadth and vagueness. The trial court's judgment was affirmed upon a finding that the ordinance was facially constitutional. The court found that the ordinance was content neutral because it unequivocally prohibited all targeted residential picketing regardless of the content of the speech. The court also found that the ordinance fully met the requirement that a valid government interest be served by the regulation of expression because it specifically stated that that the town had an interest in protecting residential privacy. Finally, the court found that the ordinance was narrowly tailored to protect unwilling occupants of a single-family residential dwelling.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1132 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bengston


C9-93-532


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


506 N.W.2d 38; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 933



September 21, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed October 20, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Le Sueur County; District Court File No. 24430. Hon. Thomas C. McCarthy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a recipient of public medical assistance, sought review of a decision of the District Court, Le Sueur County (Minnesota), which ruled that a settlement agreement did not preclude respondent State of Minnesota, Department of Human Services from recovering on a medical assistance lien.


OVERVIEW: The recipient was at her parents' home when she decided to grill pork chops. The recipient asked her brother and father for suggestions because she could not find any lighter fluid. The recipient decided to use gasoline to start a fire. After returning to check on the fire, the recipient discovered that only a few of the coals had started to turn white. The recipient poured more gas on the fire, the gas can exploded, and she was seriously burned. Through its medical assistance program, the Department disbursed money for the recipient's medical treatment. The recipient negotiated a settlement from her father's and brother's insurer. The Department filed suit to satisfy its lien out of the settlement proceeds. The district court ruled that a settlement agreement did not preclude the Department from recovering on a medical assistance lien. The court affirmed holding that the Department's failure to participate in negotiations did not preclude it from satisfying its lien out of the resulting settlement, subject to the recipient's minimum one-third take. Satisfaction of the Department's lien was not barred by the Minnesota Human Rights Act or Minnesota's Equal Protection Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment ruling that the recipient's settlement agreement did not preclude the Department of Human Services from recovering on a medical assistance lien.

 

1133 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Sadiki


C3-93-1045


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 922



September 14, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Granted October 28, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 753.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; District Court # 911977. Hon. James F. Finley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In commitment proceedings under Minn. Stat. § 526.09 (1992), appellant, a convicted sexual offender, challenged the judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) that committed him as a psychopathic personality.


OVERVIEW: While the sex offender was awaiting discharge from imprisonment after serving his sentence, the State petitioned to have him committed as a psychopathic personality. Following a hearing, the trial court ordered the commitment of the sex offender under Minn. Stat. § 526.09 (1992). The sex offender appealed. In affirming, the court concluded that the trial court's findings of fact were not clearly erroneous. In addition to the five rapes for which he had been convicted, he admitted committing approximately 35 additional rapes. The circumstances surrounding his convictions demonstrated hostile, uncontrolled, and repetitive actions. The evidence of the sex offender's continuing ability to control his sexual impulses or even to recognize precursors was clear and convincing, and the evidence was sufficient to establish that he was likely to commit similar crimes in the future. The fact that he had not recently committed such a crime was not dispositive because the artificial prison environment did not present the sex offender with an opportunity to commit additional patterned offenses, and the sex offender had been imprisoned for all but three years from age 19 to 54.


OUTCOME: The judgment of psychopathic personality commitment was affirmed.

Knudtson v. City of Coates


C2-92-2533


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


506 N.W.2d 29; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 904



September 7, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Granted October 28, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 751.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Dakota County; District Court File C9926944. Hon. Patrice K. Sutherland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city appealed from District Court, Dakota County (Minnesota), which granted respondent, a sole proprietor of a bar's request for a declaratory judgment that a city ordinance was unconstitutional and for an injunction prohibiting the enforcement of the ordinance against her.


OVERVIEW: After the city did not renew the sole proprietor's liquor license because a city ordinance prohibiting nudity in liquor establishments had been violated in her bar, the sole proprietor brought this action. On appeal, the court found that the district court properly determined that the city ordinance prohibiting nudity in liquor establishments was unconstitutional and that the city council violated the sole proprietor's constitutional rights in deciding not to renew the liquor license for the bar. The court found that the city ordinance was not a valid time, place, and manner restriction on public nudity because it was not content-neutral. The ordinance prohibited only some forms of nudity. The interest in prohibiting nude dancing was directly related to the suppression of free expression. Because the ordinance was enacted to suppress protected expression, it was not a valid exercise of the city's inherent police power. The court also found that the expression was protected under Minn. Const. art. I, § 3.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision granting the sole proprietor's request for a declaratory judgment that the city ordinance was unconstitutional.

 

1135 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jaworsky


C6-92-2499


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


505 N.W.2d 638; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 878



August 31, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied September 30, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 674.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; District Court File No. 91070918. Hon. Richard B. Solum, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which convicted him of criminal vehicular operation and driving while intoxicated and denied his motions for a new trial and to declare unconstitutional Minnesota's Sentencing Guidelines' recommended sentence for causing death while negligently operating a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was seen slumped over the wheel of his van when the van fishtailed and flipped over, killing a passenger. A blood test showed defendant's alcohol content was 0.29 at the time of the crash. Defendant claimed the accident was caused by a vehicle malfunction. He was convicted of criminal vehicular operation and driving while intoxicated. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the trial court did not err in excluding the report of an expert that examined defendant's van even though the expert died and relevant car parts were lost where the State did not have an opportunity to cross-examine the expert; (2) the jury instructions fairly presented the issue of causation to the jury; and (3) there was no equal protection violation where different prison terms were prescribed by Minn. Stat. § 609.21, subd. 1(2), pertaining to a defendant who caused a person's death by negligently operating a motor vehicle while under the influence, and Minn. Stat. § 609.21, subds. 1(3), 1(4), pertaining to a defendant who caused a person's death by operating a motor vehicle with an alcohol concentration of 0.10 or more, where the former required a showing of negligence and the latter did not.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from the trial court, which convicted defendant of criminal vehicular operation and driving while intoxicated and denied his motions for a new trial and to declare the state's sentencing guidelines unconstitutional.

 

1136 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


City of Rochester v. Peoples Cooperative Power Ass'n


C8-93-19, C4-93-20, CX-93-37, C3-93-39, C7-93-75


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


505 N.W.2d 621; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 880; 147 P.U.R.4th 223



August 31, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Olmsted County; District Court File No. C0-90-281. Hon. Margaret Shaw Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a township and an individual, sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Olmsted County (Minnesota), which authorized respondent city to acquire, by quick-take, certain electrical rights previously assigned by appellant Minnesota Public Utilities Commission (MPUC) to appellant cooperative power association.


OVERVIEW: According to an assignment by the MPUC, the area received electrical service from the association. The city filed several petitions to condemn, by quick-take, the associations electrical service rights in the area in order to extend its own utility service to the annexed area. On a prior appeal, the state supreme court determined that a city could extend its provision of utility service to annexed territory either by purchase under terms determined by the MPUC pursuant to Minn. Stat. §§ 216B.44-46, or by eminent domain proceedings under the jurisdiction of the courts, pursuant to § 216B.47. On remand, the district court authorized the city to condemn the area by quick take. On appeal, the court agreed with the district court's determination that appellants' challenge to the annexation was an impermissible collateral attack. After the city annexed the area, the area became urban; therefore, any subsequent condemnation of the utility property in the area did not interfere with the purpose of the Rural Electrification Act, 7 U.S.C.S. §§ 901-940. The quick-take method did not risk reliable service to the area because the utilities would work out a satisfactory transfer arrangement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which allowed the city to acquire certain electrical rights by quick-take.

 

1137 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Ascher v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety


C3-93-364


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


505 N.W.2d 362; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 889



August 31, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Granted October 28, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 754.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Dakota County; District Court File C89214632. Hon. Robert Carolan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Dakota County (Minnesota) that sustained the revocation of his driver's license pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 169.123, subd. 4 (1992), the implied consent statute.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that Fourth Amendment violations occurred when he was stopped at a sobriety checkpoint where television media were invited and present. He also argued that sobriety checkpoints violated Minn. Const. art. I, § 10. The court reversed the judgment that sustained the revocation of appellant's driver's license, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 169.123, subd. 4 (1992), the implied consent statute, after he failed several field sobriety tests and refused to take an Intoxilyzer test at the police station. The court concluded that law enforcement officers, by inviting the media to the checkpoint without taking any steps to protect the privacy of law-abiding citizens, grossly magnified the subjective intrusion experienced by those passing through the checkpoint. Accordingly, under the decisions of the United States Supreme Court, the court held that the sobriety checkpoint was invalid under the federal Constitution. Alternatively, the court held that, absent empirical evidence that sobriety checkpoints advanced the public interest, such wholesale, suspicionless seizures violated Minn. Const. art. I, § 10.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and the revocation of appellant's license was ordered rescinded.

 

1138 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Waughtal


C5-92-2400


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 876



August 25, 1993, Decided  
August 31, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed September 30, 1993. Petition for Review Denied October 28, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 744.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Beltrami County; District Court File Nos. K4-91-1094, K6-91-1095. Hon. John P. Smith, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged the decision of the District Court, Beltrami County (Minnesota), which held that they violated the respondent Northern Township's Water Supply System and Utility Ordinance, Northern Township, Minn., Ordinance §4(7(e)) (1988) and that the ordinance was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance made it unlawful to construct or maintain a private well for human consumption and required people to hook up to the township water system and to use that system for all of their water. The trial court found that the landowners violated the constitutional ordinance by refusing to hook up to the township water system in violation of §§ 4 (7(e)), 5(13) of the ordinance. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the landowners violated the ordinance by providing and paying for electricity to run the well's electric motor. The court held that because of the disjunctive nature of the ordinance, the township did not have to prove that the landowners' property had polluted ground water. The court held that the ordinance was not unconstitutional and it did not violate their right to privacy because the preparation and treatment of water was a common and accepted public function and the quality control measure did not ordinarily affront a person's sensibilities. The court held that even though the threat to the landowners' water supply was not imminent, the township made a sufficient showing of endangerment to justify its actions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's finding that the landowners violated the ordinance by refusing to hook up to the township water system. The court held that the ordinance was constitutional.

 

1139 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hochstein


C4-92-1982


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 807



August 10, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed September 9, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Wright County; District Court File No. K7911334. Hon. Gabriel Giancola, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court, Wright County (Minnesota) of committing a controlled substance crime in the fourth degree, Minn. Stat. § 152.024, subd. 2(2) (1992). On appeal, the main issue was whether a deputy's affidavit in support of an application for a warrant was invalid because it was not supported by facts establishing probable cause to believe contraband would be found in defendant's home.


OVERVIEW: In the affidavit, the deputy described incidents in which defendant was involved with small amounts of drugs or other drug-related items and large amounts of cash. Three incidents involved arrests for possession of a controlled substance. The deputy stated that, based on that information and his described extensive experience, he believed that defendant's home would contain controlled substances. A search warrant issued. On appeal, the court agreed that it was significant that there was no evidence that defendant did not have a large quantity of drugs associated with major sales activity, but that consideration dimmed in light of evidence of his possession of large amounts of cash, a weapon, drug paraphernalia, and incriminating notes. In the circumstances, there was an increased likelihood that police would find drugs and drug paraphernalia at his home. The affidavit was not false or misleading. By reciting only the arrests, the affidavit created no implications as to whether or not defendant was prosecuted or convicted. Nor was the information stale. By failing to raise a constitutional claim in the trial court, defendant failed to preserve the issue for appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1140 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


City of Minneapolis v. Fisher


C1-93-637, C3-93-655


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


504 N.W.2d 520; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 816



August 10, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed September 9, 1993. Petition for Review Denied September 30, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 694.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; District Court File 928094. Hon. Mary L. Davidson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, "adult" business landlords and owners, challenged the order of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which upheld the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. §§ 617.80-617.87 (1992) that permitted respondent city to enjoin appellants from operation of "adult" businesses at the location based upon proof that appellants had failed to halt prostitution on the premises.


OVERVIEW: Two prostitution convictions were based upon acts on the premises. The city sought to enjoin appellants from operating further adult businesses at the location under Minn. Stat. § 617.82 (1992). The district court found that the location was a public nuisance, closed the building for a year, and permanently enjoined the operation of an adult business there. Appellants sought review. Although appellants had possession of the building on alternate days, there was really only one entity. Because only one of the two offending owners were evicted, appellants' response was inadequate. The federal court's finding that §§ 617.80-617.87 was constitutional was binding. Appellants had notice and opportunity to be heard, which was all that due process required. Appellants were not prosecuted for crimes but for failure to prevent crimes on the premises. Appellants were free to associate with prostitutes but not to tolerate repeated criminal activity on their premises. Because the taking was temporary, was limited to "adult" businesses, and did no cause appellants to lose all economically beneficial use of the property, appellants were not entitled to compensation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the district court, which adjudicated the location a public nuisance, closed the location for one year, and enjoined appellants from operating adult businesses at the location.

State v. Harrington


C3-92-2556, C5-92-2557


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


504 N.W.2d 500; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 767



August 3, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed September 2, 1993. Petition for Review Denied September 30, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 689.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; District Court File Nos. T3-92-303343/T3-92-302593. Hon. Lawrence D. Cohen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which convicted defendants of violating a restraining order issued under the Minnesota harassment statute, Minn. Stat. § 609.748(5) (1990).


OVERVIEW: The director of an abortion clinic obtained a restraining order against defendants from target picketing the director's residence. Defendants did not appeal the restraining order. Defendants were subsequently seen carrying signs protesting abortions in front of the director's residence by both the director and the police. Defendants were convicted of violating the restraining order under the harassment statute, Minn. Stat. § 609.748 (1990). Defendants claimed on appeal that the restraining order was unconstitutional, that their convictions violated the ex post facto clause, Minn. Const. art. I, § 11, because the harassment statute was passed after the restraining order was issued, and that the evidence was insufficient to support their convictions. The court rejected defendants' claims. The court ruled that defendants could not indirectly attack the validity of the restraining order because they did not appeal the order within 30 days after it was issued, that the ex post facto laws did not apply because defendants were convicted for conduct that occurred after the harassment statute was adopted, and that defendants' convictions were supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for violating a restraining order in violation of the Minnesota harassment statute.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant psychiatric patient challenged a decision of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which ordered the patient committed as a psychopathic personality for an indeterminate period under Minn. Stat. § 526.09 (1992).


OVERVIEW: The patient argued that the trial court erred as a matter of law because there was no evidence that his behavior was uncontrollable. The court further held that, based on the patient's history of unsuccessful treatment in the past, the trial court's decision that commitment to the security hospital was the least restrictive alternative available was supported by the record and was not clearly erroneous. Finally, the court rejected the patient's claim that Minn. Stat. § 526.09 (1992) was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Waste Recovery Coop. v. County of Hennepin


C0-93-158


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


504 N.W.2d 220; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 756



July 27, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified July 27, 1993.
Reversed by, Remanded by Waste Recovery Coop. v. County of Hennepin, 517 N.W.2d 329, 1994 Minn. LEXIS 383 (Minn., 1994)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; District Court File No. 914259. Hon. Henry McCarr, Judge.
Waste Recovery Coop. v. County of Hennepin, 475 N.W.2d 892, 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 978 (Minn. Ct. App., 1991)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a county and others, sought review of a decision by the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which denied their motions for summary judgment. Appellants sought review of the order on the basis of qualified, discretionary function as well as due care in the execution of a statute immunity. The action was filed by respondents, a waste recovery cooperative and a waste hauler, who sought a restraining order and damages.


OVERVIEW: Minn. Stat. § 115A.553 (1990) required that the county ensure that materials separated for recycling were taken to markets for sale or to recycling processing centers. Two county investigators went to inspect the cooperative's facility, and they observed shredded telephone directories. Burning the directories did not fall within the definition of recycling. The court first found that appellants were immune from suit pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 under the doctrine of qualified immunity. The act of sending letter directives did not violate any Fifth and Fourteenth Amendment rights to just compensation for property taken by the government. Furthermore, there was no taking because appellants did not take possession of the directories or instigate a process to revoke any licenses so as to invoke the requirement of due process. However, the investigators acted belligerently once on the land and after a police officer arrived. Therefore, because a material fact dispute existed, the court could not conclude that the investigators were acting with due care in executing their duties. As such, immunity was properly denied under Minn. Stat. § 466.03, subd. 5 for common law trespass.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of appellants' motion for summary judgment on the issue of qualified and discretionary function immunity. The court affirmed the denial of appellants' motion for summary judgment on the issue of due care immunity. The court then remanded the action for a trial on the trespass issue. The court declined interlocutory review of the remaining issues.

Stat. § 526.09 (1992), was unconstitutional as a violation of due process.

Finally, the court concluded that the application of the psychopathic personality statute did not deny him due process or equal protection, nor was it unconstitutional. The court upheld defendant's commitment and denied the appeal.

C0-93-256


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA

NBZ Enterprises, Inc. v. Shakopee, 489 N.W.2d 531, 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 846 (Minn. Ct. App., 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the lumber company and the individual (lumber company), appealed the decision from the District Court, Scott County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment to respondent city in the lumber company's suit against the city for the denial of a conditional use permit requested by the lumber company. The denial allegedly resulted in a taking of the lumber company's property without just compensation.

Finding no justification to reverse the decision, the court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the granting of summary judgment to the city.

Grant v. Johnson


C2-93-243


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 652



June 29, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Washington County; District Court File No. C4-92-2240. Hon. R. Joseph Quinn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners sought review of the judgment from the District Court, Washington County (Minnesota) that found that a town ordinance prohibiting the keeping of wild animals without a permit was a valid exercise of police power and did not violate the law and that was granted in favor of respondent town.


OVERVIEW: The town filed an action against the owners to enforce an ordinance that prohibited the keeping of wild animals without a permit. On a motion for summary judgment, the trial court granted judgment in favor of the town and held that the ordinance was a valid exercise of police power and did not violate the law. On appeal, the owners argued that the ordinance exceeded the town's statutory authority to regulate the keeping of animals and that it arbitrarily discriminated against the private ownership of wild animals. The court held that the town's police power allowed it to regulate the keeping of wild animals and also to define nuisances and provide for their abatement. It was found that the tiger and leopard were inherently dangerous animals and presented a potential risk to the public. Therefore, the court concluded that the town was within its police authority in regulating the keeping of wild animals. Further, it was reasoned that the ordinance did not conflict with the federal Endangered Species Act, 16 U.S.C.S. § 1535(f) (1988) because it did not threaten endangered species but simply regulated their keeping within town limits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment granted in favor of the town and found the town's ordinance prohibiting the keeping of wild animals without a permit was a valid exercise of police power and did not violate the law.

In re Braun


C3-92-2167, C5-92-2168


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


502 N.W.2d 219; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 658



June 29, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; District Court File No. 92-15980. Hon. William R. Howard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contemnors sought review of the judgment of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which held both in criminal contempt for invoking their Fifth Amendment rights in a civil contempt proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Contemnors were both officers of a ministry, which participated in protest activities around a clinic that performed abortions. The trial court issued a temporary restraining order (TRO). Subsequently, the clinic brought a motion requesting that some protestors be held in civil contempt for violating the TRO. At the motion hearing, the clinic called one of the contemnors as a witness. His attorney immediately asserted his Fifth Amendment privilege, noting that he was charged with criminal contempt for violating the TRO. The trial court found him in direct criminal contempt for his refusal to answer, and sentenced to 10 days in jail and similarly with the other contemnor. The trial court later explained that its intent was to find the contemnors in contempt only for refusing to answer questions not related to any constructive criminal contempt charges. On review, the court reversed. The court held that the contemnors properly invoked their Fifth Amendment privilege in response to questions asked them in the civil contempt proceeding. Thus, the trial court erred in finding them in criminal contempt.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and held that the contemnors properly invoked their Fifth Amendment privilege in response to questions asked them in the civil contempt proceeding. The trial court erred in finding them in criminal contempt.

Elbers v. Growe


C1-92-2278


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


502 N.W.2d 810; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 684



June 29, 1993, Decided  
July 6, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed August 5, 1993. Petition for Review Denied September 30, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 698.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Ramsey County. District Court File No. CX-92-3618.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, prospective sheriff candidates and registered voters, challenged the determination of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), that the legislature might set qualifications for the office of sheriff under the Home Rule Amendment to the state constitution, Minn. Const. art. XII, § 3.


OVERVIEW: The prospective sheriff candidates complained that they could not meet the eligibility requirements in order to run for sheriff. They argued that their right to run for sheriff under Minn. Const. art. VII, § 6 had been abridged because sheriff candidates could not be required to meet eligibility requirements that were not specifically found in the state constitution. The Home Rule Amendment, Minn. Const. art. XII, § 3, authorized the legislature to set up eligibility requirements for county offices. The candidates cited the legislative history of in an attempt to show that legislature had no intention to alter eligibility requirements. The court held that the use of legislative history was of questionable value where the plain language of Minn. Const. art. XII, § 3 appeared to clearly authorize the legislature to change qualifications for office. The legislature's intent could also be discerned from actions immediately following voter approval of the amendment. In the first legislative session following ratification of the Amendment, the legislature required county attorneys to be learned in the law.Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

In re Access


C5-92-2526, C0-92-2529, C4-93-132, C6-93-133, C8-93-134


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


503 N.W.2d 480; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 701; 21 Media L. Rep. 1692



June 28, 1993, Decided  
July 6, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed August 5, 1993. Petition for Review Granted September 21, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 656.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court. Hennepin County. District Court File No. 92087464. Hon. James Johnston, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a writ of prohibition, petitioners, victims of the alleged rape and the news media, challenged an order of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota) that expunged and sealed the police department's investigative file arising out of the alleged rape involving a professional hockey player. Petitioners alleged that the trial court lacked the power to order expungement and that it was an unconstitutional prior restraint of free speech.


OVERVIEW: A hockey player alleged raped the victim in a hotel room. After a police investigation, the hockey player was not charged. The court found that the trial court had broad judicial discretion to expunge the records after all criminal proceedings were concluded and the subject of the investigation was not criminally charged. The expungement order was not a prior restraint because it did not attempt to suppress the news media's publication of material relating to the events of the alleged rape. The news media had no constitutional right of access to the information in the investigative file. The trial court properly ordered expungement of information in the file to protect the hockey player from harm that would be caused by the release of the information because the benefits to him of moving forward with a productive life outweighed the disadvantage to the public's need to know. The court declined to issue a writ of prohibition and affirmed the order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court declined to issue the writ and affirmed the trial court's order.

State v. Schmitz


C6-92-1563


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 680



June 24, 1993, Decided  
July 6, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied August 24, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 590.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court. Hennepin County. District Court File No. 91060918. Hon. Richard B. Solum, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which convicted him of three counts of aggravated robbery in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.245 (1990) and which sentenced him to consecutive sentences of 84 and 44 months and a concurrent sentence of 107 months.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his constitutional right to counsel was violated when police refused his request to consult an attorney before any identification procedure. The court declined to consider the issue and affirmed defendant's conviction because show-up identification procedures were valid when conducted without counsel. Thus, defendant could show no prejudice. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in refusing to suppress in-court identifications of him because the pre-trial identification procedures created a substantial likelihood of irreparable misidentification. The court rejected defendant's argument, finding that under the facts, there was no substantial likelihood of misidentification. Moreover, witnesses had more than adequate independent origin on which to base their in-court identification. Defendant further argued that the evidence did not justify either the convictions or the length and type of sentence. The court determined that defendant's sentence was within sentencing guidelines and did not unfairly exaggerate the criminality of his conduct. Thus, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Kimmons


C3-93-350


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


502 N.W.2d 391; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 640



June 22, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied August 16, 1993, Reported at 1993 Minn. LEXIS 573.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; District Court File No. 91017065. Hon. Robert G. Schiefelbein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota) that, following the jury trial, convicted him of simple robbery. Defendant asserted that the statute under which his sentence was enhanced, Minn. Stat. § 609.152, subd. 2, (1990), was unconstitutionally vague and unconstitutional as applied to him. He received a double upward durational depature from his presumptive sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who took a purse from an elderly woman in a parking lot, was convicted of robbery. The district court, applying § 609.152, subd. 2, imposed an enhanced sentence of 108 months. His presumptive sentence was 54 months. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding, first, that § 609.152, subd. 2 was not unconstitutionally vague. The "danger to public safety" criteria for sentence enhancement was included in other criminal statutes with which criminal courts had experience. The "high frequency rate of criminal activity," and "long involvement in criminal activity" factors did not improperly limit application to offenders with relatively minor or nondangerous offenses. The court noted that the statute was not unreasonable and arbitrary merely because a judge could have reached different results when applying it. The court also held that § 609.152, subd. 2 was not unconstitutionally applied to support the double upward durational sentence departure. The district court properly found that defendant was a danger to public safety, pursuant to § 609.152, subd. 2(2)(i), (ii), based upon his high frequency and long involvement in criminal activity, as well as the victim's advanced age.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1154 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Maras v. Brainerd


C8-92-1676, C1-92-1700


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


502 N.W.2d 69; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 639



June 15, 1993, Decided  
June 22, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed July 16, 1993. Petition for Review Denied August 16, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 569.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Crow Wing County; District Court File No. C6-91-1505. Hon. Robert Ryan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court, Crow Wing County (Minnesota), denied a motion for summary judgment filed by appellants, a city and a police officer, and respondent county, in respondent trustee's action for negligence, violation of a deceased's civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and negligence in training and supervision. Appellants challenged the denial.


OVERVIEW: The trustee's husband was shot by a police officer. The city and the county argued, inter alia, that the officer's actions were protected by governmental immunity. The court held that the trustee properly stated a § 1983 claim against the officer because the trustee alleged that the officer deprived the decedent of a federal right and that he acted under color of law. The court held that respondent county was entitled to summary judgment on the trustee's § 1983 claims because the trustee did not present evidence of an unconstitutional custom, practice, or policy. The summary judgment motion based on qualified immunity to the § 1983 claim was properly denied. The officer violated the decedent's clearly established rights and no reasonable officer would have acted similarly when the officer was not sufficiently threatened so as to justify the use of deadly force. The officer was not entitled to official immunity from the trustee's common law tort claims. The facts that the officer intentionally shot the decedent and that the officer was aware of city policy regarding the use of deadly force were sufficient to let the jury decide whether his actions constituted a malicious wrong.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the police officer's motion for summary judgment and the city and county's summary judgment motion on the issue of qualified immunity and reversed the denial of the county's motion for summary judgment on the § 1983 claims.

Lennes v. Reuben Johnson & Son, Inc.


C7-92-2320


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 557



June 1, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to Department of Labor & Industry



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator challenged a decision of the Occupational Safety and Health Review Board (OSHRB), which affirmed the dismissal by respondent Commissioner, Department of Labor and Industry, State of Minnesota, of his notice of contest.


OVERVIEW: The notice was dismissed because it was filed after the 20-day statutory deadline and relator presented no valid reason to vacate the order. Relator petitioned the OSHRB for reconsideration on the basis that unforeseen circumstances surrounding a hazardous chemical spill prevented a timely filing of a notice of contest and constituted good cause to set aside the Commissioner's dismissal. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court noted that relator had 15 days prior to the spill, and one day after clean-up efforts concluded, to file a timely notice of contest. Under those facts, the court found the OSHRB's affirmance of the dismissal to be justifiable and supported by substantial evidence as a matter of law. Further, the court held that the OSHRB relied on permissible and discernible factors in rendering its decision. According to the court, that was sufficient to survive judicial scrutiny.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1156 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Coulston


C3-92-1536


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 515



May 11, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied July 2, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 427.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Morrison, County; District Court File No. K591676. Hon. Timothy J. Baland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the District Court, Morrison County (Minnesota), which convicted him of kidnapping and two counts of criminal sexual conduct in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in admitting Spreigl evidence that defendant had been convicted of second degree criminal sexual conduct 13 years earlier. The court held that the evidence was clear and convincing that the defendant participated in the Spreigl incident, the evidence was relevant because defendant's conduct was virtually identical to the charged crimes, and the probative value of the Spreigl evidence outweighed its potential for unfair prejudice. While the victim was able to identify defendant as her attacker, it was within the trial court's discretion to find that the State needed the Spreigl evidence to meet its burden of proof. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in refusing to suppress results of a photo line-up, and in sentencing him pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 609.346 (1990). The court found that although not every person in the photo display matched the victim's description of her attacker, they bore a reasonable physical similarity to defendant. The display was not impermissibly suggestive. Lastly, the court correctly sentenced defendant to the mandatory minimum sentence because of his prior conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence.

COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant chemical dependency counselor sought review of an order from the District Court, Stevens County (Minnesota) denying the counselor postconviction relief after he was convicted on sexual misconduct charges.


OVERVIEW: This case arose after a female client of the counselor reported that the counselor had manually touched her breasts during several hugs after counseling sessions. The counselor was found guilty of six counts of fourth degree criminal sexual conduct. He did not appeal his conviction. However, the counselor filed a postconviction petition alleging that his trial counsel was ineffective. The petition alleged that counsel should have moved to dismiss the complaint on grounds that the statute was vague, should have pursued a juror misconduct issue further, and should have requested a particular jury instruction. The trial court denied the motion. On review, the court noted that, as to many of the charges, there was no record to review because the counselor failed to seek a postconviction hearing to make such a record. With reference to a charge that his counsel should have sought a hearing on the issue of juror misconduct, the court found that there was a mid-trial hearing at which the affected juror was questioned by the court. While the issue could have been handled differently, the counselor did not show that the outcome would have been different.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the counselor's motion for postconviction relief.

In re License Application of Rochester Ambulance Serv., Div. of Hiawatha Aviation, Inc.


C4-92-2131

500 N.W.2d 495; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 521



May 5, 1993, Decided

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator air ambulance service sought review of the denial by the state commissioner of health of the application by the ambulance service to provide specialized ground ambulance service. An administrative law judge recommended that the license be granted. The commissioner declined to follow the recommendation and concluded that the ambulance service failed to establish a need for service not currently being met by respondent competitor.


OVERVIEW: An air ambulance service applied for a license to provide specialized ground ambulance service. An administrative law judge recommended that the license be granted, but the state commissioner of health denied the license on the ground that the ambulance service had not established a need for service beyond that already provided by a competitor, a factor to be considered under Minn. Stat. § 144.802, subd. 3(g). The ambulance service sought judicial review of the commissioner's denial of its application. On review, the court found that the ambulance service did not establish, by the required preponderance of the evidence, that its service was needed. The court noted that discovery was available to the ambulance service to obtain this evidence, but the ambulance service made no attempt to discover the necessary information. The court also rejected the ambulance service's argument that state licensing procedures were preempted by the Federal Aviation Act, 49 U.S.C.S. § 1305(a)(1). The application was for a ground ambulance service, not an air ambulance service, and the federal statute did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the state commissioner.

 

1159 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Northwest Publications, Inc. v. Bloomington


CX-92-2358


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


499 N.W.2d 509; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 458; 21 Media L. Rep. 1474



May 4, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; District Court # 9214894. Hon. Bruce Hartigan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant press sought review of the judgment of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which determined that certain documents relating to emergency and security plans of a mall were entirely nonpublic data. The press had filed an action under the Minnesota Government Data Practices Act to obtain the sought after information from appellee city.


OVERVIEW: The city had possession of several emergency response plans relating to a mall and a protocol that governed the interaction between the police and the mall's security personnel. A reporter from the press requested access to the documents but the access was denied. The trial court found that even though not all of the document had nonpublic components, access was to be denied because all the documents were classified as unseverable bundles of nonpublic data. The court held that the trial court used the wrong standard to analyze the documents. The court found, inter alia, that (1) the Minnesota Government Data Practices Act established a presumption that government data were public and were accessible by the public for both inspection and copying, under Minn. Stat. § 13.01, subd. 3 (1992), with some exceptions; (2) one exception was a provision that classified "security information" as nonpublic; and (3) an entire document could be withheld only when the public and nonpublic information were so inextricably intertwined that segregating the material would impose a significant financial burden and leave the remaining parts of the document with little informational value.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Sanford v. State


C8-92-1788


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


499 N.W.2d 496; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 398



April 20, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Sanford v. State, 2000 Minn. App. LEXIS 1220 (Minn. Ct. App., Dec. 5, 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; District Court File No. 97351. Hon. Kevin S. Burke, Judge.
State v. Sanford, 450 N.W.2d 580, 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 30 (Minn. Ct. App., 1990)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant prisoner sought review from a decision of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which convicted him of three counts of murder in the second degree, one count of attempted manslaughter in the first degree, and denied his motion for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant along with the victims was selling drugs from defendant's mother's home. After the neighbors' complained, the mother asked them to move out. Defendant argued that while attempting to have them move out, they returned to his mother's home and he had to kill the three men in self-defense. The trial court disagreed and convicted defendant of their murders. On appeal, the court affirmed that conviction. Defendant argued that even if his belief that he was in danger of imminent bodily harm was unreasonable, he should nevertheless have been acquitted if his belief was honestly held. He thus argued a mistake of fact, rather than a mistake of law. The court held that the law upon which defendant relied was premised both upon the complexity of the tax laws and Congress' intent to make specific intent an element of tax crimes, therefore it was not controlling. The court also rejected defendant's claim that the bifurcation of insanity trials was constitutionally suspect because that procedure prohibited him from explaining in a single trial why he believed that he was in danger. The court again held that the law defendant relied upon was inapplicable and that bifurcation was sound.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying defendant's motion for post-conviction relief.

In re Applications of Q Petroleum


C6-92-2177, C0-92-2188


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


498 N.W.2d 772; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 402



April 20, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed May 21, 1993. Petition for Review Denied July 15, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 500.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari to Minnesota Petroleum Tank Release Compensation Board, Hon. George A. Beck, Admin. Law Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator petroleum companies sought review of the decisions of respondent, the Minnesota Petroleum Tank Release Compensation Board, which denied reimbursement of costs to clean up petroleum leaks.


OVERVIEW: After the Board denied the companies' requests for reimbursement for cleanup costs that were paid by insurance, the companies sought administrative review. The administrative law judge affirmed the Board's denial, and the companies sought judicial review. On appeal, the court found that most of the original applications were rejected on the basis that the companies had insurance coverage that would provide reimbursement for some of the costs. The court also found that after delays by the Board, an amendment to the Minnesota Petroleum Release Cleanup Act became effective, specifically disallowing reimbursement for insured costs. The court ruled that the Board did not err in denying the companies' requests for reimbursement of costs that were incurred in cleaning up the petroleum leaks. The court held that the Board did not act arbitrarily and capriciously in tabling some applications. The court held that the companies had no right to reimbursement until the Board had finally acted on their applications. The companies had no vested right that was constitutionally protected because the Board had not finally acted on their applications when the amendment went into effect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Board's denial of the companies' requests for reimbursement of costs that were incurred in cleaning up petroleum leaks.

Hamborg v. County of Hennepin


C4-92-2338


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


498 N.W.2d 486; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 368



April 7, 1993, Decided  
April 13, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed May 10, 1993. Petition for Review Denied June 22, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 410.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court. Hennepin County. District Court File No. MC926594. Hon. Lucy Wieland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the manager of a property, challenged a judgment of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), that granted respondent county's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the manager's appeal from a forfeiture of the property for nonpayment of real estate taxes. The district court ruled that the manager failed to comply with the deposit requirement of Minn. Stat. § 284.10 (1990) and that the deposit requirement was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Real estate taxes were unpaid for three years while the manager was employed by the property's previous owner, and they remained unpaid for three more years after a corporation in which the manager was the sole shareholder bought the property. When the manager appealed from the tax forfeiture, he deposited part, but not all, of the accumulated unpaid taxes. On appeal from the dismissal, he alleged that the deposit requirement was unconstitutional and that he should have been personally served with notice of the expiration of the redemption period. The court affirmed the district court judgment. The manager was required to deposit the full amount of delinquent taxes, and as the property's manager he had access to documents from which that amount could have been determined. The deposit requirement of § 284.10 did not unconstitutionally deprive the manager of access to the courts because he knew of the tax liability when he bought the property and the statutory process offered pre-forfeiture protections. Minn. Stat. § 281.13 (1990) was inapplicable, and Minn. Stat. § 281.23 (1990) did not require personal service on the manager as an occupant of the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court judgment.

OVERVIEW: Appellant forced an eight-year-old girl to remove her clothes and to participate in oral sex. Appellant broke into a woman's mobile home and forced the woman to remove her clothes. 1165 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Ultraflex Enters. Appeal


C8-92-1970


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


497 N.W.2d 641; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 286



March 16, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari to Minnesota Department of Administration



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator company sought review of the decision of respondent Commissioner of Administration (Minnesota), which upheld the revocation of the company's participation in Minnesota's small business procurement program.


OVERVIEW: The company's founder and president suffered from a chronic mental disability. Because of the founder's disability, the company was certified as a targeted group business for purposes of participation in the state's small business procurement program under Minn. Stat. 16B.19, subds. 2a, 2b (1990). After the company's certification, the legislature amended the act and redefined targeted groups, eliminating persons suffering from mental disabilities. As a result of the amendment, the company was no longer qualified for the program. The court affirmed the Commissioner's decision upholding the revocation. The court held that § 16B.19 subd. 2b did not deny the founder equal protection under the federal and state constitutions. The mentally disabled were not a suspect class, therefore the state only had to demonstrate a rational basis for differentiating between physical and mental disabilities. The state asserted that there was no evidence before the legislature of past discrimination against businesses that were owned and operated by the mentally disabled. The legislature was not required to address all evils at once when it adopted the remedial legislation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commissioner's decision.

St. Paul v. Spencer


C0-92-1381, C2-92-1382, C4-92-1383, C6-92-1384, CX-92-1632


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


497 N.W.2d 305; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 217



March 3, 1993, Decided  
March 9, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied April 20, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 291.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; District Court File Nos. C4-91-2759, C9-91-10243, C6-91-10426, C8-91-10427, C2-91-1299. Hon. Charles Flinn, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City of St. Paul (Minnesota) sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which dismissed the City's actions to enjoin respondent property owners from permitting a public nuisance on their properties.


OVERVIEW: Three prostitution convictions were obtained for transactions occurring in each of the property owners' establishments. After the third convictions the City sent the owners notices of the convictions under Minn. Stat. § 617.81, subd. 3 (1990), and then filed an action to abate the nuisance under Minn. Stat. § 617.83 (1990) by closure of the establishments. In affirming the dismissal of the actions for failure of notice, the court held that § 617.81, subd. 3, required that a separate notice of conviction had to be sent after each conviction to the building owner and other interested parties. The court noted that § 617.81, subd. 3, required "notice of a conviction," and that the word "a" denoted a single conviction. The court also concluded that it would be unfair and counter to the purpose of the public nuisance statute if the City was not required to advise the property owner of the first and second convictions to enable the owner to take measures to abate the nuisance before it was faced with closure of the establishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed the City's nuisance abatement actions.

Krueth v. Independent School Dist. No. 38


C6-92-1398


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


496 N.W.2d 829; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 232; 61 U.S.L.W. 2546; 61 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 361



February 24, 1993, Decided  
March 2, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed March 30, 1993. Petition for Review Denied April 20, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 285.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari to Independent School District No. 38 Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator teachers challenged by writ of certiorari the decisions of respondent Independent School District No. 38 (Minnesota), which placed the teachers on unrequested leaves of absence while retaining Native American teachers pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 126.501 (1990).


OVERVIEW: Despite their seniority rights under a collective bargaining agreement and Minn. Stat. § 125.12 (1990), the teachers were placed on unrequested leaves of absence. The court found that the District's decision was proper in all but one aspect because (1) providing preferential treatment to Native American teachers with less seniority was authorized by Minn. Stat. § 126.501 (1990), (2) this political preference survived equal protection rational scrutiny analysis, and (3) § 126.501 took precedence over general teacher tenure laws. However, the court reversed the District's decision with regard to grant-funded positions because these positions were subject to the seniority rights of Minn. Stat. § 125.12 (1990), and ordered that one of the teachers be placed in such a position with back pay. The court noted that all of the other teachers had already been recalled from leave by the District.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the District's decision with regard to grant-funded positions, and ordered that one of the teachers be reinstated to one of these positions with back pay. However, the court affirmed the District's decision against the teachers in all other respects.
