In re Welfare of E.Y.W.


C2-92-1415


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


496 N.W.2d 847; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 237



February 24, 1993, Decided  
March 2, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied April 20, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 282.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court. Hennepin County. Hon. Philip D. Bush, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, appealed an order of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which granted the State's petition to refer defendant to adult court for prosecution of first and second degree murder charges against him.


OVERVIEW: A delinquency petition, alleged that defendant, a juvenile, and two others robbed and killed a man. Defendant confessed to the murder.The State filed a petition to refer defendant to adult court for prosecution. The juvenile court found that defendant was competent and that the State established a prima facie case for reference. Defendant requested, and received, a continuance to prepare a rebuttal of the State's prima facie case. When the court reconvened, defendant rested without offering any evidence in rebuttal. The juvenile court referred defendant for prosecution as an adult for first and second degree murder. Defendant appealed. The court held that the evidence reasonably supported the juvenile court's finding that the State established a prima facie case for adult reference and that defendant failed to rebut the prima facie case. The evidence supported the juvenile court's determination that the State demonstrated by clear and convincing evidence that defendant was not suitable for treatment in the juvenile court system. The juvenile court's determination, based on the testimony of two mental health experts, that defendant was competent was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which granted the State's petition to refer defendant to adult court for prosecution.

Lessard v. Milwaukee Ins. Co.


C0-92-1526


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


496 N.W.2d 852; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 238



February 23, 1993, Decided  
March 2, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed April 2, 1993. Petition for Review Granted April 29, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 310.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court. Washington County. D. C. File No. C5-91-1894. Hon. Thomas G. Armstrong, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insured sought review of the decision of the District Court for Washington County (Minnesota), which denied him pre-award interest on an arbitration award with appellee insurer.


OVERVIEW: The insured and his wife were injured in a car collision when another vehicle crossed the median and struck their car. The insured settled with the other driver's insurer and collected a settlement amount. The insured provided notice to the insurer. The insured sought underinsured motorist coverage benefits from the insurer because of the limited coverage of the driver. An arbitrator was appointed and the arbitrator awarded the insured damages and pre-award interest. The trial court confirmed the award but refused to award interest. The court held that the amendments to Minn. Stat. § 549.09(1)(b) could apply retroactively in cases involving insurance and the trial court erred in holding that the statute did not have any retroactive effect. The court concluded that prejudgment interest was inappropriate because the interest in addition to the arbitration award exceeded the maximum liability limit of the insured's policy. The court noted that the insured did not contract for prejudgment interest exceeding the liability of his policy and to require the insurer to pay the interest would have been rewriting the parties' contract.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that denied the insured pre-award interest on an arbitration award.

In re Beals


C9-92-2335


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 254



February 23, 1993, Decided  
March 2, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Granted April 12, 1993.
Review denied by, Stay granted by In re Beals, 1993 Minn. LEXIS 264 (Minn., Apr. 12, 1993)
Related proceeding at Beals v. Gomez, 1996 Minn. App. LEXIS 760 (Minn. Ct. App., July 2, 1996)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court. St. Louis County. D. C. File No. P992600126. Hon. Robert V. Campbell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the District Court, St. Louis County (Minnesota), which committed him under Minn. Stat. § 526.09 (1990) as a psychopathic personality.


OVERVIEW: Several witnesses testified to sexual assaults committed by appellant against them. The assaults dated back 25 years, and had resulted in criminal convictions. Appellant also had been convicted of murder of a two-year old child. In affirming appellant's commitment, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing appellant's victims to testify at the commitment hearing even though the fact of the convictions appeared from his plea records. The court also held that the succinct testimony of his victims concerning the assaults was not unfairly prejudicial under Minn. R. Evid. 403 and Minn. Stat. § 526.09 (1990). The court rejected appellant's contention that the commitment order violated his plea agreements. The court noted that the plea agreements contained no promise that he would not be committed and held that dual commitments to the Commissioner of Corrections and the Commissioner of Human Services could and did withstand even a constitutional challenge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's commitment.

 

1171 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Condon


C6-92-610


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


497 N.W.2d 272; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 177



February 17, 1993, Decided  
February 23, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court. Ramsey County. District Court File No. 9101983. Hon. Charles A. Flinn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the District Court of Ramsey County (Minnesota) convicting him of criminal vehicular operation and sentencing him to 60 months imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The victim was exiting her car while her children were inside. Defendant struck the victim while driving his vehicle. After defendant failed two sobriety tests, he was arrested and taken to a hospital. He refused a blood test and asked for an attorney. The officer was informed that the victim died, so he directed workers to take a blood sample. Defendant was convicted. On appeal, he alleged that: (1) his blood test results should have been suppressed; (2) Minn. Stat. § 609.21, subd. 1(3) was unconstitutional; (3) his previous DUI conviction should not have been used; and (4) the trial court erred in departing upward. In affirming the decision, the court found that the trial court properly departed upward based upon defendant's attempt to flee and because the fatality occurred in front of children. The validity of defendant's previous conviction was properly proven. The blood test results were properly admitted because defendant had no right to refuse testing. The officer had probable cause to believe that defendant was intoxicated and had committed criminal vehicular operation. Section 609.21 was constitutional in that it required an act that was both criminal and negligent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

1172 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State by Humphrey v. Jim Lupient Oldsmobile Co.


C4-92-1190


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 181



February 17, 1993, Decided  
February 23, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Granted April 20, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Minn. LEXIS 280.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court. Hennepin County. District Court File CD2091. Hon. William S. Posten.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which awarded respondent property owner an interest rate that was greater than that set by Minn. Stat. § 549.09, subd. 1(c), for the value of land that the State acquired through eminent domain proceedings. A panel of three court-appointed commissioners determined the amount of damages that the State owed to the property owner for the acquisition.


OVERVIEW: The district court heard oral arguments in chambers from attorneys for each side and received a transcript of the deposition of witnesses. The court held that the summary proceeding did not violate the due process rights of the State because summary proceedings were authorized by statute. The court found that the landowner was entitled to that return on the money equivalent of the property which would have been available if the landowner had been timely paid and had made reasonable and prudent investments. The return that would satisfy the requirements of just compensation could be more, less, or equal to the return allowed by statute. The court found that since it could not say that the district court clearly erred, the order awarding interest was not erroneous. Further, the trial court's determination of the interest issue on the authorities, affidavits, documents, deposition, and oral arguments of counsel submitted upon the motion for interest, without the taking of oral testimony, was not an abuse of discretion and did not deny due process of law. The evidence supported the district court's award.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1173 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Rogers v. Ponti-Peterson Post #1720 Veterans of Foreign Wars, Inc.


C0-92-1462


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


495 N.W.2d 897; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 178



February 16, 1993, Decided  
February 23, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court. Itasca County. District Court File No. C6-90-198. Hon. John A. Spellacy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant club appealed from the judgment of the District Court of Itasca County (Minnesota), which had directed a verdict against it and denied its motion for a new trial in a personal injury action in which the jury had awarded plaintiff victims over $ 2 million in damages. The victims argued that the trial court erred in calculating collateral source deductions.


OVERVIEW: The victims were injured, one of them very seriously, in an accident caused by defendant driver. The driver had entered the club alone and had drunk alone in the club earlier in the day. He was not a member of the club. The club's license, under Minn. Stat. §§ 340A.404, subd. 1(4), permitted it to sell liquor only to members and bona fide guests. The court held that the trial court properly directed a verdict against the club on the issue of an illegal sale because the driver was neither a member nor a bona fide guest of the club. The court held that the term "bona fide guest" in the statute was not vague. Although not defined in the statute, it had a generally recognized meaning. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by allowing improper argument to the jury because the club failed to object. The trial court properly applied the collateral source rule to deduct from the award amounts paid by the victims' health insurer because the health insurer had no right of subrogation against the club under the dram shop act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

Indep. Sch. Dist. No. 622 v. Keene Corp.


C7-91-234


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


495 N.W.2d 244; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 114; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P13,565; 22 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 1030



February 2, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Conditional Review Filed March 5, 1993.
Review granted by Independent Sch. Dist. No. 622 v. Keene Corp., 1993 Minn. LEXIS 278 (Minn., Apr. 20, 1993)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Independent Sch. Dist. No. 622 v. Keene Corp., 511 N.W.2d 728, 1994 Minn. LEXIS 5 (Minn., 1994)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Washington County; Hon. John E. Cass, Judge. District Court File C5841701



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant manufacturer challenged an order of the District Court, Washington County (Minnesota), which entered judgment in favor of appellee school district and denied its motions for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or for a new trial in appellee's action alleging that appellant's fireproofing product contained asbestos, it was defective, its safety was misrepresented, and that appellant had breached various warranties.


OVERVIEW: School district brought an action against appellant after it discovered that manufacturer's fireproofing product contained asbestos and had to be removed. The district began removal and sued manufacturer for the costs. A jury found in favor of district on all counts and awarded compensatory as well as punitive damages. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the tort remedies of negligence and strict liability were available to the district as it was not a merchant of fireproofing material and because its cause of action was not a claim for economic loss. The 15-year statute of limitations applied to the district's action where the legislature did not manifest a clear intent to apply a 10-year statute of limitations retroactively. Manufacturer failed to produce any evidence to establish a genuine issue of fact as to product identification and, a requested comparative fault instruction was properly withheld absent any evidence supporting submission of the comparative fault issue to the jury. While punitive damages were properly awarded, pursuant to the factors set forth in Minn. Stat. § 549.20(3) the court reduced the award by one-half.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order in favor of the school district but modified the punitive damage award.

 

1175 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


C8-92-1404


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


495 N.W.2d 454; 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 133



February 2, 1993, Decided  
February 9, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed March 8, 1993. Petition for Review Granted March 30, 1993, Reported at 1993 Minn. LEXIS 226.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court. Renville County. District Court File No. T792136. Hon. James E. Zeug, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant pled not guilty to a charge of misdemeanor speeding and demanded a jury trial, over his objection the District Court, Renville County (Minnesota) allowed the State to reduce the charge to a petty misdemeanor and defendant was found guilty in a trial by the court. On appeal, one issue was whether the State had to obtain defendant's consent before reducing the charge from a misdemeanor to a petty misdemeanor.


OVERVIEW: In granting the State's motion, the trial court found that Minn. Stat. § 609.131, subd. 1 (1990) governed conflicting provisions in Minn. R. Crim. P. 23.04. Thus, defendant's consent to the reduction in charges was not required. On appeal, the court noted that its review was governed by principles of comity in that due respect for the coequal branches of government required the court to exercise great restraint before striking down a statute as unconstitutional, particularly when it involved a determination of what was a legislative and what was a judicial function. The court held that Rule 23.04 directly conflicted with Minn. Stat. § 609.131, subd. 1 (1990) as to whether defendant's consent was required. But, the court reaffirmed an earlier decision and held that § 609.131, subd. 1 governed. That, in the interim between its earlier decision and the case at bar, the advisory committee for the rules of criminal procedure had added certain language to its comment to Minn. R. Crim. P. 23.04 made no difference. Such comments were not promulgated or approved by the Supreme Court of Minnesota and the court's earlier decision had specifically addressed the issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Machau v. State


C7-92-843


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 145



February 2, 1993, Decided  
February 9, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court. Nicollet County. District Court File No. K389713. Hon. Warren E. Litynski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Nicollet County (Minnesota), that denied his motion for post-conviction relief from a sentence imposed for a conviction for possession of a controlled substance in the third degree. He had been sentenced to an executed term of 48 months in prison and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that Minn. Stat. § 152.023, subd. 2(2) (1990), which provided for a sentence for the possession of 10 grams of cocaine identical to that for the sale of 10 grams of cocaine, was a violation of due process because it imposed a presumption that a possessor of 10 grams of cocaine had an intent to sell the cocaine. The court held that appellant's due-process rights were not violated by the enforcement of § 152.023, subd. 2(2) (1990) and the Minn. Sentencing Guidelines. Also the court ruled that because the post-conviction petition only involved an issue of law an evidentiary hearing was not necessary. Lastly, the court ruled that appellant was not prejudiced by the trial court's failure to give the State an opportunity to respond to his post-conviction petition because to have relief on appeal a party had to show that he had been prejudiced by a tribunal's action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of the judgment from the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent union in the employer's declaratory judgment action on the ground that the Minnesota Striker Replacement Act, Minn. Stat. § 179.12(9) (1991), was constitutional under the Supremacy Clause of the United States Constitution.

State v. Campbell


C6-92-641


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 55



January 5, 1993, Decided  
January 12, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court. St. Louis County. District Court File K191675733. Hon. Charles T. Barnes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court, St. Louis County (Minnesota), which convicted him of manufacture of marijuana, possession of marijuana with intent to deliver, possession of marijuana, and failure to possess a marijuana tax stamp.


OVERVIEW: The police discovered marijuana plants growing in a wooded area near defendant's house. Following his convictions of several drug related offenses, defendant argued on appeal that the warrantless search of his property was unconstitutional, as the area where the marijuana was found growing was within the curtilage of his residence. The court held that the area was beyond the curtilage of defendant's residence, as it was outside of the cleared and mowed area used as a lawn and no steps had been taken to protect the area from observation. Defendant also asserted that his Fourth Amendment privacy rights were violated when the police officer left the sidewalk and walked across his lawn. Defendant contended that the evidence seized pursuant to the search should be suppressed as fruit of the poisonous tree. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the evidence seized pursuant to the search was admissible. The court reasoned that there was no flagrant violation of defendant's rights and that the marijuana growing in an open field could have been discovered by other means.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Turner


CX-92-769


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 67



January 5, 1993, Decided  
January 12, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed February 16, 1993. Petition for Review Denied February 25, 1993, Reported at 1993 Minn. LEXIS 142.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court. Hennepin County. DC File No. 91059855. Hon. Beryl A. Nord, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction of aggravated robbery, Minn. Stat. § 609.245 (1990), from the District Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued he was denied due process because the aggravated robbery statute was vague and ambiguous. The court stated it was clear that a person who committed a robbery while armed with a dangerous weapon or inflicted bodily harm was guilty of aggravated robbery under § 609.245. Simple robbery under Minn. Stat. § 609.24 required only the use of force or threatening the imminent use of force to overcome a person's resistance. It does not require bodily harm. Both statutes had specified standards of conduct. Defendant failed to show the aggravated robbery statute was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt and thereby was not denied due process. Defendant's argument for lenity, that a court should apply the least harsh statute when different statutes describe the same behavior, failed because the two relevant statutes described different behavior. Defendant also claimed the trial court erred when it refused to give jury instructions on the definition of force and on lesser included crimes. Because this case was heard by the trial court and not by a jury, the court did not reach that issue.


OUTCOME: The trial court judgment was affirmed.

 

1180 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


New Creative Enterprises, Inc. v. Dick Hume & Assoc., Inc.


C2-92-1303


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


494 N.W.2d 508; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 1307



December 31, 1992, Decided  
January 12, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed February 9, 1993. Petition for Review Denied March 16, 1993, Reported at 1993 Minn. LEXIS 192.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court. Hennepin County. District Court #9118491. Hon. Charles A. Porter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant manufacturer sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which granted respondent sales representative's motion for summary judgment in a declaratory judgment action concerning the applicability of the arbitration provisions of Minn. Stat. § 325E.37 (1990) to the parties' oral sales representative agreement.


OVERVIEW: The sales representative filed a demand for arbitration after the manufacturer terminated the oral sales agreement and refused to participate in arbitration. The manufacturer then filed a declaratory judgment action seeking a declaration that § 325E.37 did not apply to the agreement or that the statute was unconstitutional. The arbitrator held that the agreement fell within the scope of § 325E.37 because it was a renewed agreement. The trial court granted the sales representative's motion for summary judgment and ordered the parties to proceed with arbitration. The manufacturer appealed and asserted that § 325E.37 was unconstitutional and inapplicable. The court determined that the provisions of § 325E.37 that precluded judicial review of the compulsory arbitration decision was unconstitutional based on the due process guarantee of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court concluded that due process required a minimal level of judicial review of compulsory binding arbitration decisions. The court severed the unconstitutional provision of the statute and remanded the case for arbitration because the remaining provisions of § 325E.37 were applicable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court judgment as it granted the sales representative's motion for summary judgment but severed the unconstitutional provisions of § 325E.37. The court remanded the case for arbitration on the merits.

 

1181 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


New Creative Enterprises, Inc. v. Dick Hume & Assoc., Inc.


C1-92-1423


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 1310



December 31, 1992, Decided  
January 12, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Filed February 11, 1993. Petition for Review Denied March 16, 1993, Reported at 1993 Minn. LEXIS 191.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court. Hennepin County. District Court #9121636. Hon. Charles A. Porter, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant manufacturer challenged an order of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which dismissed its claims against respondents, a sales representative, its principal, its attorney, and a commercial arbitration association and its employees, for prima facie tort, abuse of process, and conspiracy to inflict economic harm and to deny civil rights.


OVERVIEW: The sales representative filed an arbitration demand with the association after the manufacturer terminated their agreement. Thereafter, the manufacturer filed its action against respondent, and the trial court granted respondents' motions to dismiss. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that because Minnesota did not recognize a prima facie tort action in the context of a proceeding for the wrongful initiation of arbitration proceedings, the claim was properly dismissed. Additionally, the manufacturer's abuse of process claim was properly dismissed because arbitration was not demanded to prevent the manufacturer from having its day in court; rather, at the time the sales representative filed its arbitration demand, Minn. Stat. § 325E.37, subd. 5 (1990) required the sales representative to submit its claim to arbitration. The court found that dismissal of the conspiracy claim was also proper because it was dependent on the prima facie tort and abuse of process claims, both of which were properly dismissed. Finally, the court held that the association and its employees were immune from civil liability claim, and thus, the claims against them were properly dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1182 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Carlson


C2-92-1429


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


494 N.W.2d 516; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 1308



December 30, 1992, Decided  
January 12, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Granted March 10, 1993, Reported at 1993 Minn. LEXIS 181.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court. Ramsey County. District Court File, #C2-92-9611. Hon. Joseph E. Salland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a state senator and other interested individuals, sought review of the judgment of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), denying their motion for summary judgment and entering judgment in favor of respondents, the Governor of Minnesota and the Commissioner of the Board. Appellants' action challenged the constitutionality of the Governor's veto of 1991 Minn. Laws 2895 ("section 5").


OVERVIEW: The vetoed legislation redirected the division and distribution of proceeds of the tax on taconite and iron sulfides. On appeal from the judgment in favor of respondents, appellants argued that section 5 was not imposed upon an item of appropriation and was therefore an improper exercise of the veto power. The court agreed and reversed the judgment. It held that section 5 was not an item of appropriation, defined as a separate and identifiable sum of money appropriated from the general fund dedicated to a specific purpose. The court reasoned that since section 5 merely authorized the transfer of the tax increase funds from the economic and environmental funds to the higher education services, it involved no new appropriation of a separate and identifiable sum. It also reasoned that the Governor's veto power was limited to items of appropriation, not of a part or parts of an item, and that the bill involved an individual allocation that was only part of an item. The court concluded that because the funds in question were to be paid over to the residuary, which did not involve the general fund, the expenditure did not "appropriate" money otherwise available for state purposes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

State v. Christie


C5-92-968


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


494 N.W.2d 492; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 1281



December 23, 1992, Decided  
January 5, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Christie, 1993 Minn. LEXIS 155 (Minn., Feb. 25, 1993)
Affirmed by State v. Christie, 506 N.W.2d 293, 1993 Minn. LEXIS 659 (Minn., 1993)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court. Otter Tail County. District Court File # K990515. Hon. Thomas M. Stringer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who pleaded guilty to one count of first-degree burglary, was sentenced as a patterned sex offender under Minn. Stat. § 609.1352 (Supp. 1989), and was given the 240-month statutory maximum for first degree burglary, appealed from a judgment of the District Court, Otter Tail County (Minnesota), which found the patterned sex offender statute to be constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his sentence, and the court affirmed the trial court's finding that defendant fit the statutory definition of a patterned sex offender. However, because defendant raised the issue of the constitutionality of the patterned sex offender's statute for the first time on appeal, the case was remanded to the trial court for an initial determination of the statute's constitutionality. On remand, the trial court concluded the patterned sex offender statute was constitutional. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court noted that the patterned sex offender statute did not take defendant's sentence outside the constraints of the sentencing guidelines, but rather was authorized by the sentencing guidelines, and concluded that the reasonableness standard in the patterned sex offender statute met due process requirements. The court also concluded that the statute was clear and definite enough to warn a person as to what conduct was punishable and how severe the punishment might be. Persons of ordinary intelligence could read the statute and determine what would subject them to enhanced punishment. Therefore, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

In re Hendrickson


C6-92-1790


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 1255



December 22, 1992, Decided  
December 29, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court. Carver County. District Court File No. P392364. Hon. Philip T. Kanning, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a patient in a state security hospital, sought review of the order of the District Court, Carver County (Minnesota), committing him to the hospital for indeterminate period as a psychopathic personality.


OVERVIEW: Over a period of about 17 years, the patient was arrested for or convicted of several sexual offenses involving young boys. Prior to the completion of a prison sentence, a petition was filed to commit him as a psychopathic personality. The trial court based its order on testimony from several mental health professionals, each of whom considered the patient to be at high risk to reoffend against young boys if released; the hospital's 60-day report agreed, and the trial court committed the patient for an indeterminate period. The court affirmed the judgment. It held that the findings and the record provided clear and convincing evidence that the patient met the standards of Minn. Stat. § 526.09 for commitment; that the fact that the trial court did not use the precise words used by the Minnesota Supreme Court to define the term "psychopathic personality" was not determinative; and that the trial court did not clearly err in its order. The court further held that previous authority holding that the psychopathic personality statute was constitutional was not distinguishable and was controlling as to the patient's claim that the statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

OVERVIEW: Defendant committed two sexual assaults and sentenced to imprisonment. Upon release from prison, defendant sexually assaulted a woman who had "passed out" after drinking too much alcohol. The court stated the hospital was developing a new series of treatment programs for sex offenders. The commitment was affirmed.

1186 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Lidberg v. Steffen


C1-92-1129


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


492 N.W.2d 560; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 1148



November 13, 1992, Decided  
November 24, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Bruce J. Lidberg's motion to dismiss the petition for further Review Denied and Hennepin County petition for Review Granted, January 15, 1993, Reported at 1993 Minn. LEXIS 30.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Judicial Appeal Panel Court. Hon. Gerald W. Kaline, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant committee sought review of the judgment of the Judicial Appeal Panel Court (Minnesota), which, following respondent Minnesota Commissioner of Human Services denial of the committee's petition for full discharge, denied full discharge, granted provisional discharge, and rejected the committee's constitutional challenge.


OVERVIEW: The committee suffered from chronic paranoid schizophrenia. He was initially committed as a person mentally ill and dangerous to the public. The committee's commitment status was subsequently amended to a mentally ill person following a determination that he was no longer dangerous to the public. The Commissioner of Human Services denied the committee's petition for full discharge. The court below denied full discharge, granted provisional discharge, and rejected the committee's constitutional challenge. The lower court's judgment was reversed on appeal. The lower court's judgment was reversed on appeal. The court determined that the committee could not continue to be held as if her were dangerous to the public because it had already been determined that he was no longer dangerous to the public. Because the committee could no longer be held as a person mentally ill and dangerous to the public, the court found that he was entitled to constitutionally adequate procedures to establish the grounds for his continued commitment. Before the committee's commitment could be continued, the committee was entitled to a hearing and determination under Minn. Stat. § 253B.13, subd. 1.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.

State v. Morrow


C7-92-1295


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


492 N.W.2d 539; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 1104



November 10, 1992, Decided  
November 17, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court. Carver County. District Court File Nos. 917826F, 917831F, 917846F. Hon. Philip T. Kanning, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment of the district court (Minnesota), which revoked his probation and executed a 34-month prison sentence as a result of his guilty plea for criminal sexual conduct when he was unable to successfully complete an in-patient sex offender treatment program, through no fault of his own.


OVERVIEW: The inmate pled guilty to three counts of criminal sexual conduct in the second degree. At the sentencing hearing, the inmate requested a dispositional departure from the presumed sentence and argued that placement in residential treatment, would make him less likely to reoffend. The lower court granted the inmate's motion for dispositional departure and placed him on probation for 15 years. Several conditions were imposed on the inmate's probation, including that he enter and complete an in-patient sex offender treatment program. The county refused to fund the treatment and the inmate, because he was indigent; the lower court revoked his probation and executed a 34-month prison sentence. On review, the inmate asserted that the lower court abused its discretion and violated the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of the United States and Minnesota Constitutions when it revoked his probation and executed the sentence. The court affirmed. The court ruled that based on Minn. Stat. § 609.135 (1990) the lower court was within its discretion in revoking the inmate's probation and the revocation was not arbitrary or fundamentally unfair.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of the inmate's probation and the imposition of the 34-month sentence.

 

1188 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hickman


C5-92-1019


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


491 N.W.2d 673; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 1052



October 21, 1992, Decided  
October 27, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied December 15, 1992, Reported at 1992 Minn. LEXIS 338.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Sherburne County; Hon. Gabriel D. Giancola, Judge. District Court File No. T692819



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the District Court, Sherburne County (Minnesota), which granted the motion of defendant to suppress evidence that he was driving with a revoked license. The State also challenged the district court's order denying its motion to reconsider.


OVERVIEW: A police officer pulled defendant over when he noticed an expired vehicle registration sticker on his vehicle license plate. Defendant had not been speeding, driving erratically, or operating a vehicle with equipment violations. While still in his patrol car after the stop, the officer saw a temporary permit in the window of defendant's car. The officer confirmed the validity of the permit as he walked to defendant's car. Nonetheless, the officer approached the car and asked to see defendant's driver's license. Defendant then admitted that he did not have a valid driver's license. The district court suppressed the evidence obtained by the officer after he had established that the vehicle was properly registered. The court agreed. The court found that detaining defendant to check his driver's license constituted an unlawful intrusion because the officer's suspicions about the vehicle's registration had been dispelled before he approached the driver. After seeing the valid temporary permit, the officer no longer had articulable and reasonable suspicion that the vehicle was unregistered, that the driver was unlicensed, or that any criminal activity was afoot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

In re Blodgett


C9-92-844


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


490 N.W.2d 638; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 960



September 8, 1992, Decided  
September 15, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by In re Blodgett, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 625 (Minn., Nov. 3, 1992)
Affirmed by In re Blodgett, 510 N.W.2d 910, 1994 Minn. LEXIS 4 (Minn., 1994)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Washington County; Hon. David E. Doyscher, Judge. District Court File No. P0915206



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a convicted felon, sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Washington County (Minnesota) that committed the felon for an indeterminate period as a psychopathic personality, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 526.09. The court allowed the Minnesota Civil Liberties Union to file a brief as an amicus curiae and allowed the attorney general to intervene.


OVERVIEW: While serving a sentence for three separate felony charges involving criminal sexual conduct and while enrolled in a pre-release program, the felon committed a sexual assault, for which he was convicted. A petition was filed to commit the felon a psychopathic personality. The trial court found no reasonable alternative commitment other than commitment as a psychopathic personality to the Minnesota Security Hospital. The court affirmed, holding that there was clear and convincing evidence that the felon exhibited emotional instability, impulsive behavior, lack of good judgment, and failure to appreciate the consequences of his acts, so as to render him irresponsible for his personal conduct with respect to sexual matters and dangerous to other persons. The trial court was not clearly erroneous in determining that the felon met the statutory requisites for commitment. The challenges to the constitutionality of the statute failed, as the statute was not void for vagueness, did not deny equal protection, and was not violative of procedural due process. The prohibition against double jeopardy did not preclude the felon's commitment as a psychopathic personality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Ragland


C5-91-2306


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 955



August 28, 1992, Decided  
September 8, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court. Ramsey County. Hon. Kathleen R. Gearin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which convicted him of two counts of third degree criminal sexual conduct under Minn. Stat. §§ 609.344(1)(b) & 609.344(1)(c) (1990).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault under Minn. Stat. § 609.344(1)(b) & (c) (1990), which prohibited penetration of a person at least 13 and less than 16 years of age by a person more than 24 months older, or penetration with force or coercion. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court ruled that statements made by the complainant several months after the alleged offense were admissible hearsay under Minn. R. Evid. 801(d)(1)(B). The court ruled that an argument challenging the constitutionality of the rule was not preserved for review and any error was harmless. The court stated that pursuant to common law, convictions for sexual assault were routinely upheld with no corroboration of the complainant's testimony. The court further held that a medical report indicating that the complainant had herpes was not admissible to controvert a contention that she went to the hospital due to a fear she was pregnant. The court further held that the trial court properly admitted defendant's statement regarding consensual sex with other women at a house which he and the complainant visited.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of two counts of third degree criminal sexual conduct.

Minneapolis Teachers Retirement Fund Ass'n v. State


CX-92-271


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


490 N.W.2d 124; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 874; 15 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2289



August 12, 1992, Decided  
August 18, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Minneapolis Teachers' Ret. Fund Ass'n v. State, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 601 (Minn., Oct. 28, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Michael J. Davis, Judge. District Court File 91200



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a teachers' pension plan and others, contested the summary judgment that the District Court for Hennepin County (Minnesota) entered in favor of respondent State of Minnesota in appellants' declaratory judgment action regarding the constitutionality of 1975 Minn. Laws ch. 306, § 30 in its effects on the teachers' pension plan under 1909 Minn. Laws ch. 343.


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued that 1975 Minn. Laws ch. 306, § 30 effected an unconstitutional impairment of contracts under the federal and Minnesota Constitutions. The trial court denied appellants' motion for summary judgment and granted that of the State. Appellants sought review but secured no relief. The court's survey of the history of 1909 Minn. Laws ch. 343 and its several amendments led the court to conclude that the legislature did not create a contractual right to employer contributions to the retirement fund in an amount that would maintain the actuarial soundness of the fund. Similarly, 1909 Minn. Laws ch. 343 did not promise that a fund, if created, would receive funds raised through taxation by state or local taxing authorities; it only stated that a plan could include a provision that a portion of said fund was to be raised by taxation upon the property of the said city. These considerations showed that, under the doctrine of promissory estoppel, appellants did not have contractual rights to pensions under 1909 Minn. Laws ch. 343. Therefore, no unconstitutional impairment of contractual rights occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1192 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Loyal Parks Hoseth


C6-91-2170


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 824



August 5, 1992, Decided  
August 11, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by, Review dismissed by State v. Hoseth, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 429 (Minn., Oct. 20, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. David M. Duffy, Judge. District Court 91007878



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction entered in the District Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota) for failing to provide his animals with necessary water or shelter in violation of Minn. Stat. § 343.21(2) (1990). He contended that the statute was unconstitutionally vague because it lacked sufficient definiteness to allow him to conform his conduct to the statute, and that the evidence did not support the conviction.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of one count of failing to provide his animals with necessary water or shelter in violation of Minn. Stat. § 343.21(2). The court affirmed and found that defendant was not entitled to an order striking the State's brief on the ground that its reference to a prior district court case involving defendant was an improper use of evidence outside the record. Although defendant was a party in the previous district court action that involved the same issue presented in the appealed case, that did not preclude the court from considering the decision rendered in that earlier district court action. The court rejected his challenge to the constitutionality of § 343.21 and found that it was not overbroad or vague. The statute's language prohibiting behavior depriving an animal of "necessary" food, water, or shelter adequately described the proscribed conduct and did not require the death of an animal in order to find that defendant had violated the statute. In addition, the evidence was sufficient to allow the jury to find him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of violating the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for failing to provide his animals with necessary water or shelter.

State v. Poole


C3-91-1963


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


489 N.W.2d 537; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 837



August 5, 1992, Decided  
August 11, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Poole, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 885 (Minn., Sept. 30, 1992)
Affirmed by State v. Poole, 499 N.W.2d 31, 1993 Minn. LEXIS 271 (Minn., 1993)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Traverse County; Hon. Bruce Christopherson, Judge. District Court File No.: K7-91-09
State v. Poole, 472 N.W.2d 195, 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 711 (Minn. Ct. App., 1991)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant doctor appeal from District Court, Traverse County (Minnesota), which convicted him of third and fourth degree criminal sexual conduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Minn. Stat. §§ 609.344, subd. 1(k) and 609.345, subd. 1(k) were vague, ambiguous and were misused by the state. Because the statutes were subject to reasonable construction and established adequate guidelines to govern law enforcement, the court concluded Minn. Stat. §§ 609.344, subd. 1(k) and 609.345, subd. 1(k) satisfied due process requirements and were not void for vagueness under either the federal or the state constitution. The court disagreed with defendant's argument that the search warrants for records at his clinic were insufficiently specific as to the items to be seized, and thus amounted to a prohibited "general" warrant. The search warrants were sufficiently specific and were supported by probable cause. The trial court's change of venue over his objection did not violate his constitutional right to be tried by an impartial jury of the county or district wherein the crime was committed. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting evidence that he engaged in sexual misconduct with his cousin. However, the court found that an 18 year sentence unfairly exaggerated the criminality of defendant's conduct and modified the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, but modified the sentence.

State v. Grandboise


C1-91-2092


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 887



August 5, 1992, Decided  
August 18, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Grandboise, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 426 (Minn., Oct. 20, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Becker County; Hon. William E. Walker, Judge. District Court File #K5-90-001022



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Becker County District Court (Minnesota) that convicted him of second-degree assault in violation of Minn. Stat. §§ 609.222 and 609.11 (1990), arguing that the gun found in his car was improperly introduced into evidence because it was the product of an illegal search.


OVERVIEW: After receiving notice of a shooting, police presented to the scene and pursued defendant. Defendant drove to his home, parked his car near the house, went inside, and refused to answer the door. The police obtained a warrant to search the "premises" for the gun, but the words "motor vehicle" were crossed off on the warrant. Despite this, police searched the vehicle and recovered the gun. Defendant ultimately surrendered and was charged with second-degree assault. At trial, the district court admitted the firearm into evidence over defendant's objection. Following his conviction, defendant appealed, challenging the admission of the gun. In affirming, the court rejected defendant's unconstitutional seizure argument. The search warrant authorized a search of the premises, and this permitted a search of any vehicle owned or controlled by the owner of, and found on, the premises. Although the words "motor vehicle" were crossed off on the warrant, this did not make the search unconstitutional but merely indicated that the general object of the search was the premises, not the automobile.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

1195 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jennings


C7-92-485


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


487 N.W.2d 536; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 767



July 22, 1992, Decided  
July 28, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Jennings, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 585 (Minn., Sept. 29, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Delila F. Pierce, Judge. District Court File 91082709



DISPOSITION: Certified question not answered and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his indictment from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) of first degree murder, a crime that violated Minn. Stat. § 609.185(5) (1990).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the statute under which he was indicted was unconstitutionally vague, and made a motion to dismiss the first degree murder portion of the indictment. The trial court denied the motion but certified a question to the appellate court as important or doubtful pursuant to Minn. R. Crim. P. 28.03. In remanding the case for trial, the court declined discretionary review of the case. The certified question was not ripe for decision because the court was to assume facts that were not in existence to establish an element of the crime. Further, the issue could be preserved for appeal if defendant was convicted. Also, the certified question dealt imprecisely with facts that the State was to prove at trial, and the case did not present a fully developed substantive issue ripe for decision. Because the court was to evaluate defendant's vagueness argument as applied to the facts of the case, it could only review the vagueness of the statute by assuming facts not in existence. Therefore, it was inappropriate to base its analysis of unconstitutionality upon such assumption.


OUTCOME: The court declined discretionary review of the case and remanded the case for trial.

In re Rickmyer


C4-92-489


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 761



July 22, 1992, Decided  
July 28, 1992, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; James F. Finley, Court Commissioner. DC File No. 91-1857



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which committed him as mentally ill and as a psychopathic personality.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that the evidence was not clear and convincing as to his mental illness. In affirming the judgment, the court found that there was nothing clearly erroneous in accepting one psychologist's testimony that appellant was mentally ill. Further, evidence supported the conclusion that appellant met the statutory definition of a pedophile and testimony was presented showing that appellant was a pedophile who was extremely dangerous to children. Also, there was clear and convincing evidence upon which to commit appellant as a psychopathic personality. Finally, nothing supported appellant's argument that his due process rights were violated because he was not advised that the interview could be the basis for the commitment and that he did not need to speak to the interviewer. Appellant decided to continue the interview with the psychologist. Even if he had not completed the interview, the petition would have been based upon the records, rather than upon any refusal to complete the interview.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that committed appellant as mentally ill and as a psychopathic personality.

Graham v. Special School Dist. No. 1


C1-92-661


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 755



July 21, 1992, Decided  
July 28, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Graham v. Special Sch. Dist. No. 1, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 617 (Minn., Sept. 29, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Charles A. Porter, Judge. District Court File No. 886406
Graham v. Special School Dist. No. 1, 472 N.W.2d 114, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 172 (Minn., 1991)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged a decision of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment after remand from the state supreme court to respondent employer in a wrongful discharge action the employee brought under the Whistleblower Statute, Minn. Stat. § 181.932, subd. 1(a) (1988), and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 (1988). The action was initially dismissed based on a previous wrongful discharge action.


OVERVIEW: An employee worked for her employer as a social worker for 10 years until she was discharged. The employee worked in a preschool education program for children with special needs. During her tenure, the employee expressed concerns to various staff members and officials, both orally and through internal memoranda, about perceived violations of state procedures for the assessment of children. She was subsequently fired. A letter the employee received from the employer specifically noted her "general litigiousness" as a factor in her termination. On review, the court found that the employee made out a prima facie case by establishing that she had engaged in statutorily protected activity, that the employer took adverse employment action against her when it discharged her, and a presumptive causal connection. By reviewing the facts in the light most favorable to the employee, the court concluded that the employee raised circumstantial evidence from which an inference of pretext could be drawn and, thus, the trial court's grant of summary judgment was erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court that dismissed an employee's action against an employer under the Whistleblower Statute and remanded the matter to the trial court.

1199 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Pike v. Gunyou


C2-92-734


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


488 N.W.2d 298; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 630



June 19, 1992, Decided  
June 20, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Pike v. Gunyou, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 628 (Minn., Aug. 31, 1992)
Vacated by Pike v. Gunyou, 491 N.W.2d 288, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 302 (Minn., 1992)



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractors brought an action against respondents, the Commissioner of Finance of the State of Minnesota and an intervening airline, seeking an order declaring 1991 Minn. Laws. 350 unconstitutional and enjoining its enforcement. The trial court (Minnesota) dismissed the contractors' action with prejudice due to their failure to file a surety bond pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 562.02 (1990). The contractors appealed.


OVERVIEW: 1991 Minn. Laws 350 authorized bonds to finance construction of aircraft maintenance and repair facilities and to provide financial assistance to airline corporations. An interagency task force determined that a certain portion of the bonds to be sold under contracts with the airline could be used to prepay the airline's pre-existing debts and expenses. The trial court ordered the contractors to post a surety bond under Minn. Stat. § 562.02 (1990). The court held that § 562.02 applied to the action, as it was brought to challenge an action taken by a public body regarding the sale of bonds, and that the delay caused by the action could have resulted in loss or damage to the public. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in requiring the contractors to post the bond, as their suit, on the eve of the bond issue, resulted in a de facto injunction against the sale of bonds to the airline, thus posing a risk of damages to the public and the governmental entities involved. The dismissal of the action did not bar later suits challenging 1991 Minn. Laws. 350, as the contractors' complaint raised valid constitutional issues, and those issues were not adjudicated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the contractors' complaint with prejudice, but the court held that the dismissal of the action did not bar a similar suit brought by another taxpayer.

 

1200 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Casanova Beverage Co. v. Commissioner of Public Safety


C3-91-2319, C3-91-2336


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


486 N.W.2d 448; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 600



June 3, 1992, Decided  
June 9, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Casanova Bev. Co. v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 503 (Minn., Aug. 4, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court. Hennepin County. Hon. Michael J. Davis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Minnesota Department of Public Safety and a liquor manufacturer, challenged a decision from the District Court. Hennepin County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent liquor wholesaler in its suit challenging enforcement of the Department's interpretation of Minn. Stat. § 340A.307, subd. 1 (1990) as requiring that liquor manufacturers sell liquor to wholesalers only if it is for use in the state.


OVERVIEW: The liquor wholesaler had licenses and places of business in both Minnesota and Wisconsin. It bought a substantial amount of the manufacturer's products for delivery in Minnesota and then shipped the liquor to its Wisconsin warehouse for resale there. The Department issued a memorandum stating that Minnesota law required that liquor wholesalers sell only with the State of Minnesota. The wholesale brought a declaratory judgment action against the Department and the manufacturer intervened. The trial court interpreted Minnesota's liquor control laws as requiring the sale of liquor to a wholesaler even though that wholesaler intended to ship the liquor to another state for sale in that state. On appeal by the Department and by the manufacturer, the court reversed. The court interpreted § 340A.307, subd. 1 to mean that manufacturers had to provide liquor to wholesalers only if the liquor was for use in Minnesota. The court noted that the intent of the legislature was to promote competition and lower prices in Minnesota. It did not intend to deregulate liquor intended for other states and could not constitutionally have done so under the Commerce Clause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the liquor wholesaler.
